Collection of Ancient and Modern Books on Medicine, Volume 238

Phlegm Gate

Huangdi's Plain Questions

On the Great Discussion of Yin and Yang Correspondences

The Taiyin is at the spring; the dampness overcomes, leading to heart pain from fluid accumulation among the people. (Note: The Taiyin at the spring corresponds to the years of Chen and Xu, where fluid accumulation causes heart pain, indicating that cold damp rises). The victory of the Taiyin uniquely overcomes, causing internal dampness to accumulate and fluid to appear above. The recovery of the Taiyin comes when the dampness transforms and the fluid arises from within.
(Note: This occurs when the fire and earth combine before the midpoint of the year. The unique victor refers to the cold damp aspect, which recovers after the midpoint of the year, leading to internal dampness that presses on the lower abdomen. The fluid emerging from within and swelling above indicates the water pathogen rises from below, between, and above. Recovery refers to overcoming the defeated qi, extreme accumulation, and subsequent rebound.)

On the Great Discussion of the Five Constants

The Taiyang governs the heavens; dampness transforms materials, causing internal fluid to accumulate.
(Note: The Taiyang governs the heavens, thus the Taiyin damp earth resides at the spring, resulting in the onset of damp-related illnesses.)[1p]
The Great Treatise on the Six Elements

When the Taiyin arrives, there will be accumulating drinking or obstruction.
[Note: This is common in spring sickness.]
When the Taiyin arrives, it will yield abundant grain.
[Note: This is common in summer sickness.]
Shaoyin governs the affairs of heaven, and when the four seasonal energies cause the people's sickness, there will be drinking and outbreaks.
[Note: This is due to the influence of damp and hot energies, hence the outbreaks.]
When the earth accumulates, the people's sickness manifests as drinking and downpour.
[Note: This is all due to the influence of damp earth energies.]

The Great Treatise on the Changing Energies

In a year when the earth is excessive, rain and dampness spread, kidney water becomes affected by evil influences, leading to severe drinking outbreaks, reduced appetite, and fullness in the abdomen.
[Note: Earth refers to its element in the ground, and dampness refers to its element in the sky; thus, in those years, the earth's energy becomes excessive, and rain and dampness spread. Drinking refers to the spleen's inability to transport and transform, resulting in phlegm and fluid accumulation. Fullness and reduced appetite arise because of earth deficiency, which cannot assist in transformation. When such excesses occur, they reverse the original deficiency and cause self-harm, leading to these sicknesses emerging at the time the earth's energy attains its proper position in the eighteen days of the seasonal months.]

The Ling Shu Classic

Discussion on Disease Diagnosis

When the skin becomes coarse like the scales of a dried fish, it indicates internal fluid accumulation.
[Note: The description of dried fish scales indicates cold sensations on the skin. Cold represents the energy of water; thus, the water evil accumulates internally, manifesting cold appearances externally.]
The Essentials of the Golden Chamber [by Zhang Ji of the Han dynasty][2p]
Phlegm and Fluid

A question was asked: There are four types of fluids, what are they? The teacher replied: There are phlegm fluid, suspended fluid, abundant fluid, and obstructive fluid.

The question was: How do the four types differ? The teacher said: The person who was once robust but is now thin has water moving in the intestines, making a dripping sound; this is called phlegm fluid. If after drinking the water lingers under the ribs, causing coughing and pain, this is called suspended fluid. If the water flows to the limbs, resulting in heaviness and pain, especially when sweating is not present, this is called abundant fluid. If coughing and difficulty lying down occur, with the person appearing swollen, this is called obstructive fluid.

Water in the heart causes hardness beneath the heart, leading to shortness of breath and aversion to drinking. Water in the lungs leads to expectoration of phlegm and a desire to drink. Water in the spleen causes slight breathlessness and heaviness in the body. Water in the liver causes fullness under the ribs, with sneezing and pain. Water in the kidneys leads to palpitations. Retained fluid under the heart makes the person's back cold, feeling like the size of a palm.

For those with retained fluid, there is pain under the ribs extending to the lower back, and coughing usually alleviates it. If there is retained fluid in the chest, the person experiences shortness of breath and thirst, with pain in the limbs at the joints. A sinking pulse indicates retained fluid.

With phlegm above the diaphragm, fullness leads to wheezing and coughing; there may be alternating chills and fever, lower back pain, and spontaneous tears; such a person will shake and tremble, surely having underlying fluid issues.

Patients who drink too much water inevitably suffer from intense wheezing. Generally, if food intake is low and water intake is high, water may accumulate beneath the heart; in severe cases, this leads to palpitations, and in milder cases, to shortness of breath. A double-string pulse signifies coldness, while all severe cases after a major purge show deficiency. A pulse that is slightly stringy indicates fluid presence. Lung fluid does not present as a stringy pulse but rather indicates wheezing and shortness of breath.[3p]
If the person has edema and is unable to lie down, with shortness of breath but a normal pulse, then for phlegm and fluid retention, warm herbs should be used to harmonize it.

If there is phlegm and fluid in the chest and diaphragm, causing fullness in the chest and sides, along with dizziness, the Ling Gui Zhu Gan decoction is indicated. For shortness of breath with slight fluid retention, it should be resolved through urination; the same decoction is indicated, as well as Shen Qi Wan.

If the patient's pulse is faint and they wish to have a bowel movement, but the result is dissatisfying, and despite having a movement, there remains fullness below the heart, this is due to retained fluid wanting to be eliminated; the Gan Sui Ban Xia decoction is indicated.

If the pulse is floating, thin, and slippery, injury from fluid is present. A pulse that is tight and rapid indicates cold fluids, which are difficult to treat in both winter and summer.

If the pulse is deep and wiry, it suggests internal pain from suspended fluids. In the case of suspended fluids, the Shi Zao decoction is indicated.

For excessive fluids, inducing sweat is necessary; the Da Qing Long decoction and the Xiao Qing Long decoction are both indicated.

In cases of fluid accumulation in the diaphragm where the individual experiences breathlessness, fullness, and hardness below the heart, with a dark complexion and a tight, deep pulse, if lingering for several days and treatment with vomiting or purging proves ineffective, the Zhu Fang Ji decoction is indicated. If they are deficient, they will recover; if they are excess, they may relapse after three days. For cases that do not improve, it is advisable to use the Zhu Fang Ji decoction without gypsum and add Fu Ling and Mang Xiao decoction.

If there are fluids beneath the heart causing the person distress and dizziness, the Ze Xie decoction is indicated. For phlegm and fullness in the chest, the Hou Po Da Huang decoction is indicated.[4p]
If there is a retained fluid causing discomfort, use the Tang of large dates and artemisia to treat it. If someone who typically experiences vomiting is not thirsty, it is due to retained fluid in the lower abdomen, treated with Xiao Ban Xia Decoction. If there is abdominal fullness and dryness of the mouth and tongue, this indicates water qi in the intestines, treated with Ji Jiao Li Huang Wan. For sudden vomiting, distention below the heart, water in the diaphragm, and dizziness, use Ban Xia Jia Fu Ling Decoction. If a thin person experiences palpitations below the navel, produces saliva and foam, and feels dizzy, this indicates water, treated with Wu Ling San. For a patient with a cough and wiry pulse, indicating water, use Shi Zao Tang.

For those with retained phlegm and chest pain, if they do not die suddenly, expect them to recover within a hundred days to a year; treat with Shi Zao Tang. Chronic cough lasting several years, with a weak pulse can be treated, but with a strong pulse, the prognosis is poor. If the pulse is weak, they will suffer from fever and discomfort, as they likely have retained fluid in the chest, thus should be treated for excess fluid.

If a patient experiences vomiting before feeling thirsty, it indicates a desire for relief; if they feel thirsty before vomiting, it means water has pooled below the heart, indicating retained fluid. A person who usually feels thirsty but now does not is likely due to retained fluid below the heart, indicating fluid retention.

Walnuts should not be consumed in excess, as they can provoke phlegm and fluid.[5p]
Treatise on Phlegm

Whenever there is water in the heart, the person experiences palpitations, shortness of breath, and fear; they may feel dizzy and delusional. If the condition arises from cold, it is seen as deficiency; if from heat, it is seen as excess. Thus, if water is in the heart, the individual’s chest feels tight, palpitates with short breaths, dislikes water and does not wish to drink. If water is in the lungs, they may spit saliva and desire to drink. If water is in the spleen, the person feels fatigued and heavy all over. If water is in the liver, they may experience fullness under the ribs, sneezing, and pain. If water is in the kidneys, they will experience palpitations in the chest.

A patient who suddenly drinks a lot of water will certainly suffer from acute asthma. Generally, if food intake is low but water consumption is high, water stagnates in the heart, leading to severe palpitations or mildly to shortness of breath. A double-string pulse indicates cold; all these conditions lead to a preference for deficiency after significant bowel movement. A side-string pulse indicates the presence of fluid. If there is lung fluid without a string-like pulse, there is a tendency for shortness of breath. If there is fluid retention, one might also experience asthma and an inability to sleep, along with shortness of breath and a smooth pulse.

In cases of retained fluid, there are no outward signs, and without heat, the pulse is weak; the individual will feel fullness and cannot eat. A deep and slippery pulse indicates the illness of retained fluid. In those with retained fluid, pain may radiate from the sides to the lower back, leading to severe coughing; individuals may cough and feel unable to lie down, experiencing neck pain while coughing, resembling a condition seen in children with convulsions. If fluid is accumulated in the chest, the person will feel short of breath and thirsty, with pain in the limbs and joints; a deep pulse indicates the presence of retained fluid.[6p]
If there is retained fluid in the chest, the person has a cold sensation on their back, and it feels as large as a hand. If the patient has a raised shoulder and difficulty breathing, these indicate fluid overflow in the chest. In chronic cases, there may be fullness like a pot and severe swelling resembling a horse’s knife, caused by phlegm-fluid. The illness above the diaphragm presents as fullness, wheezing, coughing, and expectoration, with alternating chills and fevers, back pain and aversion to cold, and weeping of the eyes. The person may shake or tremble, indicating hidden fluid. If one arm is unresponsive, sometimes shifting to the other arm, and the pulse is deep and thin, this is not wind but rather fluid present in the upper burner. A weak pulse indicates slight exhaustion because the qi of the nutritive and defensive systems is not circulating properly. In winter, recovery occurs naturally.

For treating suspended fluid, use Shizao Decoction. If there is sweating and coughing with difficulty in breathing, this is fluid accumulation. In cases of excessive fluid, one should induce sweating, and Xiao Qinglong Decoction is the primary remedy. Fan Wang used Da Qinglong Decoction.[7p]
Living Person's Book
(Song Dynasty, Zhu Gong)

Phlegm and Fluid

When phlegm is present in the Middle Palace (the central area of the abdomen), it causes dislike of cold, fever, aversion to wind, spontaneous sweating, and a feeling of fullness in the chest and diaphragm, resembling a case of typhoid fever. However, there is no headache and no stiffness in the neck, which is a distinguishing feature. I often observe damp phlegm stagnating in the neck and back, sometimes feeling numb or stiff, with a pulse that is floating and slippery but not tight.

Jisheng Prescription
(Song Dynasty, Yan Yonghe)

Phlegm and Fluid[8p]
There are six types of drinking: suspended drinking, overflowing drinking, support drinking, phlegm drinking, retained drinking, and lurking drinking; Nesting Shi has detailed these well. Pang Anchang often said: "If there is no phlegm above in the human body, then there is no water flowing upstream in the world." Truly wise words! From this perspective, the pathway of human qi is valued for being smooth; when it flows smoothly, bodily fluids circulate, and there will be no concern about phlegm or drink. If regulation and restraint are not appropriate, the qi pathway becomes obstructed, resulting in water and drink stagnating in the chest and forming phlegm. The symptoms of this illness are not one but many: it can lead to wheezing, coughing, vomiting, diarrhea, dizziness, palpitations, cold and hot pains, swelling, fullness, and constipation, all caused by phlegm or drink. If you examine the pulse, a firm or slippery pulse indicates drink.

As for the method of treating drink, it may involve purging or sweating, warming or benefiting; these are fixed methods. The foolish might think that the difference between warming and benefiting could be harmless, but if purging or sweating is misapplied, it leads to substantial illness. It is better to prioritize smoothing the qi first and then guiding it afterward. When the qi is smooth, bodily fluids circulate, phlegm and drink are moved downward, and are expelled through urination. Those with illnesses that make them want to spit phlegm and find relief from taking Eight Ingredients Pills can also have some intention behind their actions. Wang Shuhe said: "The kidneys are cold and produce much saliva." The kidneys are the organs of water; they can receive and manage water, and when kidney qi is warm and harmonious, fluids descend. When kidney qi is deficient and cold, pathogenic water rises instead. To counter this, mountain cornelian, yam, and similar herbs are used for nourishment, while aconite and cinnamon are used for warmth, and poria and water plantain for diuresis; this reasoning is indeed correct. During an acute illness, one should examine the situation carefully and in detail.[9p]
Accumulated Fluid

Accumulated fluid refers to the retention of liquid without dispersing. When water becomes dry, it dissipates; when it becomes moist, it does not dissipate, leading to accumulated fluid. Damp soil is responsible for this condition. Wine is hot in nature and induces coldness; when cold and hot coexist in the chest, they do not disperse and lead to dampness, resulting in phlegm. In severe cases, it is advisable to expel it. After expulsion, taking wuling and ganlu, which are effective in overcoming dampness and eliminating phlegm, is recommended.[10p]

The Confucian Way of Filial Piety

By Zhang Congzheng (Yuan Dynasty)

Drinking should be moderated based on the temperature of the water and the severity of the discussion.

Retention of fluids is simply the accumulation of water. In Wang's "Pulse Canon," it is classified into four types: phlegm retention, suspended fluids, obstructive fluids, and overflow of fluids. "Qianjin Fang" further categorizes it into five, all defined by the presentation of the illness. I shall not elaborate on these classifications now. The reasons for fluid retention can be traced to five causes: 1) arising from frustration and anger, 2) from exhaustion, 3) from deep contemplation, 4) from excessive drinking, and 5) from harm caused by heat during cold seasons. Although there are many manifestations of fluid retention, they all fall into these categories.

When frustration and anger are suppressed, the liver energy affects the spleen, leading to failure in digestion and hence fluid retention. The liver governs thought; prolonged indecision restricts the flow of bodily energies, resulting in fluid retention. For those who work hard and travel long distances, exhaustion leads them to drink, and with weakened spleen and stomach, they may feel lethargic and unable to disperse energy through the pulses, which also results in fluid retention.

Excessive drinking fills the stomach and intestines; further consumption exceeds the bladder's ability to excrete, leading to prolonged fluid retention. Additionally, in extreme heat, bodily fluids may dry up, leading one to crave cold water. In an attempt to quench thirst, excessive consumption leads to stagnation, resulting in fluid retention as well.[11p]
If a person suffers from the sickness of drinking, can they possibly go beyond these five issues? Water is a yin substance; when it accumulates, it produces humidity, and when liquor stagnates, it generates dryness. Over time, this leads to phlegm. If phlegm forms on the left side, it corresponds to excess fat; on the right side, it corresponds to the nature of breath. If it enters the lungs, it causes frequent coughing; if it enters the large intestine, it leads to diarrhea; if it enters the kidneys, it results in retention of water. This condition presents as a bag filled with fluid, unable to move upwards or downwards. Placed under sunlight, it becomes a form of edema—these ailments stem from rebellious qi.

Thus, when humidity is present above, the eyes turn yellow and the face swells; when it is below, the thighs and knees become swollen and numb; when it is in the middle, there is fullness and stagnation in the chest. If phlegm remains in the yang and does not disperse, over time, it transforms into qi; if it remains in the yin and does not disperse, it eventually solidifies. In contemporary treatments, it is commonly stated that drinking leads to cold accumulation, thus using damp-heat remedies to counteract the dryness. However, coldness from drink in the middle is treated with heat remedies from above, which are rebuffed by coldness, and moisture has not been resolved, resulting instead in increased heart fire.

When the fire does not descend, water flows back down, causing desiccation in the upper burner and chill in the lower. The "Nei Jing" states that if the cycles of entering and exiting are dysfunctional, the spirit and transformations become extinguished. If rising and descending are obstructed, qi becomes isolated and perilous. Can this not be taken seriously? Moreover, retaining fluid does not have any restorative treatments, and when qi is blocked and obstructed, supplementation only worsens the condition. Do we not understand the “Nei Jing,” which states that retained fluids should be attacked? Why do later generations not diligently study the ancients? Additionally, using herbs like white atractylodes, ginseng, and poria for those who drink only increases obstructions. How much more so when employing fire needling and moxibustion for bloating can the situation be understood?[12p]
In the past, practitioners used more than thirty ingredients for the Wuyin Pill, which included minerals like alum stone, as well as herbs such as pungent herbs and Aconite. Although these were purgative, they all shared the properties of dryness and heat. While there were also cooling herbs included, they lacked the strength to balance out the formula. Therefore, in modern times, Liu Hejian based his formulation of the Sanhua Shenyouwan on Zhang Zhongjing's Shizao Decoction, and added Da Huang (rhubarb) and Qian Niu (cowherb), yielding a remedy that could expel illness after taking thirty to fifty pills, allowing the harmful energy to flow out.

There was once a patient suffering from this condition for decades who came to me for diagnosis. The pulse on the left hand was weak and small across three positions, while the right hand exhibited a slippery and large pulse in the same three positions. The weak and small pulse indicated cold, while the slippery and large pulse signified dryness. I prescribed watermelon seed powder to expel their cold phlegm, resulting in several liters of sweat. Next, I employed a method to guide out the dry and dirty matter from their intestines and stomach, which also amounted to several liters. The patient improved by half; then I used a mild remedy to continue releasing the remaining buildup and a fire-reducing medicine to open the appetite. Within a month, the patient was completely healed.

Coptis and Phellodendron can clear away the excess heat and dampness above, while Astragalus and Poria can support the drainage of dampness below. The former can restrain what comes after but should not be used to drive out what comes first. Any remaining issues may be treated with bitter herbs like bitter thorn and apricot kernels, as well as mulberry root and peppercorns to expel water. All excess water should be eliminated.

In treating illness, there is an order to follow and one must not act chaotically. When the harmful energy is not yet expelled, one must be cautious about supplementation. When the great evil has just receded, there is a fear that it may rebound and intensify, becoming worse than before treatment.[13p]
In the past, there was a person in Henei who fell ill from drinking. The doctor diagnosed him with dampness in the spleen and prescribed a formulation of costus and skylark root, which he ingested more than ten times. The doctor then deceived the patient by altering the formula into pills and had him take them again for over ten times. This was followed by changing the pills back into a powder, which he took once more for over ten times. The patient became increasingly exhausted, sleeping for nearly a whole day and night. When he finally awoke, his stomach felt spacious, and he only craved a small amount of porridge. Day by day, he improved. Although they both diagnosed him with dampness, the methods of tonifying and purging differed greatly, leading to such a distinction.

The "Inner Canon" states: When the Earth element is excessive, rainy humidity spreads. The water from the kidneys is affected by evil influences, leading to an excessive accumulation of fluids. The Taiyang (Greater Yang) oversees Heaven, where humidity changes substances, causing internal accumulation of fluids that disrupt appetite. It is noted that this year, the Yin is in the springs, with dampness monitored by the Earth. The source of the illness arises from the Earth’s Qi. The Shaoyin (Lesser Yin) oversees Heaven, with damp Earth constituting the four aspects of Qi, resulting in nasal congestion, nosebleeds, and excessive fluids. Moreover, with damp Earth builds up, people suffer from fluid retention, edema, and heaviness in their bodies. When Taiyin (Greater Yin) arrives, it leads to an accumulation of yin and obstruction. The arrival of Taiyin causes ample accumulation; both the supremacy of Taiyin and its return are associated with fluid accumulation internally.

In light of this, it is understood that Earth governs the transformation of dampness but not cold, while Water governs the transformation of cold but not dampness. When there is frequent rainfall and the Earth accumulates puddles, it is considered as Water. The canon attributes this to Earth, stating frost and ice solidify, with the windy atmosphere being cold; this is the transformation of Water. Therefore, it is said that Chou and Wei (the Ox and Goat) represent the dampness of Earth, while Chen and Xu (the Dragon and Dog) represent the coldness of Water. The two transformations originate from different elements, leading to distinct ailments. When damp Earth is excessive, fluids accumulate internally. While some people believe that insufficient Spleen Earth is the issue, can ancient texts be easily interpreted? Should they be followed? Or not?[14p]
Phlegm Illness

In general, when a person suffers from phlegm, there are five main types of symptoms: the first is wind phlegm, the second is heat phlegm, the third is damp phlegm, the fourth is alcoholic phlegm, and the fifth is food phlegm. These phlegms reside in the diaphragm, causing the head and eyes to feel unclear and heavy, with thick mucus and saliva, or resulting in cough, wheezing, and fullness. Sometimes there may be tidal fever, and one can use Dusheng Powder to expel it. Next, one may take the modified Decoction or Fengsou Pills, or Liangge Powder alternately. The Inner Canon states this refers to the concept of flowing dampness and moistening dryness.

For phlegm illnesses, there are five types: wind phlegm, heat phlegm, damp phlegm, alcoholic phlegm, and food phlegm. When phlegm is present in the upper stomach, it can harm the head because all yang gathers there. This causes patients to feel heaviness in the head with watery eyes and thick mucus, or to cough and wheeze. Occasionally, there can be chills and fever; in such cases, one can take Red Adzuki Bean Soup to expel it. After vomiting, one should treat according to the symptoms, taking remedies to dispel wind, eliminate heat, drain dampness, and transform phlegm, such as Tongsheng Powder with half-sliced Pinellia to guide qi—what a marvelous approach!

For those recently afflicted with wind phlegm, they tend to feel cold and drink cold beverages; heat phlegm is produced when fire is excessive, and damp phlegm results from stagnant fluids. One can take modified Lianqiao Decoction, Dampness-Removing Pills, or Wuyou Powder. Those with alcoholic phlegm can use Jiedu San Sheng Pills. Lastly, for food phlegm, one may use Han Fangji Pills or select Dan Sha for application. Following these prescriptions will undoubtedly yield miraculous effects.[15p]
Expectoration Method

Phlegm located above the chest and diaphragm, when full and solid, cannot be expelled without expectoration. Zhongjing said: The great method is to expel during spring. This is because in spring the yang qi rises, and both human qi and pathogenic qi are also elevated, thus it is appropriate to expel. The medicines for expectoration can be in the form of pills or powders, and one should stop once the primary ailment is addressed; there is no need to exhaust the dosage, as excess can be harmful. Thus, although there are urgent situations throughout the four seasons requiring expulsion, one does not necessarily have to wait for spring; however, Zhongjing emphasized it as a principal method. Today, people do not grasp this method and have abandoned it entirely. Let us briefly list a few notable prescriptions: In Zhongjing's "Treatise on Cold Damage," there is the scallion and fermented soybean soup to expel headaches, gardenia and magnolia bark decoction to expel vexation, and melon stalk powder to expel cold damage for those experiencing fullness in the lower abdomen after diarrhea with no sweat and wheezing; the "Prescriptions of Historical Medical Texts" prescribes the rare saliva powder to expel internal fullness of the diaphragm, phlegmy cough, loss of voice, and tightly clenched jaws, as if one has lost their spirit; the "Comprehensive Prescriptions" uses the kurbute powder to expel headaches and dizziness, with aversion to wind and nausea; the "Universal Relief Prescriptions" utilizes the wind-catching powder to expel inability to open the mouth, with loss of consciousness; the "General Compilation Prescriptions" includes common mountain herbs for expelling malaria; the "Sun Shang Recipes" employs the Three Holy powder to expel mania; and the "Proven Efficacy Formulas" addresses tongue misalignment.[16p]
The "Inner Canon" states: "The high ones will overpower it." Wang Bing explains: "When the upper is excessive, it should be expelled." Zhong Jing adds: "If food stagnates in the upper abdomen, it should be vomited; also, if there is wine accumulated in the upper abdomen, it should likewise be vomited." Furthermore, he states: "If a patient has cold extremities, and the pulses of both hands are intermittently tight, indicating that pathogenic qi is in the chest, with fullness under the heart causing anxiety and an inability to eat, it is known that the ailment lies in the chest, and it should be vomited." I now apply the vomiting method according to Zhong Jing's formula. I use Gua Ti San to induce vomiting for headache due to pathogenic cold, and a scallion and fermented soybean soup to induce vomiting for miscellaneous headaches. Sometimes, using only Gua Ti San, known as "Dú Shèng," with a bit of tea powder to expel phlegm; or adding a whole scorpion's tail to induce vomiting for stabbing pain in the sides that is gurgling with sound. The "Inner Canon" mentions that dampness in the upper part should be expelled with bitter substances; is this not what it refers to? Nowadays, there are those who also use vomiting, but sometimes it succeeds and sometimes it fails, with some unable to expel or stop the outpour; they do not understand that the method of ascending and expelling is called "lifting phlegm," and the character "lifting" itself encompasses capturing and releasing. Recently, there was a physician who induced vomiting in a woman, and she could not stop for half a month, with saliva accumulating to several buckets, her life hanging by a thread, in a state of panic and miscalculation, seeking my solution. I instructed to brew a musk soup, which resolved the issue immediately upon ingestion.[17p]
Someone asked: How does musk stop vomiting? I replied: The melon seedlings die upon smelling musk. Now, the vomiting remedy with watermelon seeds is meant to resolve this. If colocynth causes continuous vomiting, it is resolved with scallion white soup; if stone medicine causes continuous vomiting, it is resolved with licorice soup. Only for grass and trees causing vomiting, musk is used as an antidote. According to the "Compendium of Materia Medica," the medicines that induce bitter cold vomiting include fermented soybeans, watermelon seeds, tea leaves, gardenia, coptis, bitter smartweed, and rhubarb; those that are acrid and cold include turmeric, common mountain herb, and colocynth; sweet and cold includes the juice of rehmannia; bitter but warm are aromatic wood,远志, and magnolia; acrid and warm include mint and peony; acrid are grains of various species and scallion roots; acrid and cold include light powder; acrid and sweet but warm include aconite and the tip of prepared aconite; sour and cold are alum, green vitriol, and sap; sour and neutral include verdigris; sweet and sour but neutral are red adzuki beans; sour and warm are rice porridge; sour, acrid, and cold include orpiment; sour and cold include white rice; spicy and salty but warm include soap pod; very salty and cold include table salt and green salt; sweet and cold includes tooth nitrate; sweet and slightly warm includes ginseng reed; sweet and spicy but hot includes scorpion tail.[18p]
Among the thirty-six substances, only Changshan, Alum, and Gourd Seeds have slight toxicity; Li Lu, Yuanhua, Qingfen, and Aconite Tails are toxic. The other twenty-six are non-toxic purgatives, and one should choose and use them according to the symptoms. This method should start with a small dose, without causing overwhelming effects, and gradually increase the amount. For those who struggle to expel phlegm, use a probe such as a pin or chicken feather to extract it; if it does not come out, apply juices to aid in expulsion. Continue probing while applying, as all should eventually be expelled. If vomiting leads to dizziness or headaches, drinking ice water will immediately relieve the symptoms; if ice water is unavailable, fresh spring water can also be taken. Strong individuals can be fine after a single purge, while weaker ones may require three or four purges, which should not cause harm. Some may feel significantly better the next day, while others may worsen, as the effects of purging may still be taking hold; in such cases, wait a few days before attempting to purge again. If one feels thirsty, fresh water, melons, and cool foods are acceptable, but one should avoid overeating or heavy, hard-to-digest dishes. Once the heart fire is subdued, the middle burner will harmonize, and yin energy will strengthen. It is crucial to avoid excessive sexual activity and to manage great worries or anger. Adhere to these precautions and do not heed unsubstantiated rumors. Only purge after gaining genuine understanding of the condition, as this will ensure safety.[19p]
Danxi Heart Method
Yuan - Zhu Zhenheng

Phlegm Disease

The pulse is floating, and one should induce vomiting. If the pulse has long been thin, it will be difficult to resolve suddenly, and one must be diligent in treatment. Generally, when treating phlegm, excessive use of purging medicines can lead to deficiency of the spleen qi, making phlegm easier to form and increase. For damp phlegm, use Atractylodes and White Atractylodes; for heat phlegm, use Indigo and the properties of Coptis and Scutellaria; for food phlegm, use Shén Qū (medicated leaven), malt, and hawthorn; for wind phlegm, use Nansh (Arisaema); for chronic phlegm, use Haishi (sea stones), Banxia (Pinellia), and herbs like Xianhe (Corydalis), and take them in pill form. If phlegm is in the diaphragm, one must use vomiting methods; purging will not be effective. Wind phlegm often presents with unusual symptoms, while damp phlegm commonly brings fatigue and weakness. If the qi is solid and phlegm heat is stagnated above, inducing vomiting will be difficult. Clear phlegm is associated with cold; use formulas like Erchen Tang. For thick and turbid phlegm, inducing vomiting is essential. Heat phlegm combined with wind shows more external symptoms. Treat the heat with clearing methods, and for food accumulation, use aggressive treatments, combined with qi tonics to help it descend. If phlegm is caused by excessive fire rising, one should prioritize clearing the fire using substances like White Atractylodes, Scutellaria, and soft gypsum.

For internally caused phlegm, one must use medicines like Ginseng and Astragalus, often combined with ginger juice for transmission, or add Banxia for stronger effects; if the deficiency is severe, add bamboo juice, and if the central qi is insufficient, add Ginseng and Atractylodes.

Phlegm as a substance rises and falls with the qi, present everywhere. For those with spleen deficiency, tonifying spleen qi and clearing central qi to facilitate phlegm descent is recommended, using formulas like Erchen Tang with added White Atractylodes, along with raising herbs like Cimicifuga.[20p]
In the middle jiao, if there is phlegm combined with food accumulation leading to illness, the stomach qi is also reliant on nourishment, and it should not be rashly attacked; if it is entirely expelled, there will be deficiency. Phlegm that has formed into clumps or cannot be expectorated, compounded by qi stagnation, phlegm dampness, or phlegm heat, is all difficult to treat. Phlegm located between the intestines and stomach can be resolved through expelling it. When it is in the meridians, it must be expelled through vomiting. The method of vomiting inherently includes a dispersing principle.

If epilepsy is caused by fright, then fright causes the spirit to leave its residence; when the residence is empty, phlegm is generated. When the blood and qi enter the residence and repel the spirit, it cannot return. For blood injuries, ginger juice must be used to facilitate movement. Huangqin treats heat phlegm, allowing one to clear the fire. Bamboo juice smooths phlegm, and only through ginger juice can it travel through the meridians. Wubeizi can treat chronic phlegm, assisting other medicines in effectively treating stubborn phlegm. Erchen Decoction can address all types of phlegm in the body; if one needs downward action, they should add herbs that guide downward, and if upward action is needed, they should add herbs that guide upward.

In general, when using vomiting herbs, it is advisable to raise and lift the qi to facilitate vomiting. Herbs such as Fangfeng, Yanzhi, Chuanxiong, Jiegang, Yacha, and fresh ginger, or the use of wax gourd stem powder can be utilized.

For cases of wind-phlegm disease, wind-phlegm medicines must be used, such as BaiFuzhi, Tianma, Xionghuang, Niuhuang, Pianqing, Jiangcan, and Zhuya Zaojiao.

In any individual, if there are masses found in the upper, middle, or lower body, they are often phlegm. After inquiring what they usually like to eat, one should use medication after expelling.

Scholar Xu used Cangzhu to treat phlegm that formed into a pocket, it was extraordinarily effective. Phlegm, combined with stagnant blood, ultimately resulted in the formation of this pocket.[21p]
In cases of dizziness and noise, it indicates the phlegm caused by fire. Use Er Chen Tang with added gardenia fruit, yellow locust root, and yellow gentian. If there is acidity in the breath, this signifies food stagnation with heat and an upward movement of fire. Use yellow gentian as the main ingredient, with pinellia and nascent ginger as deputies, and tangerine peel as a messenger. If there is excess heat, add indigo.

For phlegm under the ribs, only white mustard seeds can reach it. If phlegm is beneath the skin and outer layers, ginger juice and bamboo juice must be used to guide it. For phlegm in the limbs, bamboo juice is essential to release it. For phlegm congestion in the throat that is dry and cannot be expelled or swallowed, use phlegm-transforming herbs paired with salty tastes to soften the masses (e.g., pinellia, apricot kernel, sea stone, balloon flower, and forsythia), mixed with ginger juice and honey into lozenges for sucking.

Hai Fen refers to sea stone; it can reduce hot phlegm, dry damp phlegm, soften solidified phlegm, and dissolve stubborn phlegm. It may be used in pill form but not in decoctions. Bitter orange can expel phlegm, capable of breaking down walls. Xiao Wei Dan treats phlegm heat in the diaphragm, wind phlegm, damp phlegm, and pain in the shoulders, but it may deplete stomach qi and should be used sparingly for those with food accumulation and solid phlegm. Shen Yu Wan can dissipate phlegm.

If there is something stuck in the throat that cannot be coughed out or swallowed, this is old phlegm. In severe cases, it should be expelled; in milder cases, use pinellia varieties. If there is excessive qi, definitely use Jing Li.

Tian Hua Fen can significantly reduce heat phlegm in the diaphragm. Phlegm in the diaphragm can cause madness or forgetfulness. For wind phlegm, bamboo juice should also be used, and it can nourish the blood, serving the same purpose as Jing Li.[22p]
Those who can tolerate heavier foods should use these two ingredients for quick and stable effects. The two infusions treat phlegm that is lodged under the skin and in the meridians, which must be assisted with ginger juice. Leek juice treats stagnant blood that is not circulating, and if there is fluid in the middle burner, consuming two or three cups of fresh juice will cause restlessness in the chest, but later provides relief.

Phlegm can cause various issues such as wheezing, coughing, vomiting, discomfort, dizziness, noise in the stomach, palpitations, chills, heat, pain, swelling, a feeling of blockage, sounds in the chest and ribs, or a constant cold sensation in the back and heart, as well as numbness in the limbs. These are all caused by phlegm and fluid accumulation. To effectively treat phlegm, one does not treat the phlegm directly but adjusts the qi. When the qi is smooth, all bodily fluids will also flow accordingly.[23p]
The ancient method for treating phlegm through sweating, purging, and warming has, in my view, less merit than prioritizing the regulation of qi and then guiding it in a proper direction. Wang Yinjun states that clear phlegm is cold, while yellow and turbid phlegm is hot. If it starts clear, it can become yellow and turbid with time. Clear and white phlegm is thin and floats above, while yellow and turbid phlegm is thick and sticky, settling below. When coughing results in easy expulsion, the phlegm is clear and white; when coughing fails to bring it up, the phlegm becomes yellow and stagnant. If phlegm is coughed up for an extended period, and humidity and heat accumulate, causing a blockage above and below, it may entirely lose its clarity, even to the point of blood being present. When the blood deteriorates, it turns into black phlegm, symptomatic of a serious, obscure condition. Furthermore, clear phlegm has a mild taste, but over time it may develop a foul flavor, becoming sour, spicy, fishy, or bitter, among other unpleasant tastes. Many diseases involve phlegm, which is not widely recognized. The human body can harbor tuberculosis, which may not be painful, red, or produce pus—this is attributed to phlegm accumulation. Effective treatment for phlegm should fundamentally involve strengthening the spleen and correcting dampness.[24p]
Additional Thoughts on Diagnosis and Treatment of Phlegm Disease

Blood and qi are the essence of the body. When the essence becomes depleted, pathogenic factors can invade, possibly due to underlying conditions. If both blood and qi are deficient and phlegm resides in the middle burner, it obstructs the processes of rising and descending, leading to the dysfunction of the twelve organs. Consequently, one's perception and actions may become deluded. Treating these patients with pathogens will surely lead to death. Alas! What injustice! Who is to blame?

The younger brother of Xianmu, aged seventeen or eighteen, during the summer experienced great fatigue and thirst, excessively drinking plum juice, and subsequently suffered from profound shock three to four times, leading to delusions and hallucinations, resembling a possessed state. Upon examining his pulse, both hands showed a weak and wiry pulse but were also heavy. I said, "The rapid pulse indicates heat; the weak and wiry pulse reflects the profound shock." Additionally, the sourness from the plum juice had stagnated in the middle burner. To replenish the deficiency, clear heat, and expel phlegm, his condition could be stabilized.

I thus prescribed a decoction of ginseng, white atractylodes, dried tangerine peel, poria, scutellaria, and lonicera, mixed with bamboo sap and ginger juice for him to take. After ten days without effect, everyone criticized the inadequacy of the prescription. Upon further pulse examination, I discerned that his deficiency was incomplete and that the phlegm had not been successfully expelled. I adjusted the formula to include chrysanthemum sap and after another ten days, he recovered.

My cousin, after drinking heartily one day, also exhibited nonsensical speech and delusions. Upon inquiry, it seemed that he was possessed by the spirit of his deceased brother, recounting events from his life. My uncle reprimanded him, saying, "This is not the case; it is merely due to excessive consumption of fish and wine that has resulted in phlegm." A large bowl of saltwater was forced upon him, resulting in the expulsion of one to two liters of phlegm. Consequently, he sweated profusely, fell into a deep sleep for the night, and thereafter felt well.[25p]
A woman of the Jin family, in her prime, attended a banquet in the hot season and returned home. Her mother-in-law questioned her about being out of order in her seating, causing her to blush and feel ashamed. As a result, she fell ill and became incoherent, often repeating, “I am not myself.” Her pulse was rapid and string-like. I said, “This is not an imbalance but a phlegm disorder. Just by nourishing the spleen, clearing heat, and guiding out phlegm, she should recover in a few days.” However, her family did not believe me and invited several shamans to sprinkle water and chant spells for her. After about ten days, she died. When asked why the wrongly diagnosed illness led to death so swiftly, I replied: “In the hot month attending a feast, the external environment is steaming hot, and spicy food is appetizing. Internally, she had stagnant heat, worsened by phlegm accumulation and feelings of shame and distress. How could the phlegm and heat not be overwhelming? Now, in addition, she was startled by medical measures, which frightened her spirit and unsettled her blood.”[26p]
Spraying with medicinal water solidifies its essence and tightens its surface, preventing sweat from escaping. If sweat does not escape, then internal heat steams and burns, causing blood to become unsettled, leading to the depletion of yin and the inability of yang to stand alone. If one does not die, what is the wait for! Some say that there is a section on forbidden spells in the "Essential Secrets of External Affairs," so can it be disregarded? I say: transforming essence into energy is merely a minor technique, suitable for treating small ailments. However, if there is internal deficiency and external excess, one must use a proper and grand method, which has been established and can be clearly examined. Yet, the virtue of talismanic water is only effective for heat phlegm in the stomach; a sip of cool water can alleviate stomach heat, which can indeed bring comfort. But if there is internal injury and deficiency, combined with the severe cold of winter, swallowing talismanic water will certainly freeze the stomach and cause harm. When there is stagnant heat above and heat pathogens on the surface, sweat must be released to resolve it. If one achieves coolness while the skin pores remain firm and tight, how can the heat be resolved? This must lead to internal attack, separating yin and yang, and causing blood and qi to conflict, bringing death ever closer.[27p]
Phlegm Illness Emetic Method

Emetic Method: Use a combination of tea buds, thin water, ginger juice, a little vinegar, and a small amount of Luosang powder, along with fangfeng and jiegeng to stimulate the qi, facilitating vomiting. Emetic Method: Use aconite tips, jiegeng, ginseng, melon stems, Lilu, mugwort leaves, tea buds, etc. These can induce vomiting on their own without needing to probe with the hand; both the medicine and broth can induce vomiting. Emetic Method: First use cloth to tie around the shoulders and waist in a place without ventilation to perform this method. Grind half a sheng of radish seeds and strain with a bowl of pulpy water, then mix in a little oil and honey, and drink when it’s warm. Afterwards, use a goose feather to induce vomiting. When using a goose feather, it must be soaked in tung oil and washed with soapberry water to remove fat, then dried for use. Another method: Use half a pound of shrimp with shells, boiled with garlic, scallions, ginger, and other spices to make a broth. First eat the shrimp, followed by drinking the broth, and use a feather to induce vomiting, making sure to tightly constrict the abdomen.[28p]
The "Inner Canon" states: All stagnant qi belongs to the lung metal. When lung qi is stagnant, it generates heat; when heat is excessive, it produces phlegm. Danxi notes: From heat comes accumulation, from accumulation comes phlegm, which carries blood stasis and leads to the formation of lumps; this is the sequence for the symptoms of stagnation, pain, and reversed stomach issues. Wang Yinjun mentions that the phlegm syndrome has not been clearly detailed in ancient and modern times. Although medical texts differentiate between various types of fluids—suspended, retained, supporting, and phlegm fluids—there is little understanding of their source as a disease. Symptoms may include headaches, dizziness, tinnitus; or spasms of the mouth and eyes, itchiness in the eyebrows and ears; or swelling and stiffness in the limbs that feels like pain but is not; or tooth and cheek pain, with gingival swelling, presenting different levels of pain and itch; or acid regurgitation, noisy belching; or difficulty swallowing, with what is coughed up appearing like blackened coal, resembling torn cotton, peach resin, or clam meat; or a feeling beneath the heart like ice, with cold pain at times; or strange dreams of ghosts; or weakness in the legs and ankles, sudden back pain; or general aches in the joints of the limbs without a specific pattern, even leading to numbness in the hands and pain in the arms, resembling sprains; or a painful area in the spine the size of a palm, similar to ice cold; or a feeling throughout the body as if insects are crawling; or itching along the eyes, mouth sores, and tongue ulcers, severe enough to cause a feeling of a closed throat; or lumps around the neck that resemble throat cancer but are not; or a sensation in the chest and abdomen as if two energies are intertwined, causing obstruction and discomfort, like smoke rising, with a feeling of heat in the head and face; or feelings of despair, madness, paralysis from stroke; or conditions like exhaustion, wind-dampness, or beriberi; or palpitations and anxiety beneath the heart, akin to fearing capture; or wheezing, coughing, and vomiting; or the vomiting of cold saliva, green water, or black water, which may indicate lung abscess, intestinal toxicity, or severe complications with pus and spasms.[29p]
All internal and external diseases arise from phlegm. When fluids become thick and turn into phlegm and drinking, they surge upwards causing dryness of the mouth and throat. When they flow downwards, they block the flow of urine and feces, leading to a face that appears like dry bones and hair that is charred and dry. In women, this results in blocked menstruation, while in children, it can cause convulsions and seizures. The treatment should first focus on expelling the bad phlegm, then consider the condition's deficiency or excess to adjust the therapy. Therefore, the formulation of the "Rolling Phlegm Pill" is crucial for addressing phlegm and fluid issues in the three burn areas. It seems to me that many treatise are thorough, yet if they do not differentiate between deficiency and excess, and simply use harsh medicines, they might not truly address the core issue. There are differences in constitution; the severity of disease can vary. A misstep may lead to greater complications. Danxi said: Excessive use of draining medicines for phlegm can weaken the spleen's energy, causing phlegm to easily recur. He also stated that in cases where phlegm and food stagnation occur in the middle burner, the stomach qi needs nurturing; thus, it should not be recklessly attacked. If the attack is too severe, the condition may worsen and become more deficient. The "Rolling Phlegm Pill" should only be given to those with strong vital energy and substantial phlegm accumulation. It must not be used lightly on individuals with weak energy.[30p]
Essential Strategies for Diagnosis and Treatment
[Ming Dynasty, Dai Sigong]

Ceasing Consumption to Resolve Phlegm

There are six types of fluids: suspended, overflowing, obstructed, phlegmatic, retained, and latent. Phlegm-damp is merely one of these six types. When a person suffers from a condition referred to as phlegm-damp, it is generally due to prolonged stagnation, leading to the accumulation of phlegm, often caused by blockages in the airways resulting in the obstruction of bodily fluids. This can be likened to a blocked ditch where water accumulates and stagnates, causing backflow and leading to foul, corrupted smells.

If one does not open up the ditch but instead seeks to clear and purify the stagnant water, it is illogical. Conditions such as wheezing, coughing, nausea, diarrhea, dizziness, palpitations, chills and fevers, painful swelling, distended epigastrium, or sounds of fluid in the chest and sides, or a sensation of coolness in the back and heart—all result from the dampness, reminiscent of the foul, corrupted water.

Therefore, a good treatment for phlegm involves focusing on the qi rather than directly addressing the phlegm. When qi is regulated, the bodily fluids will follow suit. It is advisable to use a combination of Suzi Jiangqi Decoction and Phlegm-Guide Decoction, both in equal parts. Alternatively, one may utilize Xiao Banxia Fuling Decoction, adding Zhi Shi and Mu Xiang in equal weight, taken in five pill doses, or prepare a dosage of five pills brewed as a potion, which is especially effective.

In general, if there are no other issues and only a few phlegmatic symptoms, whether clear or viscous, it is recommended to use Er Chen Decoction or Xiao Banxia Fuling Decoction. If phlegm is abundant, intermittently taking Qingzhou White Pills mixed with Lai Fudan is beneficial.[31p]
The divine remedy returns to the elixir, named Qing Shen Wan. This is not only for treating phlegm and fluids but is especially effective for alleviating coughs, vomiting, and counteracting reversed stomach energy. If the medicine does not work, use Er Sheng Tang with half a qian of Mu Xiang. If stubborn phlegm rises with the qi and is not resolved by the medicine, it should be addressed from below; it is advisable to use Wu Ge Kuan Zhong San with half a qian of Ban Xia, swallow the broken pills, and also take Ban Liu Wan. To prevent constipation and ensure complete relief from fluids, Ban Liu Wan should be taken regularly. If bowel movements naturally occur without medication, and for elderly or weak individuals, it is important to facilitate urination, using Xiao Ban Xia Fu Ling Tang, replacing with Chi Ling and doubling the amount; alternatively, use Dao Tan Tang with half a qian of Zhu Ling.[32p]
For phlegm and fluids causing dizziness or inducing syncope, it is advisable to supplement with Shēng Táng with Mu Xiang, and swallow Qingzhou Baiwanzi mixed with Ling Sha Dan, called Qingjin Dan; alternatively, swallow Yangzheng Dan or Banliuhuan.

When phlegm and fluids flow into the limbs, causing soreness in the shoulders and back, along with weakness and numbness in the hands, if a doctor mistakenly diagnoses it as wind, that is incorrect. It is recommended to use Dao Tan Tang with half a coin of Mu Xiang and Jiang Huang.

If phlegm and fluids change into various symptoms, do not be misled by these symptoms and falsely name conditions. The treatment for phlegm should take precedence; once the phlegm is resolved, the symptoms will heal. In cases of sudden faintness, crookedness of the mouth and eyes, appearing as if it is a stroke but actually not, with limbs feeling heavy and the body feeling like a floating cloud—these are all caused by phlegm and fluids. Additionally, there may be kidney deficiency with cold preventing the retention of water, causing water evil to overflow upward and lead to phlegm and fluids; for this, Bawei Wan is suitable.

For those who have a history of phlegm and fluids causing pain in the shoulder and back, Xingxiang San should be used, or Dao Tan Tang followed by Wutaowan.[33p]
Medical Principles [Ming - Lou Ying]

Phlegm and Fluid

For anyone with phlegm, there will certainly be dark ash-black discoloration on the eyelids and under the eyes, easily observable without pulse diagnosis. Dark eyes and flushed cheeks indicate hot phlegm; a large yellow face also suggests hot phlegm. The external signs will surely include fullness and heat in the chest, a dry mouth with a longing for coolness, constipated stools, and red hot urine. Prolonged conditions may lead to wind, dizziness, tinnitus, and visual disturbances, with many signs of deficiency. When treating, the use of warming drugs is required; prolonged use will certainly lead to a large, strong pulse, can cause extreme heat and stroke, and should be addressed urgently.

If the eyes are dark and walking is labored with groans, this indicates phlegm that has entered the bones. Symptoms include pain throughout the body and joints. Dark eyes with a muddy complexion, weakness in the limbs, and difficulty in bending and stretching point to wind-damp phlegm. Dark eyes with shortness of breath signify phlegm due to shock. A large pulse on both sides of the radial artery indicates the presence of phlegm in the chest, which may be expelled; if the patient fears vomiting, use an enema instead.

For anyone with a cold sensation along the spine resembling a line, it is advisable to induce vomiting or use a purgative. If patients have ailments that are unresponsive to numerous medicines, and their pulse is hidden yet strong, it indicates phlegm; in this case, use the Miao Ying Pill.

Modification principles: for shock phlegm, add two qian of cinnabar and two whole scorpions, taking eight or nine pills regularly; for alcohol-associated phlegm, add two qian each of realgar and whole scorpion, taking ten pills each time; for hot phlegm, add equal parts of gypsum powder, taking three to six pills each time; for cold phlegm, add equal parts of pepper, cloves, scorpion, and cinnamon, taking twenty-five pills each time.[34p]
Phlegm as a disease can manifest as偏头风 (side head wind), 雷头风 (thunder head wind), or 太阳头痛 (sun headache). Symptoms include dizziness as if seated in a boat, a wandering spirit, twitching of the mouth and eyes, itchiness in the eyebrows, ears, and every part of the body; swelling and hardness in the jaw and limbs, resembling pain yet not quite so. The whole body feels dry and itchy, scratching brings forth itchy rashes, the skin feels hot like fire, with a color resembling brocade. The teeth and gums may feel itchy or painful, with pain shifting unpredictably. The mouth feels full of floating teeth, with pain and itchiness varying, belching sourness, smelling burnt, feeling a bean-like scent in the throat, causing annoyance and nasal obstruction, with difficulty swallowing or expelling, sometimes expelled by sneezing or salivating when in motion. The phlegm may appear like black ink, broken fluff, peach gum, or clam meat.

At times, the heart feels as if ice or iron is lodged inside, causing stagnation and oppression, leading to repeated belching and symptoms resembling phlegm in the diaphragm. Dreams may involve punishment and violence with swords, or being surrounded by walls in a house with difficulty escaping, not knowing the way out. Other dreams may entail flames with smoke surrounding, with the smell of burning bones and no clear path to exit. Sometimes, there may not be an external trigger, yet feelings of anger and sorrow arise, with tears raining down upon waking.

Occasionally, while wandering outdoors, one may see two moons shining together at the horizon or multiple beams of golden light, only to turn and find nothing. One may experience weakness in the knees and feet, pain in the bones, waist, and kidneys, difficulty in breathing, or pain between the body’s muscles and bones as if being struck, coming and going unpredictably. There may also be occasional numbness and pain in the arms, resembling rheumatism, restlessness while lying down, feeling pricked like with thorns, or heaviness in the limbs, with difficulty opening and closing the eyes as if stung by a wasp.

During changes in weather, chest tightness and blocked energy may cause toothaches and throat pain. When the mouth ulcerates and the tongue rots, sudden outbursts may bring forth repeated sneezing, initially producing thick, sticky mucus followed by clear, profuse fluid. One may see darkness before the eyes, hear wind behind the brain, and experience the buzzing of cicadas in the ears, with the eyes twitching uncontrollably due to the disarray.[35p]
Those who treat it do not say that the pores are not tight, and when the wind invades, they say the upper part is abundant and the lower part is empty, sometimes calling it cold vacuity or the onset of evil. Only the adept in treating this suffering can manage it. The onset of the illness feels as if there are two energies intertwining in the chest and abdomen, leading to choking and annoyance, like smoke and fire surging upward, causing the head and face to feel hot, with dizzy eyes and ringing ears. Phlegm, saliva, tears—all surge from the lungs and stomach, causing the hair to stand on end, leading to repeated sneezing, and then a restlessness throughout the body. One may shed their clothes and feel cold, which may provide temporary relief; during the coolness of spring or autumn, adding clothes and blankets may also temporarily alleviate it. Some may drink cold water suddenly, others may drink to excess, bringing temporary comfort, yet none can eradicate the root of the illness.

Thus, the secret recipe of aromatic pills has often shown great efficacy, curing tens of thousands, but it is not wished to be casually shared with others, so it is stated in veiled language. The poem says: "In the steamer, one turns over in a golden belt, now wearing a hat deep in the grass hall. Meeting at eighteen, seeking the correct measurement, the refinement of salt makes the blue mist heavier than sinking. Among the seventeen taels, half a tael of the sinking, water and tablets of phoenix seeds must be measured. To eliminate the strange illness and calm the mind, the watery diarrhea of both bodies cannot be endured."[36p]
On Old Phlegm

Phlegm is a term for a disease. When a person's qi and blood are clear and flowing, bodily fluids circulate properly, and there is no phlegm. However, when qi and blood become turbid and stagnant, bodily fluids do not clear, leading to their accumulation and transformation into phlegm. The root of phlegm is water, originating in the kidneys. The activity of phlegm is linked to dampness, primarily governed by the spleen. The ancients used Erchen Decoction as a general remedy for phlegm because it strengthens the spleen and dries dampness, thus treating the symptoms. It is indeed effective for damp phlegm, cold phlegm, phlegm fluids, and phlegm saliva.

If phlegm is caused by fire rising, causing the lung qi to become obstructed, leading to coughing during this time, and there is old, accumulated phlegm that forms into thick blocks, making it difficult to expel, this phlegm is all due to the fire evil rising, affecting the upper jiao, and obstructing the lung qi. Thus, the bodily fluids that follow the qi rise are steamed by fire, becoming turbid and stagnated. Over years, it becomes deeply rooted, hence called old phlegm or obstructed phlegm, and its essence is fire.

The illness resides in the upper jiao, particularly between the heart and lungs, and the throat, unlike the damp phlegm of the middle jiao's spleen and stomach, cold phlegm, phlegm fluids, or phlegm saliva, making it difficult to treat with decoctions. It cannot be cured with herbs like Pinellia, Poria, Atractylodes, Zhiqiao, and Nanjing. Instead, the focus should be on relieving obstruction, lowering fire, clearing and moistening the lung metal, and dissolving the accumulated phlegm to treat it gently and effectively.[37p]
The current prescription for phlegm-dissolving pills includes one tael each of Asparagus, Huangqin (Scutellaria), stir-fried with alcohol, Hai Fen (sea powder), and Tangerine peel; five qian each of crushed Platycodon, Forsythia, and Cyperus soaked and stir-fried in light saltwater; three qian each of ground Indigowood and Glauber's salt; and one tael of ground Trichosanthes fruit, all to be made into a fine powder. Add a small amount of honey and ginger juice, mix the herbs very well, and form pills the size of longan. Melt one pill in your mouth or chew it well, then swallow with clear broth; alternatively, make balls the size of millet and take five to sixty with light ginger soup.

[Note: The ingredients here have sweet, bitter, and salty qualities and are cold in nature, capable of softening hardness, relieving stagnation, dissolving phlegm, and reducing fire, but they might harm the stomach. It is suitable for those with excessive spleen deficiency, phlegm caused by stagnation and internal heat. However, for those with weak spleen and qi deficiency leading to phlegm, using this could cause fullness, acid regurgitation, abdominal swelling, and hindered urination, potentially leading to death.]

Old phlegm is often found in those who drink alcohol.[38p]
The ascending wine vapors create fire, causing both the lungs and stomach to be afflicted by heat, resulting in stagnation. Use Tian Maidong and Huangqin to drain lung fire; Haifen and Mangxiao are salty and help soften stagnation; Lou Ren moistens the lungs and clears phlegm, Xiangfu Mi alleviates stagnation and descends qi, Lianqiao opens stagnation and lowers fire, and Qingdai cools excess heat. Avoid using aromatic and drying agents.

[Note: If there are signs of poor appetite or chest discomfort, this indicates weakness of the central qi, and the main formula should be Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang. Once the central qi is strengthened, phlegm will naturally be resolved. If kidney qi is deficient and fluids cannot descend, leading to turbid phlegm, it is a true viscera syndrome, and the primary formula should be Liu Wei Di Huang Wan. Once kidney qi is robust and fluids are clarified, there will be no phlegm. Additionally, there may be cases of phlegm due to spleen and stomach deficiency, where the center’s qi is weak and unable to digest food, or due to excessive harshness leading to worse spleen qi, causing fluids to stagnate and form phlegm; in these cases, the focus should be on strengthening the spleen and stomach.][39p]
Introduction to Medicine [Ming Dynasty, Li Chan]

Phlegm: New and Old Distinction

Phlegm is formed from bodily fluids and blood, rising and falling with the Qi. When Qi and blood are harmonious, phlegm flows and does not accumulate; if there is internal or external injury, it can become blocked and cause problems. Fresh and light phlegm appears bluish-white, thin, and has a mild taste. Old and heavy phlegm is yellow, turbid, thick, sticky, and hard to expel, gradually becoming foul-tasting with sour, spicy, fishy, greasy, salty, and bitter notes. In the initial stages of phlegm symptoms, there may be headaches and fever, resembling an exterior pathogenic condition; if it persists, there could be tidal fevers at night, resembling internal injury from Yin fire. Additionally, if phlegm fluid causes pain in the limbs and joints, it resembles a wind condition. However, in cases of phlegm-induced chest fullness and reduced appetite, the skin color remains the same, and the pulse is slippery, irregular, and unstable, indicating a different condition.[40p]
All Diseases Associated with Phlegm

People know that qi and blood can cause illness, but they are unaware that phlegm diseases are even more numerous. When phlegm originates in the spleen, it may lead to fatigue in the limbs, abdominal pain, swelling, and diarrhea, known as damp phlegm. If combined with food stagnation and blood stasis, it can form nodules and masses, called food phlegm. If it lingers in the stomach region, it may cause frequent vomiting and acid regurgitation, with an uneasy sensation rising, as well as heat in the head and face, referred to as hot phlegm. If it arises from drinking alcohol, it may result in dry heaving, belching, and pain in the sides, known as alcohol phlegm. When it originates in the lungs, it may cause a dry cough, paleness like withered bones, along with dryness in the throat and mouth, referred to as dry phlegm, which can develop into chronic phlegm or stagnant phlegm over time. Moreover, emotional disturbances can cause phlegm to obstruct the throat and diaphragm, leading to fullness in the chest and sides, known as qi phlegm. If it confuses the heart, it may lead to palpitations, madness, and strange dreams, referred to as heat phlegm. If it affects the liver, it may cause dizziness and headaches, shaking of the eyes, itching of the ears, pain in the sides, paralysis on one side, numbness, and odd symptoms, called wind phlegm. Accumulated in the kidneys, it may lead to soreness and weakness in the legs and knees, stiffness and pain in the lower back, coldness in the limbs, joint pain, known as cold phlegm, also referred to as deficient phlegm.[41p]
Generally, if the entire body feels habitually as if worms are crawling, or if there are nodules inside the body that are neither red nor swollen, or if there are nodules on the neck that resemble sores but are not, or if there is throat obstruction like a horse's bridle, or if there is a sensation as if two energies are entwined in the chest and abdomen, causing choking and discomfort, or if there is a constant cold pain in the back, or if there is cold pain beneath the heart, or if the limbs are swollen and hard, feeling like pain but not quite, or if there are intermittent sharp pains in the joints, or if one vomits cold saliva, green water, or black bile, or if there is pus in urine or stools, or if the circulation is blocked, leading to consumption, or if a woman experiences missed menstrual periods, or if a child has convulsions, one must first eliminate phlegm before regulating the body. Additionally, for injuries to the breastbone from fighting, where the pain is unbearable and blood dispersing medication has no effect, drinking one's own urine may lead to vomiting phlegm and instantly relieve the pain. This holds true for hundreds of diseases involving phlegm.

Identifying Colors

Wind Phlegm: Caused by external wind pathogens, or dryness from the kidneys causing movement in wood, or internal wind and heat, appears blue and shiny. For wind deficiency, use San Sheng drink or Gu Long Hu Dan; for wind-heat, use Xiao Sheng Feng Tang, Sou Feng Hua Tan Wan, Si Shen Dan, or Zhu Li Gao.

Cold Phlegm: Due to cold from environment or cool drinks, appears deep blue-black like ash, and is prone to spitting or wheezing. For mild cases, use Wu Ji San or Huo Xiang Zheng Qi San; for severe cases, use Wen Zhong Hua Tan Wan or Gu Ban Liu Wan.

Damp Phlegm: Either from external dampness or stagnation of fluids. If the color is white and causes rapid breathing, use Qian Qian Tang; for heart pain, use Dan Ban Xia Wan or Shen Zhu Wan; for damp heat, which appears yellow, use Zhong He Wan or Qing Ge Cang Sha Wan; if the dampness is internal, use Qing Meng Shi Wan.[42p]
Fire Heat as Cause

Heat Phlegm: This is caused by rich foods building up heat, or externally caused erroneous warmth, resulting in yellow sputum, which may contain blood or appear purple. Use Qingqi Huatan Wan boiled to take, or Da Jin Hua Wan and Gun Tan Wan.

Fire Phlegm: This results from consuming thick foods and bedding, which steams the body's fluids, creating thick and turbid phlegm. Use Er Chen Tang with additions of Qinqin, Lian, and Shan Zhi, or suppressing pills and moistening pills.

Stagnant Phlegm: This is prolonged fire phlegm trapped in the heart and lungs, leading to blockage in the chest and difficult expectoration. Avoid drying drugs like Nanshing and Banxia; it is best to open appetite, lower fire, clear metal, and nourish the lungs gently during treatment. Use Jie Zhai Huatan Wan, Xie Fu Qingjin Wan, Dan Bei Mu Wan, and Xia Tian Gao.

Qi Phlegm: This arises from emotional stagnation, leading to difficulty in expectoration or swallowing. The phlegm resembles broken cotton or plum pits. Use Si Qi Tang. For prolonged cases, omit Su Zi, and use Huang Qin, Shan Zhi, or Hai Shi. Use San Xian Wan and Qian Jin Zhi Mi Wan.

Diet and Alcohol as Cause

Diet Phlegm: This occurs from undigested food, resulting in blockages. Use Ju Ban Zhi Shu Wan. For sputum causing wheezing and urgency, use Lou Shi Wan or Shan Zha Mai Ya Tang. For those with Yin deficiency, use Huang Bai Wan. If there is a hard feeling in the heart cavity like a cup, this is named Qi Fen; use Zhi Zhu Wan boiled to take. If phlegm is as hard as a cup, with occasional water sounds, use Shen Bao Wan. For wine phlegm, use Xiao Diao Zhong Tang and Xiang Fu Lou Qing Dai Wan.[43p]
Phlegm and fluids have five types.

Phlegm accumulates in the channels, coming out through the lungs as a cough; saliva accumulates in the spleen, flowing from the corners of the mouth; fluid arises in the stomach, being expelled from the epigastrium. The five types of fluids and six symptoms, together with retained fluids and hidden fluids, form a single entity. All of this is due to the retention of water and tea or wine, combined with external pathogens causing cold, and emotions clashing to produce phlegm. In cases where phlegm from alcohol persists and dampness prevails, it closely resembles the water condition in severe cold, with a pulse often being wiry and slippery or hidden, and the skin under the eyes appearing dark and ashen.

Phlegm and fluids cause stagnation in the intestines and stomach, leading to rumbling sounds in the abdomen, resulting in dramatic weight gain or loss; suspended fluids cause water to flow in the flanks, resulting in pain when coughing or spitting; overflowing fluids cause water to flow into the limbs, resulting in heavy body pain; stagnant fluids cause water to accumulate above the diaphragm (in cases of food inability), leading to shortness of breath; retained fluids cause water to stagnate below the heart, resulting in a chilling sensation like a cold hand, possible shortness of breath and thirst, and joint pains in the limbs. Pain in the flanks radiates to the back, and coughing increases; hidden fluids cause water to stagnate and fullness of the diaphragm, leading to vomiting, coughing, fever with chills, back pain, tearing, or shivering.

Zhongjing treats various fluids under the skin and in the channels with the Xiao Qinglong Decoction; those in the chest and diaphragm are treated with Guadi Powder; those in the limbs and channels are treated with Wuling Powder; and those in the intestines and stomach are treated with Shizao Decoction.[44p]
This is all a method of treating the symptoms superficially. For mild cases, use a decoction with Shensu and sweat it out, or vomit using Erchen Decoction with added Fangfeng and Jiegeng. For more serious blockages, apply Wuyin Decoction or the Jiezhuh Wan. In between, alternate with Xiaobansha Decoction, Gutingli Powder, Jiezhuh Wan, Wen Zhong Huatan Wan, Qingqi Huatan Wan, and Banxia Wenfei Decoction, adjusting according to deficiency or excess without being overly fixed.

The ancient method prioritizes guiding Qi first and then dispersing. When Qi rises it belongs to fire; phlegm that moves due to Qi is called phlegm-Qi, treated with the Shunqi Daotan Decoction. If it’s due to fire, it’s called phlegm-fire, thus treated by the Qingtian Daotan Decoction. If due to dampness, it's termed damp-phlegm, for which we use Qushi Daotan Decoction. The universally applied Erchen Decoction can facilitate stool and prolong urination, especially vital for guidance and dispersion.

When wind is involved, add Nanshen, Zaoji, BaiFuzhu, and Zhuli; for cold-related issues, use Banxia with ginger, Fuzhu, and ginger juice; for fire-induced conditions, include Shigao and Qingtai; damp conditions call for Cangzhu and Baizhu; dryness needs (Cao's) Lou and Xingren; chronic phlegm requires Haishi, Mangxiao, and (Cao's) Lou; food stagnation adds ShanZha, Shenqu, and MaiYa; water retention incorporates Binglang; phlegm located below the ribs uses Baijiezi for movement; phlegm in the limbs utilizes Zhuli; for phlegm in the meridians utilize this probing method; and for phlegm in the skin or outer membranes, combine Baijiezi, Zhuli, and ginger juice; in cases of strong Qi, use Jingli.[45p]
Phlegm Syndrome

Phlegm originates in the kidneys, moves in the spleen, and lodges in the lungs. With the rise and fall of water and fire, and the harmony of the spleen and stomach, from where does phlegm emerge? If yang is deficient and the kidneys are cold, they cannot restrain the pathological water, leading to the overflow of cold phlegm, which may cause cough and wheezing at night. For this, Bawei Pill, Sanwei Anshen Pill, or Heixi Dan can be used to settle the condition. If phlegm accumulation leads to counterflow, Suzi Jiangqi Decoction, Sansheng Drink, or Gu Liu Gong Dan should be employed. If the spleen is deficient and unable to transform, it is advisable to tonify and dry dampness with Liujunzi Decoction, adding Zhuli and ginger juice. If overexertion damages the spleen’s ability to rise and descend, then Buzhong Yiqi Decoction should be used, with additions of Banxia, Zhuli, and ginger juice.[46p]
When there is deficiency of qi and blood, phlegm obstructing the central gave, and blocking the clear pathways, it is advisable to warm the middle and dry the spleen with Er Chen Tang; if there is qi deficiency, combine with Si Jun Zi Tang; if there is blood deficiency, combine with Si Wu Tang; if there is yin deficiency with kidney fire rising and lung dryness, combine Er Chen Tang with Si Wu Tang, removing Chuan Xiong and Ban Xia, and adding Bei Mu, Mai Men Dong, (Herb) Lou Ren, and Jie Geng to moisten and reduce it. Alternatively, use Shen Qi Wan or San Yi Shen Qi Wan. It is said: phlegm has no nourishment method. Moreover, chronic phlegm is congealed and sticky; it cannot be resolved without temporarily using warming herbs to guide it, otherwise there will be a risk of obstruction. When wind and cold phlegm and qi are internally constrained, not using warming dispersants, how can one open up the stagnation? These issues cannot be strictly confined to a lack of nourishment. Generally, when phlegm causes wheezing with a loud voice, pulse is scattered, and sweat is profuse like oil, the body feels cold, it can lead to death.

Phlegm is the transformation of bodily fluids; wind injures the lungs, and dampness injures the spleen, congealing and becoming turbid. Externally, symptoms manifest as discomfort in the head and neck, resembling cold and heat causing a febrile disease. Initially, there is fullness and oppression in the chest, qi rushes up to the throat, with a floating pulse indicating abnormality. If there is heat, use Shen Su Yin, Jin Fei Cao San, or Chai Hu Ban Xia Tang; if there is no heat, use Er Chen Tang or Wen Dan Tang. Phlegm-dispelling decoction can be used broadly. For phlegm obstructing the chest, use He Ding Dan or Zhi Ju Er Chen Tang; if phlegm rises and attacks the upper without corresponding headaches, use Gua Di San to expel it.[47p]
Phlegm and Fluid

Thick and turbid substances are phlegm, while clear and thin ones are fluids. In discussing phlegm diseases, six or seven out of ten cases arise, and the "Inner Canon" describes four categories of phlegm and fluid, all due to the harm caused by damp earth. Thus, the sages say: the spleen is the source of phlegm, and also state: treating phlegm without addressing the spleen and stomach is not proper treatment. When fluids enter the stomach, they flow out nourishing energy, which ascends to the spleen. The spleen's energy disperses this essence, which returns to the lungs, regulating the water pathways and then descending to the bladder. The essence of water distributes evenly, and the five meridians function seamlessly; how can there be phlegm? Only when the spleen's earth is deficient and damp, does the clear fail to rise and the turbid fail to descend, becoming trapped and stagnant, thus forming phlegm.
