Moreover, if one is affected by cold winds, vomiting can disperse it; if injury is caused by food and drink, vomiting can clear it; if there is stagnation due to heat, vomiting can release it; if the heat evil is severe, vomiting can mobilize the yang energy; if various evils are descending, vomiting has the function of rising; if evils are accumulating, vomiting has the power to dissolve them. Furthermore, all diseases in humans are fundamentally due to an obstruction in the flow of vital energy. Vomiting can facilitate the movement of this energy; when energy flows, nothing remains unaddressed, and thus there are no diseases. Therefore, for any strange and hard-to-treat illness, when physicians exhaust all their skills without success, they must employ the method of vomiting to reveal miraculous results, which is something not well-known to people.

Additionally, as for the concept of generating energy, not only do people not understand it, but they may also outright disbelieve it. I, through personal practice and experience, have begun to perceive its subtlety. The workings of heaven and earth, which never cease, fundamentally revolve around the rise and fall of two forms of energy. Rising is rooted in yang, the way of growth; descending is rooted in yin, the way of decline. My use of energy is based on this rising and uplifting principle. It can be quick or slow, naturally incorporating the life force; without harm or violence, it encompasses the miraculous effects of non-medicinal means. Therefore, after vomiting, the spirit and energy are bound to be enhanced, as you have observed. The path of yang must surely flourish; this is what I usually verify. If it were not for vomiting being able to generate energy, could it be so? Taoists use the Governing Vessel, while I employ the Conception Vessel; the methods used are different, but they lead to the same outcome. This not only counters illness but also extends life.[101p]
I say this is not erroneous, you should fully understand it! Those who follow this instruction and practice it regularly will find it effective, though it may not reach the divine subtlety of the late Emperor. Since the time of Xuanchi, only you, Zi He, have adeptly employed the method of expelling. Comparatively, if one were to measure with the Emperor's techniques, the differences in difficulty and efficacy are like the contrast between heaven and earth. The one said to be unparalleled since ancient times certainly cannot be Zi He. If the wise see the same, they will certainly follow in your footsteps, and those to come should not be few. However, I fear that in a hundred generations, this heart and the marvelous way may fade, which is why I have detailed and recorded these teachings, providing a complete account of the method below:

The late Emperor's method of expelling was practiced at the time of the fifth watch, when waking from sleep, lying on one's back, using belching to guide the breath. If the breath is insufficient, one swallows to belch, lifting the breath as one swallows, and phlegm will inevitably follow the breath. Even the deepest phlegm can be expelled, but the last to exit may have an appearance, color, and odor that is exceedingly vile and cannot be put into words. Therefore, after expelling, one may find their lips swollen and throat sore, but this can be relieved with a few sips of cool water. After expulsion, one should avoid all five flavors for breakfast, only consuming one or two bowls of plain porridge to nourish the clear energies within the stomach. After a period of forty days, one should absolutely avoid alcohol. Those who practiced this expelling method for over forty years, thus growing stronger with age, lived to their eighties and could still climb mountains and transcribe ancient books under the lamp. Later, without illness, one suddenly smiled and began fasting, reaching the age of eighty-two.[102p]
The Root of Treating Phlegm

Excess phlegm in a person arises from a deficiency in the internal system. Phlegm is essentially water, with its foundation in the kidneys and its manifestation in the spleen. In the kidneys, it is due to water not returning to its origin, causing it to become phlegm. In the spleen, it occurs when food and drink are not transformed, as the earth does not control the water. Observing robust individuals who indulge in excess drinking and eating, one finds that their consumption is swiftly transformed, and they do not manifest phlegm. It is only those who cannot eat that tend to produce phlegm, because their spleen is deficient and cannot metabolize food, and thus food becomes phlegm. Therefore, in cases of deficiency and exhaustion, there is bound to be an increase in phlegm, and in critical illnesses, phlegm becomes even more severe, primarily because the spleen's energy becomes increasingly deficient, resulting in an inability to transform it, leading all liquids to turn into phlegm. Thus, is the relationship between disease and phlegm such that disease comes from phlegm or phlegm from disease? Is it not clear that phlegm must arise from deficiency? It can be seen that there are very few cases of actual phlegm, and similarly few opportunities to address phlegm. Therefore, in treating phlegm, one must warm the spleen and strengthen the kidneys to address the root of phlegm, ensuring that the foundation gradually becomes more robust, leading to the natural resolution of phlegm without needing treatment.[103p]
On Phlegm and the Meridians

I have often heard it said in common discourse: phlegm pervades the whole body, causing ailments that are hard to diagnose. Conditions such as paralysis, stroke, and hemiplegia are all due to phlegm stagnating. If this is the case, then phlegm is indeed an evil influence; if phlegm is not eliminated, how can the illness possibly recover? I say: do you know the origin of phlegm?

The phlegm in the meridians arises from the transformation of bodily fluids and blood. When the Wei and Ying energies are harmonized, the fluids flow properly and blood circulates freely, then what phlegm could exist? It is only when the original Yang is depleted and the Spirit's mechanism is exhausted that the water becomes devoid of vitality, leading to thickened fluids and deteriorated blood, which then transforms into phlegm. This is indeed phlegm, it is truly essence and blood. How can there be a notion of phlegm separate from essence and blood?

If one asserts that phlegm resides in the meridians and cannot be expelled without attacking it directly, then one must also eliminate essence and blood alongside it, which might be acceptable. Otherwise, how can one solely target phlegm while essence and blood remain untouched? If the bodily fluids and blood are further harmed, the original vital energy will become increasingly depleted, and anything removed will lead to further transformation of phlegm; thus, those who treat phlegm cannot fully succeed, and what they do manage to expel is merely the original energy.

Moreover, there are cases where phlegm is nonexistent at the root, yet misguided efforts identify something as phlegm, leading to mistaken treatment—how profoundly ignorant this is! Therefore, any use of phlegm remedies such as rolling phlegm pills or wind-searching and qi-regulating pills must ensure that the original energy remains unharmed, and only in situations of occasional stagnation or slight unclarity of phlegm can these remedies be temporarily employed; it cannot be said that they are ineffective. If the original energy is affected and one only knows to address the symptoms, there has never been an instance where daily treatment did not lead to daily decline.[104p]
On Non-Wind Phlegm Syndrome

When treating phlegm, if it is not a case of initial wind disease and the phlegm qi is not severe, one must not hastily assume it is phlegm and recklessly use phlegm-dispelling medicines; this is a great caution. If phlegm and saliva are obstructively excessive, filling the chest and diaphragm to the point that neither soup nor liquid can enter, then one must first open the phlegm to clear the pathway for medicines and food. The most effective method to open phlegm is through vomiting, as in the ancient formulas like Du Sheng San, Cha Diao San, and Xi Yan San, all of which are remedies for inducing vomiting. However, there is concern that if the vital energy is greatly deficient, it may not withstand such harsh treatments; thus, it would be more prudent to use new vomiting methods or utilize medicines like Niu Huang Wan or Bao Long Wan, ensuring that the throat and qi are unobstructed enough to allow for ingestion of soup and drink. One must not entirely attack the phlegm to the point of jeopardizing health, which requires utmost caution. Therefore, the method of treating phlegm must also assess whether it can be attacked or not before proceeding; this will avoid errors. If the eyes are glaring and the teeth are clenched, the limbs are rigid, and the face is flushed strong and vigorous, even if there is a clouded mind, it is still treatable. First, use a coarse utensil to pry open the mouth, then with a solid writing rod, keep the jaws steady, and slowly administer a light ginger and salt soup. Next, insert two fingers into the throat, slowly guiding them to induce vomiting. If the fingers cannot reach, a goose feather dipped in soup can substitute for probing to induce vomiting.[105p]
After several attempts, if one can expel the phlegm and feel relief, one is bound to gradually awaken, and then it is appropriate to consider administering medicine. This is the method for treating phlegm obstruction. However, if the signs of death are already present and there is a gurgling sound of phlegm in the throat, expelling it will be of no benefit and there is no need to do so. If the phlegm and qi are exceedingly strong and cannot be expelled, it is also a sign that no treatment is required. Additionally, for those whose constitution is severely weak, one should avoid means of expulsion, as they should not be attacked in this manner. If the physical symptoms are established but the phlegm and qi are not severe, one should absolutely not treat the phlegm. Instead, one should focus on regulating qi and blood to achieve gradual recovery. If phlegm and fluids are not yet cleared, the treatment for phlegm should distinguish between deficiency and excess. If qi is not significantly deficient, and phlegm is produced from either cold or heat, one should use Liu'an Decoction or Erchen Decoction. If fire is the cause of phlegm, Qingge Drink, Bamboo Juice, or children's urine should be used. With severe fire, the Chouxin Drink is appropriate. For those with spleen deficiency and a tendency to vomit with excessive phlegm, Liu Junzi Decoction or Wumei Yigong Powder should be considered. If there is insufficient yin energy, with abundant phlegm and dryness accompanied by thirst, Jinshui Liu Jun Decoction is recommended. For yin deficiency leading to water overflowing as phlegm, one can take Liuwei Wan or Bawei Wan in appropriate doses, or prepare them as soups. If phlegm is produced due to the spleen and kidneys being deficient, cold, and unable to transform, one need not treat both phlegm and qi, but should rather focus on warming and strengthening the roots. If there is a deficiency of middle qi, Lichong Decoction or Wengwei Drink is suitable. For those with insufficient yin, the treatment should prioritize decoctions for nourishing yin.[106p]
Secret Formula of the Stone Chamber - Chen Tuduo (Qing Dynasty)

Phlegm Disease

The treatment of phlegm involves the obstruction of phlegm between the throat and the windpipe. Although it seems trivial, it can lead to serious health issues, which is why the ancients established a separate approach for its treatment. However, the methods created focus only on the symptoms of phlegm and do not address its root cause. Therefore, the Erchen Decoction was established to treat both recent and chronic illnesses, yet it proves ineffective. I now propose three formulations: one for newly occurring phlegm, one for phlegm in existing illnesses, and one for phlegm in long-standing conditions. Although phlegm diseases are numerous, they do not transcend our scope of treatment. For early onset, the symptoms of wind-cold, cough, and phlegm are present. Use equal parts of Banxia, Chenpi, Tianhuafen, Fuling, Gancao, and Suzi, each weighing ten grams, and decoct in water for consumption. After two doses, the phlegm will dissipate; this formula eliminates phlegm from the upper jiao. The phlegm in the upper jiao originates from the stomach rather than the lungs. By removing the phlegm from the stomach, the lung's metal energy is restored, preventing any rise of fire. For phlegm in existing diseases, it resides in the middle jiao, and one must observe its color, distinguishing between white and yellow distinctly. Yellow indicates the fire has begun to recede, while white shows the fire is still rampant.[107p]
For excessive heat, it is appropriate to use cool and cold substances; when the heat is receding, it is advisable to add herbs that dispel it. I now prescribe a formula that can treat both conditions: three qian of white atractylodes, three qian of white mustard seed, five qian of polyporus, one qian each of dried tangerine peel and licorice, one qian of gardenia for phlegm, and five fen of bitter orange, to be decocted in water and taken. This formula is a remedy to strengthen the spleen, not specifically for dispelling phlegm. However, the accumulation of phlegm is often due to dampness in the spleen. By strengthening the spleen, the dampness will descend, and if the dampness does not remain in the spleen, where will it rise from? Moreover, with the addition of a remarkable remedy for dispelling phlegm, can the phlegm remain restless and persist? As for phlegm from prolonged illness, one must not equate it with phlegm due to spleen dampness. Prolonged illness invariably leads to depletion of kidney water; if the kidney water does not rise to become phlegm, then the fire in the kidney boiling can also manifest as phlegm. Thus, for phlegm from chronic illness, one should tonify the kidneys to dispel it. The formula includes five qian each of cooked rehmannia, coix seed, and foxnut, three qian each of cornelian cherry, ophiopogon, polyporus, and Chinese yam, one qian each of northern five-flavor fruit and plantago seeds, and three fen of alpinia galanga, decocted in water and taken. This remedy is particularly effective for phlegm caused by kidney water rising. If the phlegm is due to boiling fire, add one qian of cinnamon.[108p]
This formula is remarkable for its ability to nourish the kidneys while also eliminating dampness and transforming phlegm. When water enters the kidney palace, it is transformed into true essence; how can it rise and become phlegm? This is a method for treating phlegm in the lower jiao. With these three formulas, we can adjust the dosage according to the symptoms and manage phlegm without further issues.

Moreover, there are two other formulas for treating longstanding phlegm that has become chronic. The formula includes Chaihu and licorice, each one qian; Baijiezi and Yiyiren, each five qian; Fuling and Baishao, each three qian; Chenpi three fen; Danpi two qian; and Tianhuafen eight fen, to be prepared as a decoction. This formula is special because it uses Baijiezi as the sovereign, with Yiyiren and Baishao as ministers, and Chaihu and Huafen as assistants, ensuring that the chronic phlegm has nowhere to hide and is gradually digested. This formula can be taken in eight doses, and it eliminates all chronic phlegm, named Xiaozhuo San.

Another formula is for stubborn phlegm. If it forms lumps and obstructs the throat, it is called stubborn phlegm; if it remains in the chest and does not transform, it is called chronic phlegm. The formula includes Ziwanyuan two qian; Banxia, Beimu, Fuling, Jiegeng, Baizhu, and Shenchu, each three qian; as well as BaiFan and licorice, each one qian, to be prepared as a decoction.[109p]
This prescription is remarkable for using both Fritillaria and Pinellia together; one is dry and the other moist, preventing phlegm from hiding anywhere. Additionally, with the use of white alum to dissolve lumps, and Platycodon and Aster to eliminate邪, Licorice harmonizes the center. Is there anything that will not work like this?

For those suffering from phlegm diseases that do not heal after a long time, take a pig's lung, five qian of radish seeds, and one tael of white mustard seeds, all ground into a powder. Mix them well and steam in a rice pot until cooked. Eating one portion after a meal will cure you. This method treats phlegm in the upper jiao, especially when decoctions are ineffective, and it is indeed miraculous. It clears out the phlegm that has long resided in the lungs, making it an excellent treatment.

For middle phlegm, the prescription includes three qian each of Ginseng, Atractylodes, and Poria, one qian each of Aconite and Tian Nanxing, and two qian of Pinellia; boil in water to take as a decoction. It will cure immediately upon reaching the throat. Phlegm arises due to the deficiency of qi, and qi deficiency arises from the coldness of the organs. Thus, in the prescription, Ginseng and Atractylodes are used to replenish the vital qi, while Pinellia, Tian Nanxing, and Poria are used to expel phlegm, and Aconite warms the center, which leads to quieting the phlegm sound and clearing the phlegm qi.

If the phlegm enters the upper jiao, causing stagnant lumps that neither rise nor fall, blocking the chest, resulting in shortness of breath, the urge to vomit without success, or the inability to cough it up, the method should then employ Yin Yang water to induce vomiting.[110p]
One may use the juice of melon seeds or the herb lungs of wild goose to induce vomiting, but this should only be done if one has phlegm and qi stuck in the chest causing pain. Otherwise, it is absolutely forbidden. The vital energy of a person cannot be harmed; vomiting even once will lead to a cycle of disturbance in the five organs and will definitely shorten life. Therefore, one must first inquire whether the person has chest pain, whether there is a blockage in the qi, whether there is an obstruction in the throat, and whether the phlegm that is expelled is yellow. Only when these conditions are present should one consider using the aforementioned remedy to induce vomiting.

Vomiting should not be taken lightly. If one is unaware of the contraindications and rashly induces vomiting, it will definitely disturb the five organs. One must observe whether the expelled phlegm has a shiny appearance against the wall, akin to the shine of snail saliva, which indicates that it is safe to vomit. All else should be avoided. However, if it is shiny, it does not matter whether the phlegm is located in the upper, middle, or lower parts. This shiny color must wait until the phlegm is dried and identified clearly; it cannot be assumed to be shiny just because it is wet.

When there is both central qi and phlegm, though different in nature, they are essentially both rooted in the deficiency of qi. When qi is deficient, phlegm is naturally abundant; when phlegm is abundant, it inevitably consumes qi, thus they are divided yet fundamentally connected.[111p]
Take one tael of ginseng, three qian each of pinellia, poria, and south bitter herb, one qian each of aconite and licorice, and decoct in water to be taken. This will remedy the symptoms of central qi and phlegm. Ginseng is originally a divine agent for the qi, and it is also a marvelous medicine for resolving phlegm. Pinellia and south bitter herb, while being superior in expelling phlegm, also support the righteous qi. Aconite and licorice, one nourishing and one courageous, assist each other to become formidable allies. Used among these three flavors, strengthening the righteous will certainly remove the evil, and resolving phlegm will inevitably benefit the qi. There is a division and combination without an apparent form, an extraordinary uniqueness and marvelous transformation that must not be overlooked.

The treatment of qi is important, as there are many qi disorders; I will discuss the major ones, such as qi counterflow and phlegm obstruction. The obstruction of phlegm is not due to phlegm itself but to the stagnation of qi. If one only addresses phlegm without benefiting the qi, I have not seen phlegm dissipate and the illness alleviate. The formula includes two qian of white atractylodes, three qian of poria, and one qian each of ginseng, aged tangerine peel, trichosanthes root, white mustard seed, szechuan pepper, and perilla seed, along with three lumps of cardamom, decocted in water to be taken. The brilliance of this formula lies in treating phlegm while first regulating the qi. When the qi is smooth, the phlegm becomes active; when the qi flows freely, the moisture circulates, and phlegm will not even arise. This is the appropriate approach to treating qi, and one can immediately gain insight into methods for addressing stagnant qi through a single formula.[112p]
For the condition of qi deficiency with excessive phlegm, the phlegm is fundamentally due to dampness. In treating phlegm, one must not merely eliminate the dampness but should first supplement qi, and then assist with phlegm-resolving ingredients. The formula consists of three qian each of ginseng, pinellia, and poria, five qian of coix, one qian each of shenqu, dried tangerine peel, and licorice, all decocted in water. Although this formula includes pinellia and dried tangerine peel to resolve phlegm, without sufficient ginseng, the phlegm will not dissipate; ginseng aids qi, and ingredients like coix and poria can strengthen the spleen to eliminate dampness. Once the dampness is removed, phlegm will naturally resolve; this is a method for treating qi deficiency.

For cases of qi deficiency with cold phlegm, simply add three qian of cinnamon and half a qian of dried ginger to the previous formula. For cases of qi deficiency with heat phlegm, one should not use the previous formulation but instead employ three qian each of lianhua, white peony, and angelica; one qian each of tianhuafen, licorice, dried tangerine peel, and white mustard seed; and two qian of poria, along with three fen of shenqu, all decocted in water. The efficacy of this formulation lies in its ability to avoid excessive dryness while also supplementing qi; it moistens and transforms phlegm, so when phlegm is expelled, qi will naturally become sufficient as well. With these two formulations, treating qi deficiency will be no challenge.[113p]
If there is a rise of kidney water leading to excessive phlegm, one should use the Six-Flavor Decoction with the additions of aconite and cinnamon, prepared as a decoction and consumed in several bowls for recovery. In cases of deficiency of kidney water and kidney fire, even if there are signs of heat in the upper jiao, the tongue remains slippery and not dry, unlike the dryness associated with the extreme heat in yang conditions.

Fat individuals tend to have phlegm, which results from qi deficiency; when qi is deficient, it cannot move, causing phlegm to accumulate. Therefore, treating phlegm must also involve tonifying qi while simultaneously eliminating the phlegm. However, when tonifying qi, one must not solely focus on strengthening the spleen and stomach; it should also include augmenting the fire of the Mingmen (Gate of Vitality). Fire generates earth, and earth produces qi; when qi is ample, phlegm will naturally dissipate. Not treating phlegm directly is part of treating phlegm.

The prescription includes three taels each of ginseng, eucommia bark, and white mustard seed; five taels each of white atractylodes, coix seed, and fox nut; eight taels of cooked rehmannia; four taels of shan yue; two taels each of cinnamon and poria; five qian of cardamom; and one tael each of Alpinia fruit and dried tangerine peel, all ground into powder and mixed with honey to form pills, taken with five qian of boiling water each day.

The effectiveness of this formula lies in cinnamon, which tonifies the fire of the Mingmen and heart protector. When the fire in the heart protector is sufficient, it can stimulate appetite and eliminate phlegm; when the fire of the Mingmen is strong, it can invigorate the spleen and eliminate dampness. Moreover, the ingredients in this formula are primarily tonifying to the heart and kidneys, and cinnamon among these tonifying herbs promotes harmony between heaven and earth. With the water returning to the channels, where would phlegm accumulate? This is the method for treating fat individuals.[114p]

Phlegm Door

Formulas

Ling Gui Zhu Gan Decoction (by Zhong Jing, same below)
For treating phlegm and fluid obstruction beneath the heart, fullness in the chest and flanks, and dizziness.

  • Fu Ling: 4 taels
  • Gui Zhi: 3 taels
  • Bai Zhu: 3 taels
  • Gan Cao: 2 taels
    Combine these four ingredients with 6 sheng of water, boil to obtain 3 sheng, and divide into three warm doses. It promotes urination.

Ten Jujube Decoction
For treating suspended fluid.

  • Yuan Hua, Ao, Gan Sui, Da Ji: equal parts
    Grind and sift these three ingredients, then add 1 sheng 5 he of water. First boil 10 large jujubes, reduce to 8 he, remove dregs, and mix in the powdered medicine. For strong individuals, take 1 qian per dose; for frail individuals, take half a qian, and consume warm at dawn. If not effective, increase the dose by half a qian the next day. After achieving results, nourish with congee.

Xiao Qing Long Decoction
For treating overflow of fluid.

  • Ma Huang (without stems), Shao Yao, Gan Cao (roasted), Gan Jiang, Gui Zhi (peeled), Xi Xin: each 3 taels
  • Ban Xia (washed) and Wu Wei Zi: half sheng each
    Combine these eight ingredients with 10 dou of water. First, boil Ma Huang, reduce by 2 sheng, remove the foam, then add the other herbs, boil to obtain 3 sheng, strain, and consume 1 sheng warm.[115p]
    Mufangji Plus Fuling Mangxiao Decoction: Treats edema.
    Mufangji and Guizhi, each 120 grams; Ginseng, Mangxiao, 90 grams; Fuling, 240 grams. Take these five ingredients, boil with six liters of water until two liters remain. Strain, add Mangxiao, lightly reboil, and take warm in divided doses. If there is slight relief, then you will recover.

Fangji Jiumu Tingli Dahuang Pill: Treats abdominal fullness and dryness of the mouth and tongue, as there is water vapor in the intestines.
Fangji, Jiumu, Tingli, Dahuang, each 30 grams. Grind these four ingredients into a powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a walnut. Take one pill before meals, three times a day, and gradually increase. If there is saliva in the mouth, for thirsty patients, add 15 grams of Mangxiao.

Wuling Powder: For thin individuals experiencing palpitations below the navel, excessive salivation, and dizziness; this indicates water retention. This formula addresses it.
Ze xie, 1.5 grams; Zhu ling, Fuling, Bai zhu, each 1.5 grams; Guizhi, peeled, 0.75 grams. Grind these five ingredients into a powder, take a teaspoon with warm white drink three times a day, and drink plenty of warm water to promote sweating and recovery.

Wai Tai Fuling Decoction: Treats phlegm and stagnant water in the chest; after expelling water, if there is still a feeling of emptiness in the chest and fullness preventing eating, this will resolve phlegm and qi, allowing one to eat.
Fuling, Ginseng, Bai zhu, each 180 grams; Orange peel, 120 grams; Zhi shi, 120 grams; Fresh ginger, 240 grams. Boil these six ingredients with six liters of water until one liter and eight taels remain. Take in warm doses three times a day, as if walking eight to nine miles.[116p]
Gui Ling Wu Wei Gan Cao Decoction treats the rush of phlegm in drinkers.
Cassia twig, peeled, and Poria fungus, each four taels; honey-fried licorice three taels; five-flavor fruit half sheng. Combine these four ingredients with eight sheng of water, boil down to three sheng, strain, and divide into three warm doses.

Ling Gan Wu Wei Ginger and Acrid Decoction treats cough and fullness in drinkers.
White Poria fungus four taels; licorice, dried ginger, and fine bitter cress each three taels; five-flavor fruit half sheng. Combine these five ingredients with eight sheng of water, boil down to three sheng, strain, and take half sheng warm, three times a day.

Ling Gan Wu Wei with Ginger, Acrid, Half Summer, and Apricot Kernel Decoction treats water retention with nausea and body swelling.
Poria fungus four taels; licorice, dried ginger, and fine bitter cress each three taels; peeled apricot kernels, half summer, and five-flavor fruit each half sheng. Combine these seven ingredients with one dou of water, boil down to three sheng, strain, and take half sheng warm, three times a day.

Ling Gan Wu Wei with Ginger, Acrid, Half Apricot, and Rhubarb Decoction treats water retention with stomach heat, causing heat in the face akin to intoxication.
Poria fungus four taels; licorice, dried ginger, fine bitter cress, and rhubarb each three taels; five-flavor fruit, half summer, and apricot kernels each half sheng. Combine these eight ingredients with one dou of water, boil down to three sheng, strain, and take half sheng warm, three times a day.[117p]
Water-boiled Golden Flower Pill: Cleanses ancient impurities, treats all phlegm.

Tian Nan Xing and Ban Xia, each one tael for use in their raw form; Tian Ma, five qian; Xiong Huang, two qian; Bai Mian, three qian. Grind these into fine powder, mix with water to form small pills the size of a mung bean. Take fifty to one hundred pills at a time, boil the herbs in the broth until it floats, strain out, soak in diluted broth, then take with ginger soup. There’s also a method involving one tael of Han Shui Shi, calcined to retain its essence.

Phlegm-Dispersing Decoction (from "Ji Sheng Fang"): Treats excess phlegm and fluid, retained in the chest and diaphragm, causing obstruction and pressure. Ban Xia stirred seven times, four taels; TianNan Xing, roasted and peeled; Zhi Shi, stir-fried with wheat bran; Red Fu Ling, peeled; Ju Hong, each one tael; Gan Cao, roasted, half a tael. Grind these and take four qian each time, boiled with one cup of water and ten slices of ginger, simmer until reduced by a third, then take warm after meals.

Wind-Expelling Phlegm Pill (from "Dan Xi Xin Fa"): Treats wind phlegm. Ren Shen, Jiang Can, Huai Jiao, Bai Fan, Tian Ma, Chen Pi (white part removed), Jing Jie, each one tael; Ban Xia, four taels, soaked in soup; Chen Sha, half a tael. Grind into powder, mix with ginger juice to form pills, using a coating except for Chen Sha. Take forty pills at a time, with ginger soup.

Little Yellow Pill: Treats hot phlegm cough. Wash Tian Nan Xing and Ban Xia with soup, and Huang Qin, each one tael.[118p]
The right ingredient is fine powder; mix it with ginger juice to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take 50 to 70 pills each time, followed by ginger soup, after meals.

White Atractylodes Pills: Treats phlegm and cough due to dampness.
Ingredients: Nanxing and Banxia, each one tael, both washed with soup; one and a half taels of White Atractylodes. The right ingredients are ground into fine powder, mixed with soup to form pills the size of a walnut. Take 50 to 70 pills each time, followed by ginger soup, after meals.

Jade Powder Pills: Treats cough with qi and phlegm.
Ingredients: Nanxing and Banxia, each one tael, both washed with soup; two taels of orange peel, white removed. The right ingredients are ground into fine powder, mixed with soup to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take 50 to 70 pills each time, followed by ginseng and ginger soup, after meals.

Ginger and Cinnamon Pills: Treats cough due to cold phlegm.
Ingredients: Nanxing and Banxia washed; Guankui with coarse skin removed, each one tael. The right ingredients are ground into fine powder and mixed with steamed dough to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take 30 to 50 pills each time, followed by ginger soup, after meals.

Platycodon Decoction: Eliminates phlegm and descends qi; treats fullness in the chest and sides, cold and heat vomiting, hardness below the heart, shortness of breath, restlessness, phlegm reversal causing nausea, and inability to eat.
Ingredients: Platycodon finely shredded and slightly stir-fried, Banxia washed in soup seven times, made with ginger juice; aged tangerine peel with white removed, each ten taels; Zhiqiao stir-fried until reddish-yellow, five taels. The right ingredients are coarsely ground. Each dose is two qian (6 grams), boiled with one medium cup of water, adding five slices of ginger, simmer until reduced to seven parts, then strain. It can be taken warm at any time.[119p]
Xiao Banxia Jia Fuling Decoction [Zhongjing]
For treating phlegm and fluid retention.

  • Banxia: 1 sheng
  • Fuling: 3 liang
  • Fresh ginger: 0.5 jin

Take 5 qian each time, with 1.5 bowls of water, decoct until reduced by 30%, and take at any time.

Chuanxiong Pill [From the Book of Practical Formulas]
For treating phlegm above the diaphragm.

  • Chuanxiong: 2 liang, finely grated, slow-cooked until fully absorbed
  • Dahuang: 2 liang, steamed until dry

Grind these two ingredients into a fine powder, and use 5-7 pieces of non-eaten soapberry, knead with warm water to extract the juice, filter through silk to remove dregs, and cook in a pottery jar until it turns into a paste. Mix with the previous two ingredients to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take 15 pills each time; for children, take 3 pills, using ginger decoction to wash them down.

Xiao Wei Dan
For treating phlegm retention in sturdy individuals.

  • Yuánhuā (Daphne) vinegar mixed and stirred for one night, constantly stirred in an earthenware vessel, roasted until black but not burnt
  • Gānsuì (Sichuan hogweed) adjusted with water, wrapped in flour and cooked, soaked in running water for half a month, boiled and sun-dried
  • Dàjǐ (Euphorbia) boiled in running water for one hour, then washed and sun-dried, both at 0.5 liang
  • Dàhuáng (Rhubarb) wrapped in damp paper and cooked, not burnt, cut and dried, sautéed with wine until cooked, then dried, both at 0.5 liang
  • Huángbò (Phellodendron) sautéed: 3 liang

Grind these into a powder, and mix with Baizhu ointment to form pills the size of a radish seed. Swallow with saliva before bedtime, or wash down with white broth, to eliminate phlegm and heat accumulation above the diaphragm, according to one’s feelings. For a laxative effect, take on an empty stomach. In one version, add 0.5 liang each of Muxiang and Betel nut.[120p]
Da Qinglong Decoction: Treats cold phlegm and water retention.

  • 6 taels of Ephedra, remove the joints
  • 2 taels of Cinnamon twig, remove the bark
  • 2 taels of Licorice, honey-fried
  • 40 pieces of Apricot kernel, remove the skin
  • Gypsum the size of a chicken egg, crushed as fine as rice
  • 3 taels of Fresh ginger, sliced
  • 12 pieces of Jujube, split

Combine these seven ingredients with 9 sheng of water. First, boil the Ephedra and reduce to 2 sheng, skim off the froth, then add the other herbs, decoct to get 3 sheng, strain, and take 1 sheng warm.

Ze Xie Decoction: Treats spleen deficiency with water overflowing as phlegm.

  • 5 taels of Alisma
  • 2 taels of Atractylodes

Use 2 sheng of water, decoct to get 1 sheng, and divide the warm solution to take twice.

Bei Zhu Pills: Treats five types of water retention:

  1. Retained water (liuyin) - water stagnates below the heart;
  2. Accumulated water (poyin) - water on both sides;
  3. Phlegm water (tanyin) - water in the stomach;
  4. Overflowing water (yiyin) - water overflowed in the diaphragm;
  5. Flowing water (liuyin) - water in the intercostal space with a dripping sound.

All caused by excessive drinking or consumption of cold beverages.

  • 2 taels of Atractylodes
  • 1 tael each of Cinnamon heart and Dried ginger.[121p]
    The text describes a medicinal preparation known as "Honey Pills," which are to be taken before meals. The recipe for "Da Wuyin Wan" (Great Five Drink Pills) includes various ingredients such as Polygala, bitter bush, and rhubarb, among others. Each ingredient is measured carefully, and a specific method for preparation is outlined, recommending three pills daily, with a careful avoidance of certain foods, particularly raw and cold items.

Additionally, "Wuyin Decoction" (Five Drink Decoction) is noted for its efficacy in treating the condition related to five drinks, comprising ingredients like Xuanfu flower, ginseng, and others, boiled adequately with specified quantities and consumed warm, with the option to enhance with certain herbs following wine consumption.[122p]
Guan Phlegm Pill (from "Yangseng Zhu Lun")
This treats all phlegm-related diseases.
Steam Dahuang (Rhubarb) briefly, turn it over and steam again for a short while, then take it out. Do not overdo it.
Add eight taels each of Huangqin (Skullcap)
and Qinglongshi (Alchemilla), calcined until golden.
Add five qian each of Chenxiang (Agarwood) and Baiyao (various medicinal herbs) decoction.
Grind these ingredients into a powder, form pills the size of a tung seed, and take with warm water after meals on an empty stomach. This formula is derived from the secrets passed on by the recipe of Baiyao.
This pill, made from these medicines, can gather and contain stubborn phlegm throughout the body, collecting it in one place, and then assist in elimination, exhibiting extraordinary effects. For those suffering from loss of spirit and resolve, whether mania or madness, take one hundred pills each time. If the person has a strong constitution and appetite, and is severely manic, add twenty more pills. Adjust dosage temporarily as needed.

Li Phlegm Pill (from "Yuan Zhu", same source)
This treats phlegm and fluids.
Take two taels each of Naxing (South Star), Zaojiao (Soapberry), Shigao (Gypsum), Qianniúzhǐ (Morning Glory), and Yuanhua (Cynanchum) powder.
Grind these into a fine powder, use ginger juice to form pills the size of a tung seed. Each dose consists of twenty pills, adjusted according to the individual’s condition, taken with ginger soup.
In one variation, add five qian of Qingyan (blue salt) and a small amount of Bodi (Castor bean), as well as five qian of Qingmengshixin (Blue Mungo stone) calcined until golden.
If phlegm and wind are obstructing, this medicine serves as the first remedy; taking it will resolve the phlegm immediately. It is not suitable for cold conditions.[123p]
Phlegm-Dissolving Pill treats all phlegm.

Take six taels of Pinellia, divide into three parts: one part with one tael of fine alum powder, soak in water; one part with one tael of roasted soapberry ground into powder, soak in water; one part with one hundred seeds of Croton tiglium ground into powder, soak in water. The aforementioned items should be placed underneath, with Pinellia on top. Soak for ten days or half a month, stirring the water to ensure the two medicines blend well. Afterward, remove the Croton seeds and soapberry, and simmer the remaining water on low heat until it thickens. Take out the Pinellia, chop and crush it, then sun-dry or shade-dry it, both are fine.

Add:

  • Sweet root processed
  • Two taels of various medicinal decoctions
  • One tael each of whole scorpion and silkworm

Grind the above ingredients into fine powder, form into small pills the size of a nut. Take ten or fifteen pills each time, adjusting according to one’s condition, and swallow with warm water.

Pine Flower Paste treats coughs lasting from two to twenty years and prepares the lungs in September; it addresses phlegm and lung accumulation, alleviating wheezing and coughing.

Equal parts of:

  • Siler root
  • Dried ginger
  • Wild chrysanthemum
  • Swallowwort
  • Goji berries
  • Licorice
  • Atractylodes
  • Polygonatum

Grind into powder, take the Polygonatum root, cook it into a paste, mix with the powdered medicines, and form pills the size of a marble. Chew one pill thoroughly and swallow with cold water. Do not eat dinner before bedtime, and take one pill of the medicine.[124p]
Dingxiang Wutao Pill: Treats deficiency of spleen qi, stagnation in the three burners, inability to disperse water and food, leading to phlegm and fluid build-up, chest congestion, vomiting, nausea, distension and fullness preventing eating. Frequently taking this warms the spleen and regulates qi.

Each piece of Naxing is cut into about ten parts, soaked in water for three days, changing the water daily. Then use two liang of alum, crushed and ground with water added, soak for another three days, wash and dry.

Cut Banxia and others into pieces, each two liang: dry ginger prepared, white atractylodes, ginger, poria, all one liang; cloves must not be exposed to fire; wood incense, dried tangerine peel (white part removed), and young tangerine peel, each half a liang.

The above are ground into a powder. Use one liang of Shenqu and two liang of barley malt, ground into powder and rolled into pills the size of Wu Tong seeds. Take fifty pills, increasing to seventy, at any time, taken with warm cooked water.

Erchen Decoction: Treats phlegm and fluid pathology, whether it be vomiting and nausea, or headache and palpitations, or discomfort in the epigastrium, or ingestion of raw, cold food and excessive alcohol, due to disharmony of spleen and stomach; it is advisable to take this.

Wash Banxia in water seven times. Use five liang of tangerine peel, three liang of white poria, and one and a half liang of roasted licorice.

The above should be chewed, with four qian taken each time, mixed with one cup of water, seven slices of ginger, and one dried plum, decocted to six parts. Drink hot at any time.[125p]
Entering the Spirit and Reviving the Dan
Treats Yang deficiency with phlegm and Qi counterflow.
One tael of nitrum, ground with sulfur into powder, stir-fried in an earthenware container over a mild fire, using a willow stick to stir; do not let the fire be too intense to avoid damaging the potency of the medicine, grinding it very finely, termed "Two Qi Powder."
Five Spirit Butter and clarified water, filter to remove sand and stones, then dry in the sun.
Dried tangerine peel, orange peel, two taels each.
Trade-sourced sulfur, agarwood, benzoin, tian nanxing, and lunarium essence stone, one tael each.

Shenxian Zhua Tan Wan: This medicine treats phlegm accumulation, chest and diaphragm blockage, and is effective in expelling phlegm.

Use the dried pods of soapbark that are free from insect damage; peel and roast them until yellow, and remove the seeds. Use 1.6 taels of this. Grind these ingredients into a fine powder, then add water to make pills the size of a walnut. Take 30 pills each time, gradually increasing to 100 pills, swallowed on an empty stomach with warm wine. Depending on the severity of the illness, lighter cases will recover in 5 to 10 days, while more severe cases may take half a month to a month. Long-term use prevents paralysis.

Sou Yin Wan: This treats the aforementioned conditions.

Take one wood pear, remove the top and core. Mix raw white alum and half summer (Pinellia ternata) in equal parts. Grind these two ingredients into a fine powder, fill the wood pear with it, cover it with the original top, and bind it with hemp thread. Steam it in a rice steamer twice, then mash it up, mixing it with steamed pancake to make pills the size of walnuts. Take 30 to 50 pills each time, at any time, swallowed with ginger soup.

Method for Half Summer Medicinal Recipe
Dissolves fluid and phlegm, strengthens the spleen and regulates qi.
Wash half summer (Pinellia) in water seven times, soak in concentrated rice wash for one night. For each ounce of half summer, use one and a half ounces of white alum, grind finely and dissolve in warm water. Soak the half summer, leaving about two fingers' depth of water, stir frequently, and during winter, place in a warm location to soak for five nights. Take out and dry. Use one money of lead white frost, dissolve in warm water, soak for one night, then take out after seven days. Next, use rice wash, simmer over low heat without boiling, waiting until the rice wash is very hot, then take out and dry. Store in ceramic vessels. Take one or two grains after meals, chew finely, and take with warm ginger soup. Another method is to prepare as before, using one ounce of half summer, a little alum water to soak, and fine vermilion powder, soaking overnight, then dry and roast. According to the previous method, you can also use fresh ginger juice for soaking and roasting.[135p]

  • Chenpi (Dried Tangerine Peel) - a small amount
  • Banxia (Pinellia) - a small amount
  • Fuling (Poria) - a small amount
  • Gancao (Licorice) - a small amount
  • Cangzhu (Atractylodes) - a small amount
  • Jianghuang (Turmeric) - a small amount
  • Zhihua (Bitter Orange) roasted - a small amount
    Simmer these with 2 cups of water, 5 slices of ginger, and 2 jujubes until reduced to 8 portions, take away from meals.

Three Immortal Pills [from "Bai Yi Xuan Fang"]
For treating all kinds of damp phlegm and fluid retention, chest fullness, obstruction of phlegm, and confusion of the head and eyes.
Ingredients:

  • Naxing (Arisaema) processed - 5 qian
  • Banxia (Pinellia) processed - 5 qian
  • Xiangfu (Cyperus) processed - 5 qian
    Use Naxing and Banxia soaked beforehand to make a powder, mix with fresh ginger juice to a firm consistency, wrap in paper or leaves, and package again to ferment, turning yellow, then sun-dry and store. This should be prepared in May or June.
    For each batch, use 2 taels of Naxing, 2 taels of Banxia, and 1 tael of Xiangfu, grind into a fine powder, and form pills the size of mung beans. Take 40 pills after meals with ginger soup.[143p]
    Shen Zhu Wan Scholar - For treating phlegm and fluid retention.
    Cang Zhu from Maoshan, one pound; raw Hemp oil, half tael; water, two cups. Grind to extract the paste. Fifteen large dates, cooked soft and removed from the pits. Combine the three ingredients into balls the size of a wutong seed, dry in the sun. Take seventy pills each time with warm wine on an empty stomach.

Xing Ban Wan (Dan Xi, same below) - For treating damp phlegm.
Nan Xing and Ban Xia, each prepared, one tael; gecko, three taels. Grind them to a fine powder. Soak in ginger soup and steam into pills, coated with qing dai (blue indigo). Take fifty pills each time, swallowed with ginger soup.

Er Zhu Wan - For treating damp phlegm.
Bai Zhu, six qian; stir-fried Cang Zhu, three qian; stir-fried Shao Yao, two and a half qian; Xiang Fu, half qian. Grind these into a fine powder, steam into pills.

Xiao Huang Wan (Dong Yuan, same below) - For transforming phlegm and saliva, eliminating dampness, regulating stomach qi, and benefiting the diaphragm.
Huang Qin, one and a half tael; Ban Xia and Bai Zhu, each two and a half; Gan Jiang, five qian; Ze Xie, three qian; Huang Qi, two qian. Grind into a fine powder, steam into pills the size of a mung bean. Take fifty pills each time with warm wine.

Run Xia Wan - For treating phlegm in the diaphragm, effectively descending qi.

Wafun (Caoshe) Lou Pill [Secret Recipe]
Treats all stubborn phlegm blockages, difficult to cough up, prolonged cough without cessation, qi blockage causing discomfort, phlegm-fire cough, and is effective in all cases.
Walongzi, also known as Huanzi, is fired, calcinated twice, and ground into a very fine powder. During the time when (Caoshe) Lou frost turns yellow and ripe, the pulp and seeds are taken, mixed with the powdered Walong, and pounded into cakes. Remove the white from dried Chenpi in equal parts.
After careful preparation, dry and turn into powder; then soak in broth for steaming into pills the size of mung beans. Take eighty pills after meals or before bed, washed down with ginger soup.

Bamboo Juice Pill Recipe
Clears phlegm and reduces fire, transforms phlegm and clears the diaphragm, stops coughing and vomiting, stimulates appetite, and treats labor cough.
Remove the white from Chenpi, roasted Bai Zhu, Bai Fu Ling, honey-fried Gan Cao, Bai Mu Er, Ban Xia Qu, Zhi Ke, fried Shen Qu, and Jie Geng, each three taels; Yuan Ming Powder and processed Xiang Fu Zi, each one tael.
The above are coarsely ground. In a large ceramic basin, use one bowl of bamboo juice, half a cup of ginger juice wine, mix well with all the herbs, and dry in the sun at noon. Repeat mixing with bamboo juice and ginger juice for drying seven times, then grind finely. Form into pills the size of mung beans. After meals or when resting, wash down eighty pills with white soup. Effects can be seen after three days, and for those with prolonged illness, it takes seven days to take effect, while the fatigued can recover in a month. This recipe was obtained from a Taoist from the sea and is not publicly shared; I obtained it to treat phlegm-fire, and it has proven effective.[145p]
Flowing Gold Ointment Experience Formula
For treating all phlegm, cough, and related symptoms.
Jin Dahuang (Golden Rhubarb), ground without iron implements to the size of beans, soaked in wine for half a day, then nine times steamed and dried. Gypsum, lightly calcined and ground, both at two taels. Huangqin (Scutellaria), washed in wine, Chenpi (dried tangerine peel), each at half a tael. Lianqiao (Forsythia), washed in wine, and the following herbs: Jiegeng (Platycodon), Chuanxiong (Ligusticum), and Bei Mu (Fritillaria), each at one tael. Danxing (Bitter Orange), mint leaves, and Xiangfuzi (Cyperus), each at half a tael.
These ingredients should be finely processed into a very fine powder, then refined into pills the size of marble balls. Take one in the afternoon or before lying down, chew it finely. Avoid wine and all damp-heat foods.

Huangqin Erchen Decoction
For treating hot phlegm.
Huangqin, Chenpi, Banxia (Pinellia), and Fuling (Poria), each at one qian. Licorice at five fen.
Combine these with half a cup of water, and three slices of ginger, decoct until two-thirds remains. Take it far from meals; adjustments can be made according to symptoms.

Qingge Daotan Decoction
For treating stomach fire from rich flavors, hot phlegm above the diaphragm, difficulty expelling phlegm that is thick and sticky when coughing.
Hua Fen (flower pollen), Lou Ren (Trichosanthes), Baizhu (Atractylodes), and Baifuling (white Poria), each at eight fen. Gypsum and nitrate, each at one qian and a half. Huangqin and Bei Mu, each at one qian. Jiegeng, Chenpi, and Licorice, each at five fen.
Add two cups of water, twenty bamboo leaves, wash and mash them well, and decoct until two-thirds remains. Take it far from meals.[146p]
Lao Tan Pill

Clears dryness and alleviates stagnation, lowers heat and resolves phlegm. It treats chronic phlegm that has thickened into clumps, stagnating in the throat, obstructing the clarity of lung qi, leading to difficulty in expectoration, often caused by fiery evils rising and blocking the heart and lungs. It is advisable to alleviate stagnation, lower heat, and resolve phlegm.

Ingredients:

  • Tianmen Dong
  • Huangqin, stir-fried in wine
  • Hai Fen, ground separately
  • (Caoshe) Lou Ren, ground separately
  • Ju Hong, white parts removed, each one liang
  • Mang Xiao, ground, two qian
  • Lianqiao
  • Jiegeng
  • Xiangfuzi, soaked in light salt water and stir-fried, each half liang
  • Qingshi, ground separately, one qian

The above ingredients are ground into a fine powder. Then, mix with a little honey and ginger juice, and shape into pills the size of longan. Chew one pill with clear soup and swallow slowly; alternatively, shape pills the size of mung beans and swallow five to sixty pills with light ginger soup.

Such chronic phlegm is often found in individuals who drink alcohol frequently. The vapors from alcohol rise, causing fire evil to affect both the lungs and stomach, leading to accumulation and phlegm formation. This prescription includes Tianmen Dong and Huangqin to drain lung heat, Hai Fen and Mang Xiao to soften hardness, (Caoshe) Lou to moisten the lungs and resolve phlegm, Xiangfu and Lianqiao to alleviate stagnation and lower heat, and Qingshi to clear stagnation fire, which is why there are no acrid or drying ingredients used.[147p]

Treats heat and phlegm in the upper abdomen.
Ingredients: Raw Huangqin and toasted Huangqin, each 1 tael; Banxia, Nanzheng, Huanglian, and Zhike (stir-fried), each 2 qian; Bai Fuling, Chenpi, each 2 qian; Zexie 1/2 tael; Baizhu 1 qian.
Grind these into a fine powder, mix with water to form pills the size of a willow seed. Take 50 pills each time, before meals, with warm water.

Xingfeng Decoction [from "Good Formulas"] - Treats phlegm-induced syncope.

  • Grind into a fine powder; mix with ginger juice to form pills the size of Wutong seeds. Take thirty pills after meals with ginger soup. If wind is dominant, take with Bohe soup.

Clove Poria Decoction (Yang's Method)

Treats spleen and stomach deficiency-cold, stagnant fluids, obstruction, and failure of Qi to rise or descend, leading to vomiting of saliva or sour fluid, and a lack of appetite.

  • Ban Xia (Pinellia) processed, Chen Pi (Aged Tangerine Peel), and Fu Ling (Poria), each 1.5 ounces.
  • Ding Xiang (Clove), Fu Zi (Aconite) processed, Rou Gui (Cinnamon), and Sha Ren (Amomum), each 0.5 ounce.

    New Banxia Decoction: Treats weakness of the spleen and stomach, phlegm and fluid stagnation, nausea with sour water, fullness in the chest and sides, dizziness and nausea, loss of appetite. Ingredients: Sand ginger, fried shenqu, dried tangerine peel, and grass fruit, each half a tael; white cardamom and cloves, each two qian; banxia two taels; licorice one tael. Grind to a fine powder. Ingredients: Wood fragrance five qian; sand ginger, peony, sandalwood, poria, cinnamon, and patchouli leaves, each one qian; dried tangerine peel, dried kudzu, high ginger, cloves, and roasted licorice, each two qian. Warming Middle and Resolving Phlegm Pills treat phlegm retention and dampness, chest fullness, dizziness, nausea, and cough with phlegm. Ingredients include: tangerine peel, green tangerine peel, ginger, and dried ginger, each 120 grams. These are ground into a fine powder, mixed with vinegar, and made into pills the size of a phoenix seed. The dosage is 30 pills taken with warm rice drink on an empty stomach.

Shun Yuan Powder treats qi deficiency in the middle, phlegm obstruction, and cold-induced faintness that prevents sleep. Ingredients include: prepared tian nan xing (arisaema), 30 grams; prepared chuān wū tóu (aconite) and fu zi (prepared aconite), each 15 grams; and 12.5 grams of mu xiang (costus) powder. The dosage is 30 grams, cooked with one cup of water and ten slices of ginger, simmered down to seven parts, and taken warm.

Ling Sha Dan treats excessive conditions above and deficiency below with phlegm and mucus obstruction. This medicine is particularly capable of settling, regulating yin and yang, pacifying the five organs, and supporting vital energy. Ingredients include: one pound of mercury and four ounces of sulfur. The sulfur is melted in a new iron ladle, then mercury is added and roasted into granules. This is placed in a tightly sealed jar that is secured with salt mud and red stone resin, fixed with three nails in the ground, surrounded by bricks, and heated with both gentle and strong fire for one day until the jar is bright red. After cooling, it is removed to yield Ling Sha, which is ground into a very fine powder, and formed into pills the size of hemp seeds. The dosage is 20 grains taken with warm rice drink on an empty stomach. This Ling Sha is the same granulation obtained from the mouth of the furnace used to refine vermillion.[152p]

Here is the translated text:

This is a fine powder. Each dose is one or two qian, mixed with juice for drinking. For side pain, add whole scorpions; for headaches, mix with turmeric.

Tea Powder, also known as Mysterious Immortal Powder, treats the above symptoms.
Two qian of melon seeds, one qian of good tea.
This is a powder; each dose is two qian, mixed with juice for drinking.

Thin Saliva Powder treats the above symptoms.
Roasted pig's tooth soap, peeled and string removed, one tael; five qian of lixum. This is a fine powder, each dose is five fen or one to two qian, mixed with water for ingestion. For those with locked jaws, administer by mouth.

Three Saints Powder treats the above symptoms.
Ground melon seeds are lightly roasted and ground into powder; strain and roast again. One tael of Fangfeng and three qian of lixum, remove the buds and heart. This is a coarse powder; each dose is about half a tael, mixed with three tea cups of juice, first boiling one cup for three to four times, removing the juice, then adding the second cup, boiling to three times. Bring the original two cups together, simmer two to three times, remove the dregs and clarify, let it cool, and drink slowly; there is no need to finish the entire dose, use vomiting as a gauge.

Turmeric Powder treats the above symptoms; this is a light dosage.
Half a tael each of turmeric, talcum, and Chuanxiong.
This is a fine powder; each dose is one or two qian, mixed with empty stomach juice for drinking.

Indigo Powder treats the above symptoms.
One piece of pig's tooth soap; one piece of Yanhusuo; and a small amount of indigo.
This is a fine powder, to be blown into the nose so that saliva will flow naturally.[155p]
Sheng Jin Wan (Victory Gold Pill): For treating pre-existing symptoms. Ingredients: 250 grams of mint, 250 grams of gourd seeds, 30 grams of processed rhei, 30 grams of soapwort root, 15 grams of mercurial red.

Preparation: Roast the soapwort, remove the skin and string, crush it, then mix with one liter of water and mint to extract the juice, reducing it to a paste. Grind the rhei and other components into a fine powder, mix with the paste into pills the size of longan fruits, coating with the remaining mercurial red. Take one pill dissolved in warm wine, expelling as needed. If vomiting brings insight into personal matters, recovery ensues. Otherwise, there is no remedy.

Kong Xian Dan (Controlling Phlegm Pill): For sudden chest, back, hands, feet, neck, waist, and buttock pains that are unbearable, with pulling and stabbing pain in muscles and bones, and instability of movement, due to phlegm in the heart and diaphragm.

Ingredients: Equal portions of Gan Sui (Ground Euphorbia), Da Ji (Large-leafed Euphorbia), real white mustard seeds.

Preparation: Grind into a powder, form into pills the size of a Chinese parasol seed, and take 5 to 10 pills with light ginger soup or warm water just before sleeping. Increase dosage if phlegm is severe.

San Hua Shen You Wan (Three Flower Divine Guard Pill from Hejian): Treats all diseases caused by phlegm and fluid disorders.

Ingredients: 15 grams of yanhua, 15 grams of Da Ji, 15 grams of Gan Sui, 60 grams of black chòu (using only the heads), 30 grams of rhubarb, 1 gram of light powder.

Preparation: Grind into a fine powder, form into small pills the size of adzuki beans. Start with five pills, increasing by five with each dose taken with warm water, three times daily, as needed for relief. If experiencing severe fullness, start with a smaller dose of two to three pills, then gradually increase. If relief is achieved, cease further dosage.[156p]

Wuban Wan [From "Yilin"]
Used to treat stubborn phlegm obstructing the chest and diaphragm for a long time, leading to phlegm-qi accumulation. Symptoms include a pale, swollen face, lack of appetite, widespread pain, inability to sleep at night due to obstructed qi, alternating chills and fevers, cold and painful hands and feet, and difficulty turning over. Despite repeated use of Nànxīng, Bànxià, Hēixī, and Língshā, the phlegm does not descend and cannot be expelled. This indicates hardened and stagnant phlegm; hence, this medicine is appropriate. If it effectively clears the stubborn phlegm like fish brains, recovery will follow; if not successful, take it again.
Two taels of Wu Mei flesh, five pieces of Ba Dou, oil removed.
Use two bowls of water, boil the Wu Mei flesh in a sand pan until soft, allow the water to reduce slightly, add the Ba Dou, and stir with a bamboo stick until it becomes a thick paste. Take it out, pound it well, and form into pills the size of walnuts. Take seven, nine, ten, eleven, or fifteen pills each time, taken with ginger soup, at any time.
