在脾经者，名曰湿痰，脉缓面黄，肢体沉重。嗜卧不收，腹胀食滞，其痰滑而易出，二陈汤、白朮丸。挟虚者六君子汤，伤酒者白蔻、干葛，挟食者保和丸，挟暑者消暑丸，惊者妙应丸。在肺经者名片燥痰，又名气痰，脉涩面白，气上喘促，洒淅寒热，悲愁不乐，其痰濇而难出，利金汤、润肺饮。在肝经者名曰风痰，脉弦面青，四肢满闷，便溺秘濇，时有躁怒，其痰青而多泡，水煮金花丸、防风丸、川芎丸。在心经者名曰热痰，脉洪面赤，烦热心痛，口干唇燥，时多喜笑，其痰坚而成块，小黄丸、天黄汤。[49p]

In the spleen channel, this is called damp phlegm; the pulse is slow and the face is yellow, with heavy limbs. One has a desire to sleep but cannot be refreshed, abdominal distention and food stagnation occur, and the phlegm is slippery and easily expelled. Prescription: Er Chen Tang, Bai Zhu Wan. If accompanied by deficiency, use Liu Jun Zi Tang; if caused by alcohol injury, use Bai Dou Kou and Gan Ge; if associated with food, use Bao He Wan; if associated with summer heat, use Xiao Shu Wan; if related to fright, use Miao Ying Wan.

In the lung channel, this is called dry phlegm, also known as qi phlegm; the pulse is thin and the face is pale, with breathlessness and difficulty inhaling, alternating chills and fever, feelings of sorrow and unhappiness; the phlegm is thick and difficult to expel. Prescription: Li Jin Tang, Run Fei Yin.

In the liver channel, this is called wind phlegm; the pulse is wiry and the face is blue, with fullness and heaviness in the limbs, secretive and difficult urination, and occasional irritability. The phlegm is bluish and bubbly. Prescription: Shui Zhu Jin Hua Wan, Fang Feng Wan, Chuan Xiong Wan.

In the heart channel, this is called heat phlegm; the pulse is surging and the face is red, with feelings of annoyance, heat, and heart pain, dry mouth and chapped lips, often showing signs of laughter. The phlegm is hard and formed into lumps. Prescription: Xiao Huang Wan, Tian Huang Tang.[49p]

在肾经者名曰寒痰，脉沉面黑，小便急痛，足寒而逆，心多恐怖，其痰有黑点而多稀，姜桂丸、八味丸、胡椒理中丸。其人素盛今瘦，水走肠间辘辘有声，名曰痰饮，心下冷极，以温药和之，桂苓甘朮汤主之。饮后水流在胁下，咳唾引痛，名曰悬饮，十枣汤下之。饮水流于四肢，当汗不汗，身体疼重，名曰溢饮，大青龙汤汗之。咳逆倚息，短气不得卧，其形如肿，名曰支饮，五苓散、泽泻汤利之。膈满呕吐，喘咳寒热，腰背痛，目泪出，其人振振恶寒，身瞤惕者，名曰伏饮，倍朮丸。[50p]

In the kidney channel, it is called cold phlegm. The pulse is deep, the face is dark, and there is urgency and pain in urination, with cold feet and reversed flow. The heart is filled with fear, and the phlegm is thin with black spots. Treat with ginger and cinnamon pill, eight treasures pill, or pepper remedy. This person was once robust but is now thin; water runs in the intestines making a rumbling sound, known as phlegm-fluid, with extreme coldness below the heart. Warm herbs are used to harmonize it, and the Gui Ling Gan Zhu soup is the main remedy. If water flows beneath the ribs after drinking, with coughing and painful sputum, it is called suspended fluid, to be treated with the Ten Jujube soup. If water flows to the limbs, with a sensation of sweat not being released and a heavy pain in the body, it is called overflow fluid, to be treated with the Major Qinglong soup. If there is reversed coughing while resting, shortness of breath making it hard to lie down, and the body appears swollen, it is called support fluid, treated with the Wuling powder or Ze Xie soup. If there is fullness in the diaphragm with vomiting, wheezing, coughing, chills and fever, back pain, watery eyes, and the person shivers with cold, feeling tense, it is called lurking fluid, treated with the double Atractylodes pill.[50p]

更有一种非痰非饮，时吐白沫，不甚稠粘，此脾虚不能约束津液，故涎沫自出，宜用六君子汤加益智仁以摄之。嗟乎！五痰五饮，证各不同，治法迥别，稍或不详，妄投药剂，非徒无益，而又害之。至如脾肺二家之痰，尤不可混。脾为湿土，喜温燥而恶寒润，故二朮、星、夏为要药；肺为燥金，喜凉润而恶温燥，故二母、二冬、地黄、桔梗为要药。二者易治，鲜不危困。世俗恶半夏之燥，喜贝母之润，一见有痰，便用贝母。若是脾痰，则土气益伤，饮食忽减；即使肺痰，毋过于凉润，以伤中州，稍用脾药以生肺金，方为善治。故曰，治痰不理脾胃，非其治也。[51p]

There is also a type that is neither phlegm nor fluid, which sometimes produces white foam that is not very thick or sticky. This is due to the spleen being weak and unable to control the fluids, leading to the spontaneous production of saliva and foam. It is advisable to use the Six Gentlemen Decoction with the addition of Galangal seeds to restrain it. Alas! The five types of phlegm and five types of fluids are all different, and their treatments are entirely distinct. If one does not understand this clearly and recklessly administers medications, it is not only ineffective but may also cause harm. Particularly, the phlegm from the spleen and lungs must not be mixed. The spleen is associated with damp earth, favoring warmth and dryness while disliking coldness and moisture, thus the two Atractylodes (zhuzhu) and Poria are essential medicines. The lung, being associated with dry metal, prefers coolness and moisture while disliking warmth and dryness, so the two Mothers (Ophiopogon) and the herbs of the two winters, Rehmannia, and Platycodon are key medicines. The treatment for them is relatively easy and rarely leads to complications. In common practice, people dislike the drying effect of Pinellia and prefer the moistening effect of Fritillaria, immediately using Fritillaria upon seeing phlegm. However, if it is spleen phlegm, the earth aspect is further damaged, and food intake suddenly declines; even if it is lung phlegm, one should not use too much cooling moisture as it could hurt the middle qi. One should slightly employ spleen herbs to nourish lung metal for effective treatment. Thus, it is said that treating phlegm without addressing the spleen and stomach is not the correct approach.[51p]

　　　　医贯 【明　赵献可】

　　　　　痰论

　　王节斋云：痰之本，水也，原于肾。痰之动，湿也，主于脾。古人用二陈汤为治痰通用，然以治湿痰寒痰则是矣。若夫阴火炎上，熏于上焦，肺气被郁，故其津液之随气而升者，凝结而成痰，腥秽稠浊，甚则有带血而出者，此非中焦脾胃湿痰寒痰之所比，亦非半夏、枳壳、南星之所治，惟用清气化痰，须有效耳。噫！节斋论痰，而首揭痰之本于肾，可谓发前人所未发，惜乎启其端而未竟其说，其所制之方，皆治标之药，而其中寒凉之品甚多，多致损胃。[52p]

Discussion on Phlegm

Wang Jiezhai says: The origin of phlegm is water, stemming from the kidneys. The movement of phlegm is due to dampness, which is under the control of the spleen. In ancient times, the Er Chen Decoction was commonly used to treat phlegm, specifically for damp phlegm and cold phlegm. However, when the yin fire rises and affects the upper burner, obstructing the lung qi, the fluids that rise with the qi condense into phlegm, which becomes thick, foul, and in severe cases, can even be blood-streaked. This is not comparable to the damp phlegm and cold phlegm of the middle burner, nor can it be treated with Banxia, Zhike, or Nansheng. Only by using clear qi to transform phlegm can there be effective results. Alas! Jiezhai discusses phlegm, and initially identifies its fundamental source in the kidneys, which can be considered an insight not previously uncovered. Unfortunately, while he touches upon the topic, he does not complete the discussion. The remedies he proposes are primarily for symptomatic treatment, and among them, there are many cooling substances that often cause harm to the stomach.[52p]

惟仲景先生云：气虚有痰，用肾气丸补而逐之。吴茭山《诸证辨疑》又云：八味丸治痰之本也。此二公者真开后学之聋瞶，济无穷之夭枉。盖痰者病名也，原非人身之所有，非水泛为痰，则水沸为痰，但当分有火无水之异耳。肾虚不能制水，则水不归源，如水逆行，洪水泛滥而为痰，是无火者也，故用八味丸以补肾火。阴虚火动，则水沸腾，动于肾者，犹龙火之出于海，龙兴而水附；动于肝者，犹雷火之出于地，疾风暴雨，水随波涌而为痰，是有火者也，故用六味丸以配火。
此不治痰之标，而治痰之本者也。然有火无火之痰，何以辨之？曰：无火者，纯是清水；有火者，中有重浊白沫为别耳。善用者，若能于肾虚者，先以六味、八味，壮水之主，益火之原，复以四君子或六君子补脾以制水；于脾虚者既补中理中，又能以六味八味制水以益母，子母互相生克，而于治痰之道，其庶几矣。[53p]

Zhongjing said: When there is deficient qi with phlegm, use Shenqi pill to tonify and expel it. Wu Jiaoshan in "Differentiating Various Conditions" also stated: The Eight-Treasure pill addresses the root of phlegm. These two scholars truly enlighten later learners who suffer silently, alleviating countless ailments. Phlegm is a term for illness and is not an inherent part of the human body; it is not simply water turned into phlegm nor water boiling into phlegm; rather, it must differentiate between the presence of fire and the absence of water.

When kidney deficiency cannot control water, it fails to return to its source, leading to water flowing backward, and a flood-like situation results in phlegm—this is the absence of fire. Hence, the Eight-Treasure pill is used to tonify kidney fire. When yin is deficient and fire is active, water boils over; if it is moving in the kidneys, it is like dragon fire emerging from the sea—where the dragon rises, water follows; if it is stirring in the liver, it is akin to thunderfire erupting from the earth, causing strong winds and torrential rains; water surges and turns into phlegm—this is phlegm with fire. Thus, the Six-Treasure pill is utilized to complement the fire.

This does not target the symptoms of phlegm but addresses its root cause. However, how can one differentiate between phlegm with and without fire? It is said: Without fire, it is simply clear water; with fire, it contains heavy and turbid white froth. Those who are good at using these methods can first apply the Six-Treasure and Eight-Treasure pills to strengthen the source of water and benefit the original fire; then they can use the Four Gentlemen or Six Gentlemen formulas to tonify the spleen to control water.

For spleen deficiency, not only is the middle strengthened, but the Six-Treasure and Eight-Treasure pills can also control water and nourish the mother. The mutual generation and overcoming between mother and child suggest that we can approach the treatment of phlegm effectively.[53p]

　　庞安常有言：有阴水不足，阴火上升，肺受火侮，不得清肃下行，由是津液凝浊，生痰不生血者，此当以润剂，如门冬、地黄、枸杞之属滋其阴，使上逆之火得返其宅而息焉，则痰自清矣。投以二陈，立见其殆。有肾虚不能纳气归原，原出而不纳则积，积而不散则痰生焉，八味丸主之。　　《蒙筌》谓：地黄泥膈生痰，为痰门禁药，以姜汁炒之。嗟乎！若以姜汁炒之，则变为辛燥，地黄无用矣。盖地黄正取其濡润之品，能入肾经。若杂于脾胃药中，土恶湿，安得不泥膈生痰？八味、六味丸中诸品，皆少阴经的药，群队相引，直入下焦，名曰水泛为痰之圣药，空腹服之，压以美膳，不留胃中，此仲景制方立法之妙，何必固疑。[54p]

Pang An often said: When there is insufficient yin fluid and the fire of yin rises, the lungs suffer from the heat and cannot properly descend and clear. Consequently, the fluids become thickened and turbid, resulting in phlegm without producing blood. One should use moistening agents, such as Ophiopogon, Rehmannia, and Goji berries, to nourish the yin, allowing the rising fire to return to its dwelling and rest, thereby clearing the phlegm on its own. If two treasures are applied, one will quickly see its effectiveness.

In cases of kidney deficiency unable to gather qi, the qi flows out without being retained, leading to accumulation; if this accumulation does not disperse, phlegm will arise, and the Eight Herb Pill addresses this. The "Mengquan" states: Rehmannia mud can create phlegm, making it a restricted medicine, which should be stir-fried with ginger juice. Alas! If stir-fried with ginger juice, it becomes spicy and dry, rendering the Rehmannia ineffective. Rehmannia is primarily valued for its moistening properties and its ability to enter the kidney channel. If mixed with spleen and stomach medicines, which dislike dampness, how can it not create phlegm? The various ingredients in the Eight Herb and Six Herb Pills are all medicines of the lesser yin channel, working together to directly reach the lower jiao; hence they are known as the sacred medicine for phlegm generated by water. It should be taken on an empty stomach, followed by a nutritious meal, without lingering in the stomach. This is the wonderful principle of formulations established by Zhang Zhongjing, so why must we remain doubtful?[54p]

古今图书集成医部全录卷二百三十九

痰门

　　　　医门法律 【清　喻昌】

　　　　　痰饮论

　　痰饮为患，十人居其七八，《金匮》论文最详，分别而各立其名。后世以其名之多也，徒徇其末而忘其本，曾不思圣人立法，皆从一源而出，无多岐也。盖胃为水谷之海，五脏六腑之大源，饮入于胃，游溢精气，上输于脾，脾气散精，上归于肺，通调水道，下输膀胱，水精四布，五经并行，以为常人。《金匮》即从水精不四布，五经不并行之处，以言其患。谓人身所贵者，水也。天一生水，乃至充周流灌，无处不到，一有瘀蓄，即如江河回薄之处，秽莝丛积，水道日隘，横流旁溢，自所不免。必顺其性因其势而疏导之，由高山而平川，由平川而江海，庶得免乎泛滥。[55p]

On Phlegm and Fluid Disorders

Phlegm and fluid disorders are a major concern, affecting seven or eight people out of every ten. The "Jin Kui" texts elaborate on this matter in great detail, categorizing and naming the different types. Later generations, overwhelmed by the multitude of names, often lose sight of their fundamental essence, failing to consider that the sages established laws from a single source without divergence.

The stomach serves as the sea for food and water, and is the main source for the five organs and six bowels. Sustenance enters the stomach, where it nourishes and energizes the body, ascending to the spleen. The spleen then disseminates the energy and returns it to the lungs, regulating the pathways of water before ultimately descending to the bladder. The essence of water disperses throughout the body, and the five meridians operate harmoniously, which is the norm for healthy individuals. The "Jin Kui" speaks of the disorders arising when the essence of water does not disperse properly, and the five meridians do not operate in unison.

Water is the most precious element in the human body. Heaven gives rise to water, which circulates everywhere without exception. If there is stagnation, it is like the low-lying parts of rivers where refuse accumulates, the waterways become narrow, and overflow occurs, which cannot be avoided. One must follow the natural tendencies and guide the flow, from high mountains to plains, and from plains to oceans, in order to avoid flooding.[55p]

所以仲景分别浅深诲人，因名以求其义焉。浅者在于躯壳之内，脏腑之外，其名有四：曰痰饮，曰悬饮，曰溢饮，曰支饮。痰饮者，水走肠间，沥沥有声；悬饮者，水流胁下，咳唾引痛；溢饮者，水流行于四肢，汗不出而身重；支饮者，咳逆倚息短气，其形如肿。一由胃而下流于肠，一由胃而旁流于胁，一由胃而外出于四肢，一由胃而上入于胸膈。始先不觉，日积月累，水之精华转为混浊，于是遂成痰饮，必先团聚于呼吸大气难到之处，故由肠而胁而四肢，至渐渍于胸膈，其势愈逆。是痰饮之患，未有不从胃起者矣。其深者，由胃上入阳分，渐及于心肺；由胃下入阴分，渐及于脾肝肾。[56p]

Therefore, Zhongjing distinguishes between the shallow and deep to teach people, naming them to seek their meanings. The shallow pertains to within the body but outside the organs, and it has four names: phlegm flu, suspended fluid, overflowing fluid, and constrained fluid. Phlegm flu is when water moves in the intestines, making a dripping sound; suspended fluid is when water flows under the ribs, causing pain when coughing or expectorating; overflowing fluid is when water flows in the limbs, preventing sweating and resulting in a heavy feeling in the body; constrained fluid is when one coughs, has difficulty breathing, and presents a swollen appearance.

One type flows from the stomach down to the intestines, another flows from the stomach out to the sides, another flows out to the limbs, and another ascends from the stomach into the chest and diaphragm. Initially, one does not notice it; as days and months accumulate, the essence of water turns turbid, eventually forming phlegm flu. It first gathers in the places difficult for breath to access, thus flowing from the intestines to the sides and limbs, gradually saturating the chest and diaphragm, with its effects becoming more pronounced. The problem of phlegm flu has invariably originated from the stomach. The deeper issues ascend from the stomach into the Yang regions, gradually affecting the heart and lungs; from the stomach descending into the Yin regions, gradually affecting the spleen, liver, and kidneys.[56p]

故水在心，心下坚筑短气，恶水不欲饮，缘水攻于外，火衰故水益坚，火郁于内，气收故筑动短气，火与水为仇，故恶而不饮也。水在肺，吐涎沫，欲饮水，缘肺主气，行荣卫，布津液，水邪入之，则塞其气道，气凝则液聚，变成涎沫，失其清肃，故引水自救也。水在脾，少气身重，缘脾恶湿，湿胜则气虚而身重也。水在肝，胁下支满，嚏而痛，缘肝与胆为表里，经脉并行于胁，火气冲鼻则嚏，吊胁则痛也。水在肾，心下悸，缘肾水凌心，逼处不安，又非支饮邻国为壑之比矣。夫五脏藏神之地也，积水泛为痰饮，包裹其外，诗有谓波撼岳阳城者，情景最肖，讵非人身之大患乎？然此特随其所在，辨名定位，以期治不乖方耳。[57p]

Thus, when water resides in the heart, it strengthens the spirit below, creating shortness of breath; one does not wish to drink this bad water. When water attacks from the outside, fire diminishes, causing the water to become firmer. When fire is blocked internally, the breath constricts, leading to this shortness of breath. Fire and water are enemies, hence one does not drink it.

When water is in the lungs, it produces spittle and foam, creating a desire to drink water. This is because the lungs govern qi, circulate nourishment, and distribute fluids. When water evil enters, it obstructs the qi pathways, causing the qi to condense and fluids to gather, transforming into spittle and foam, losing its clarity; thus, one resorts to drinking water for relief.

When water is in the spleen, there is a lack of qi, and the body feels heavy, as the spleen dislikes dampness. If dampness prevails, vitality diminishes, and the body feels heavy.

When water is in the liver, there is fullness beneath the ribs, causing sneezing and pain, as the liver is related to the gallbladder, with their meridians running alongside the ribs. When the fire qi surges to the nose, it causes sneezing, and tension in the ribs results in pain.

When water is in the kidneys, there is a palpitation below the heart, as kidney water overwhelms the heart, creating discomfort. It is not merely a pit of neighborly drink.

The five organs are where the spirit resides. When water accumulates, it manifests as phlegm and fluids, enveloping from the outside. The poetry mentions waves shaking the city of Yueyang, which vividly reflects the situation; is this not a major ailment of the human body? However, this merely depends on its location, clarifying the names and positioning, aiming for proper treatment without deviation.[57p]

究竟水所蓄聚之区，皆名留饮，留者留而不去也。留饮去而不尽者名伏饮，伏者伏而不出也。随其痰饮之或留或伏，而用法治之，始为精义。昌试言之。由胃而上胸膈心肺之分者，驱其所留之饮还胃，下从肠出，或上从呕出，其出皆直截痛快，而不至于伏匿，人皆知之。若由胸膈而外出肌肤，其清者或从汗出，其浊者无可出矣，必还返于胸膈，由胸膈还返于胃，乃可入肠而下出，驱之必有伏匿肌肤而不胜驱者。若由胸膈而深藏于背，背为胸之腑，更无出路，尤必还返胸膈，始得趋胃趋肠而顺下。岂但驱之不胜驱，且有挟背间之狂阳壮火，发为痈毒，结如橘囊者。伏饮之艰于下出，易于酿祸，其谁能辨而出之耶？昌以静理而谭医施治，凿凿有据，谨因《金匮》秘典，直授金针，令业医之子，已精而益求其精耳。[58p]

Ultimately, the areas where water accumulates are called "retained drinks," as they remain and do not leave. When retained drinks are present but do not exhaust completely, they are called "hidden drinks," as they hide and do not emerge. Following the various phlegm and drinks that are either retained or hidden, and treating them according to their nature, is the essence of proper method. Let me explain it further.

From the stomach upward through the divisions of the chest, diaphragm, heart, and lungs, one should drive those retained drinks back to the stomach and eliminate them, either through the intestines below or vomiting above. Such expulsions are direct and satisfying, and do not lead to hiding. This is known by all. If the drinks exit through the skin, the clear ones may surface as sweat, while the turbid cannot escape and must inevitably return to the chest and diaphragm. From the chest and diaphragm, they should return to the stomach before they can enter the intestines and be expelled. Driving them out must involve hidden drinks within the skin that resist expulsion.

If they are deeply stored in the back, which serves as a cavity for the chest, there is even less opportunity for escape, and they must return to the chest and diaphragm before they can proceed to the stomach and intestines for proper downward movement. It is not only that they resist expulsion, but there is also the dangerous excessive yang heat implicated, which can lead to sores and poisons that accumulate like an orange pouch.

The difficulty in expelling hidden drinks can easily lead to harm; who can discern and resolve this? I, Chang, apply calm reasoning and speak on medical practice, with firm evidence, carefully based on the secret text of the "Golden Coffer," directly imparting the golden needle technique, urging the heirs of medical practitioners to refine their understanding and further pursue precision in their craft.[58p]

　　　　　痰饮脉论

　　痰饮之脉，《金匮》错出不一，难于会通。以鄙见论之，亦有浅深微甚之不同，可预明也。脉要精微篇曰：肝脉软而散，色泽者，当病溢饮。溢饮者，渴暴多饮，而易入肌皮肠胃之外也。此特举暴饮水溢，饮病之最浅者为言耳。仲景会其意，即以饮证分之为四，统言其纲曰：痰饮、悬饮、溢饮、支饮，大都为由浅及深者商治。失此不治，而至于积水滔天，即此四饮，自有不可同语者矣。其谓饮脉不弦，但苦喘短气者，见饮脉本弦。饮脉不弦则水之积也不厚，然亦害其阳气，微喘短气而已。[59p]

Treatise on the Pulse of Phlegm and Fluid

The pulse of phlegm and fluid, as mentioned in the "Jin Kui," varies inconsistently, making it difficult to interpret comprehensively. In my humble opinion, there are also differences in depth and severity, which can be clarified. The section on important pulse subtleties states: the liver pulse is soft and scattered; in terms of color, it indicates the presence of excessive fluid. Excessive fluid refers to extreme thirst and frequent drinking, which easily enters the muscles, skin, and gastrointestinal tract. This specifically highlights the condition of excessive drinking as the most superficial manifestation of drinking-related illness. Zhang Jing understood this concept and categorized the symptoms of fluid retention into four types, summarizing them as: phlegm fluid, suspended fluid, overflowing fluid, and restrained fluid, generally discussed from shallow to deep in treatment. Failing to address this and allowing it to escalate into a flood of accumulated fluids means that these four types cannot be discussed in the same manner. The pulse of fluid that is not taut, but merely indicates pain and shortness of breath, refers to the true pulse of fluid. If the fluid pulse is not taut, this suggests that the accumulation of water is not significant; however, it still harms the yang energy, leading only to mild shortness of breath.[59p]

其谓支饮亦喘而不能卧，加短气，其脉平者，见支饮上于胸膈喘而短气，其脉仍平，有而若无，才有停积，未至留伏，故不见于脉也。其谓脉浮而细滑者伤饮，见浮而细滑，非伤风伤寒之比，亦饮之初郁气分而未深也。医者于此时，早思昏垫之灾，亟兴己溺之念，而行因势利导之法，患斯解矣。否则证成深锢，末流愈分，伏根之所，愈不可识，经年检方问药，漫图成功，其可得乎？故凡见脉转沉弦一派，即当按法求之。其曰脉沉者，胸中有留饮，短气而渴，四肢历节痛，言肺之治节不行，宗气不布，故短气；气不布则津亦不化，故膈燥而渴；脾气不运，水饮流于肢节，则作痛也。[60p]

It is said that when there is edema, the patient may wheeze and be unable to lie down, experiencing shortness of breath. When the pulse is still steady, and one observes the edema rising to the chest and diaphragm, accompanied by wheezing and shortness of breath, with a pulse that remains steady, it may seem present yet is nearly absent, showing only a slight accumulation, not yet settled deeply, hence not evident in the pulse. It is said that if the pulse is floating, thin, and slippery, it indicates injury from fluid intake; this floating, thin, and slippery pulse is not similar to that from wind-cold, but rather is due to the initial stagnation of fluid, which has not penetrated deeply yet. At this time, the physician should urgently consider the dangers of stagnation and promptly activate the body's own elimination, employing strategies according to the circumstances, which would resolve the issue. Otherwise, if the condition deepens and the final portion of the illness separates more, the root becomes increasingly difficult to diagnose. Year after year, if one merely inspects formulas and seeks remedies without success, can success be achieved? Therefore, whenever one observes the pulse turning deep and string-like, one should apply appropriate methods to investigate. When it is said that the pulse is deep, it indicates the presence of retained fluid in the chest, leading to shortness of breath and thirst. This results in pain in the limbs and joints, indicating that the lung's ability to regulate is not functioning, and the vital energy is not dispersing, hence the shortness of breath; without the dispersal of energy, the fluids do not transform, resulting in dry phlegm and thirst; if the spleen's energy is not moving, the fluid accumulates in the joints, causing pain.[60p]

似此一证，肺脾交病，所称饮入于胃，游溢精气，上输于脾，脾气散精，上输于肺之常者，且转而借寇兵賷盗粮矣，欲求其安，宁可得乎？至论弦脉，则曰咳者其脉弦，为有水；曰双弦者寒也，皆大下后虚；脉偏弦者饮也，为喘满；曰脉弦数有寒饮，冬夏难治；曰脉沉而弦者，悬饮内痛。此即沉潜水蓄，支饮急弦而广其说，除大下后，其脉双弦者，有虚寒之别，其偏弦者，俱为水饮也。冬夏难治，亦因其用寒远寒，用热远热之法，不若春秋为易施耳。悬饮内痛，谓悬饮结积于内，其甚者则痛也。[61p]

This evidence suggests that there is a mutual disease between the lungs and spleen. The so-called fluids entering the stomach and spreading their essence upward to the spleen, dispersing the spleen's energy and ascending to the lungs, is a common occurrence. If one then resorts to hiring soldiers and stealing grain to seek peace, can such tranquility be obtained? Concerning the pulse characteristics: it is said that a cough corresponds to a string-like pulse, indicating the presence of fluids; a double string-like pulse denotes cold, often resulting from a significant depletion after a purge; a pulse that is slightly string-like indicates fluid retention, leading to wheezing and fullness; a rapid string-like pulse indicates cold fluids, which are hard to treat in winter and summer; a deep and string-like pulse suggests hanging fluids causing internal pain. This describes the accumulation of water, addressing the urgent fluid retention and broadening the explanation. Aside from significant purges, a double string-like pulse indicates a difference between deficiency and cold, while a slightly string-like pulse indicates fluid retention. The difficulty in treatment during winter and summer stems from the use of cold methods for cold conditions and hot methods for heat conditions, making spring and autumn far more conducive to treatment. The internal pain from hanging fluids refers to a substantial accumulation of such fluids, leading to pain in severe cases.[61p]

更有沉紧之脉，主心下痞坚，面色黧黑之证，谓水挟肾寒，杂揉于心肺之分，则心下坚而面色黑也。有脉伏而为留饮之证，积饮把持其脉而不露，较濇脉尤甚矣。又曰：脉伏便利，心下绩坚，此为留饮欲去故也。又曰：久咳数岁，其脉弱者可治，实大数者死；其脉虚者必苦冒，本有支饮在胸中故也。凡此皆病深而脉变，当一一溯其流而穷其源者。夫天枢开发，胃和则脉和，今为痰饮凝结其中，则开阖之机关不利，而脉因之转为沉弦、急弦、偏弦、弦数、弦紧，或伏而不见，非亟去其痰饮，亦胡由脉复其常耶？浅者浅治，深者深治，浅深之间者适其中而治。留者可攻，伏者可导，坚者可削。再一因循，病深无气，洒洒时惊，不可救药矣。[62p]

There is also a deep and tight pulse, indicating a firm mass beneath the heart and a dark complexion, signifying water accompanied by kidney cold, mixed in the heart and lungs. This leads to a firm sensation below the heart and a dark complexion. If the pulse is hidden, it is a sign of retained fluids, where accumulated fluids hold the pulse and do not reveal themselves, being even more pronounced than a thin pulse. Moreover, when the pulse is hidden yet smooth, it indicates that the retained fluid wants to disperse. If there has been a persistent cough for several years, a weak pulse can be treated, but a strong and full pulse signifies death; a weak pulse will inevitably suffer from phantasms because there is already retained fluid in the chest. All these indicate that the disease is deep and the pulse has changed, requiring one to trace its flow and investigate its source thoroughly. When the heavenly pivot opens and the stomach is harmonized, the pulse is smooth. However, if phlegm and fluids are condensed within, the mechanisms of opening and closing are not functioning properly, and the pulse transforms into deep, taut, rapid, biased, numerous, or tense forms, or may even be hidden and unseen. Without urgently removing the phlegm and fluids, how can the pulse return to its normal state? Those with shallow conditions can be treated lightly; those with deep conditions require deep treatment, and those between shallow and deep should be treated accordingly. Retained fluids can be attacked, hidden ones can be guided, and firm ones can be dispersed. If one continues to follow past practices, the disease deepens with no energy, leading to sudden distress; at that point, it is beyond the reach of medicine.[62p]

　　　　　痰饮留伏论

　　痰饮之证，留伏二义，最为难明。前论留饮者留而不去，伏饮者即留饮之伏于内者也。留饮有去时，伏饮终不去，留伏之义，已见一斑。而《金匮》奥义，夫岂渺言能尽？谨再陈之。《金匮》论留饮者三，伏饮者一。曰：心下有留饮，其人背寒如掌大。曰：留饮者，胁下痛引缺盆。曰：胸中有留饮，其人短气而渴，四肢历节痛。言胸中留饮，阻抑上焦心肺之阳，而为阴曀，则其深入于背者，有冷无热，并阻督脉上升之阳，而背寒如掌大，无非阳火内郁之象也。[63p]

Discussion on Retained Phlegm and Fluids

The conditions of retained phlegm and fluids have two meanings that are particularly difficult to understand. To discuss retained fluids refers to those that remain and do not disperse, while hidden fluids are those that remain concealed within. Retained fluids can eventually leave, while hidden fluids will never depart; thus, the meanings of retention and concealment begin to become clearer. The profound meaning of the "Golden Coffer" cannot be fully expressed in mere words, and so I will explain it again. In the "Golden Coffer," there are three observations on retained fluids and one on hidden fluids. It states: when there is retained fluid below the heart, the person feels cold in the back, as if the size of a palm. Secondly: retained fluid causes pain in the side and pulls toward the lower abdomen. Thirdly: when there is retained fluid in the chest, the person experiences shortness of breath and thirst, with pain in the joints of the limbs. Speaking of retained fluid in the chest, it obstructs and represses the yang of the upper jiao, namely the heart and lungs, leading to a yin stagnation. Thus, for those with deep cold in the back, there is only cold without heat, which obstructs the upward movement of the governing vessel's yang, resulting in cold in the back like the size of a palm, all of which is merely a manifestation of internal stagnation of the yang fire.[63p]

胁下为手足厥阴上下之脉，而足少阳之脉，则由缺盆过季肋，故胁下引缺盆而痛，为留饮偏阻木火不伸之象。饮留胸中，短气而渴，四肢历节痛，为肺不行气，脾不散精之象也。合三条而观之，心肺肝脾痰饮，皆可留而累之矣，其义不更着耶。至伏饮则曰：膈上病痰，满喘咳吐，发则寒热，背痛腰痛，目泣自出，其人振振身瞤剧，必有伏饮。言胸中乃阳气所治，留饮阻抑其阳，则不能发动，然重阴终难蔽晛，有时阳伸，阴无可容，忽而吐发，其留饮可以出矣。若更伏留不出，乃是三阳之气伸而复屈。[64p]

The channels of the hand-foot Jueyin run below the ribs, and the channel of the foot Shaoyang passes through the diaphragm and the lateral ribs. Therefore, pain in the side is linked to the diaphragm and is a sign of retained phlegm obstructing the movement of wood and fire. When phlegm is retained in the chest, it causes shortness of breath and thirst, while the limbs ache at the joints, indicating a failure of the lungs to circulate qi and of the spleen to disperse essence. When viewed altogether, heart, lungs, liver, spleen, and phlegm are all capable of retention and burdening one another—this meaning does not change.

As for the retained phlegm, it manifests as phlegm in the upper diaphragm, fullness with dyspnea, coughing, and expectoration. It may lead to alternating chills and fever, back pain, waist pain, and tears streaming from the eyes. The afflicted person often shows signs of tremors and severe twitching; there must be retained phlegm present.

The heart and lungs govern the chest, and when phlegm retention obstructs the yang qi, it cannot be mobilized. Nonetheless, heavy yin is ultimately difficult to conceal; sometimes the yang extends, with no accommodation for yin, leading to sudden vomiting or expulsion, allowing the retained phlegm to emerge. If further withholding occurs without expulsion, it indicates that the three yang energies are extending and retracting again.[64p]

太阳不伸，作寒热，腰背痛，目泣；少阳不伸，风火之化，郁而并于阳明土中，阳明主肌肉，遂振振身瞤而剧也。留饮之伏而不去，其为累更大若此。然留饮伏饮，仲景不言治法。昌自其遏抑四脏三腑之阳而求之，则所云宜用温药和之者，岂不切于此证而急以之通其阳乎？所云苓桂朮甘汤者，虽治支满目眩，岂不切于此证而可仿其意乎？故必深知比例，始可与言往法也。[65p]

When the sunlight does not extend, it causes cold and heat, back pain, and tears in the eyes. When the lesser yang does not extend, the transformation of wind and fire becomes constrained and blends within the broad yang of the earth. The broad yang governs the muscles, leading to trembling of the body and intense suffering. If the retained fluids do not disperse, the burden becomes even greater. However, for the treatment of retained fluids, Zhongjing does not mention a method. If one seeks to control the excessive yang of the four organs and three cavities, then using warming herbs to harmonize should address this condition, shouldn’t it? The Decoction of Poria, Cinnamon, Atractylodes, and Licorice is meant to treat fullness in the chest and dizziness; does this not align with the understanding of this condition and can it not be applied accordingly? Therefore, one must thoroughly understand the ratio before one can discuss the therapeutic methods.[65p]

后人不明《金匮》之理，妄生五饮六证之说，即以海藏之明，于五饮汤方下云：一留饮在心下，二支饮在胁下，三痰饮在胃中，四溢饮在膈上，五悬饮在肠间，而统一方以治之，何其浅耶！　　按痰饮总为一证，而因则有二。痰因于火，有热无寒；饮因于湿，有热有寒，即有温泉无寒火之理。人身热郁于内，气血凝滞，蒸其津液，结而为痰，皆火之变现也。水得于湿，留恋不消，积而成饮，究竟饮证热湿酿成者多，寒湿酿成者少。盖湿无定体，春曰风湿，夏曰热湿，秋曰燥湿，冬曰寒湿。三时主热，一时主寒，热湿较寒湿三倍也。《内经》湿土太过，痰饮为病，治以诸热，非指痰饮为寒。后人不解，妄用热药，借为口实。讵知凡治六淫之邪，先从外解。故治湿淫所胜，亦不远热以散其表邪，及攻里自不远于寒矣。[66p]

Later generations do not understand the principles of the "Golden Coffer" and arbitrarily create theories of the five types of fluid accumulation and six signs. They, with a shallow understanding, apply the teachings regarding fluid accumulation, stating: first, heart retention; second, side retention; third, phlegm retention in the stomach; fourth, overflow retention above the diaphragm; fifth, hanging retention in the intestines. They propose a unified treatment for all, how superficial this is!

Note that phlegm retention is fundamentally one condition, but there are two causes. Phlegm arises from fire, characterized by heat without cold; fluid retention, on the other hand, is due to dampness, characterized by both heat and cold, maintaining that there are warm springs without cold fire. When the body is heated and agitated internally, the qi and blood stagnate, causing the essential fluids to steam and congeal into phlegm, an expression of fire.

Water comes from dampness, lingering and unconsumed, accumulating into fluid retention. Ultimately, cases of fluid retention primarily arise from the combination of heat and dampness, with fewer cases resulting from cold and dampness. Dampness lacks a fixed form; in spring it is termed wind-damp, in summer hot-damp, in autumn dry-damp, and in winter cold-damp. Three seasons are dominated by heat, while one season is dominated by cold, with heat-damp conditions occurring three times more frequently than cold-damp.

According to the "Inner Canon," when dampness and earth excessively dominate, phlegm retention can become a disease, treated with various heat remedies, not implying that phlegm retention is cold in nature. Later generations do not understand this and recklessly use heat medications as a pretext. What they fail to realize is that to treat the six external pathogens, one must first resolve external disturbances. Thus, to address the dominance of dampness, it is also necessary to warm the exterior to disperse its pathological influences, and when attacking internally, it will not stray far from cold either.[66p]

况始先即不可表，而积阴阻遏身中之阳，亦必借温热以伸其阳，阴邪乃得速去，若遂指为漫用常行之法，岂不愚哉！　　《小学》有虚实分治之法，谓疾病之生也，皆因外感内伤，生火、生湿、湿热、生痰，四者而已。审其少壮新病，是湿则燥之，是火则泻之，湿而生热则燥湿而兼清热，火而生痰则泻火而兼豁痰，无余蕴矣。审其衰老久病，又当攻补兼施。如气虚而有湿热痰火，则以四君子汤补气而兼燥湿清热豁痰泻火；如血虚而有痰火湿热，则以四物汤补血而兼泻火豁痰清热燥湿。如此则攻补合宜，庶乎可也。[67p]

Moreover, at the beginning, there can be no outward expression, and the accumulation of yin blocks the yang within the body, it is necessary to employ warmth to promote the yang for the yin pathogens to swiftly depart. If one merely relies on common methods blindly, would that not be foolish!

"The Lesser Learning" discusses the method of differentiating between deficiency and excess, stating that the origin of illness is due to external influences and internal damage, leading to the generation of fire, dampness, damp-heat, and phlegm—these are the only four causes.

When assessing recent illnesses in the young, if it is dampness, we should dry it; if it is fire, we should purge it. If dampness generates heat, we should dry the dampness while simultaneously clearing heat. If fire produces phlegm, we should drain the fire while also dispersing the phlegm, ensuring no residue remains.

In examining the elderly or those with chronic illnesses, one should apply both attacking and tonifying methods. For instance, if there is qi deficiency with damp-heat phlegm-fire, one would use the Four Gentlemen Decoction to tonify qi while simultaneously drying dampness, clearing heat, dispersing phlegm, and draining fire; if there is blood deficiency with phlegm-fire damp-heat, one would use the Four-substances Decoction to tonify blood while also draining fire, dispersing phlegm, clearing heat, and drying dampness.

In this way, a combination of attacking and tonifying methods is appropriate and should be feasible.[67p]

故曰：少壮新病，攻邪可审；老衰久病，补益为先。若夫阴虚火动，脾胃衰弱，真阴者水也，脾胃者土也，土虽喜燥，然太热则草木枯槁，木虽喜润，然太润则草木湿烂，是以补脾滋肾之剂，务在燥湿得宜，随证加减焉耳。　　后世治痰饮有四法：曰实脾、燥湿、降火、行气。实脾燥湿，二陈、二朮最为相宜，若阴虚则反忌之矣。降火之法，须分虚实，实用苦寒，虚用甘寒，庶乎可也。若夫行气之药，诸方漫然，全无着落，谨再明之。风寒之邪，从外入内，裹其痰饮，惟用小青龙汤，则分其邪从外出而痰饮从下出也。浊阴之气，从下入上，裹其痰饮，用茯苓厚朴汤，则分其浊气下出而痰饮上出也。[68p]

Thus it is said: In the young and robust, new ailments should be examined by attacking the pathogenic factors; in the old and frail, nourishing and tonifying remedies should take precedence. As for the deficiency of Yin leading to excessive fire, and the weakness of the spleen and stomach, the true Yin is akin to water, while the spleen and stomach correspond to earth. Though earth prefers dryness, excessive heat will cause plants to wither. Likewise, though wood thrives in moisture, too much humidity leads to rot. Therefore, when using remedies to tonify the spleen and nourish the kidneys, it is essential to balance dryness and dampness, adjusting them according to varying conditions.

Later generations treat phlegm and fluid retention with four methods: strengthening the spleen, drying dampness, reducing fire, and promoting Qi circulation. To strengthen the spleen and dry dampness, the formulas of Er Chen and Er Zhur are most suitable, though they should be avoided if there's Yin deficiency. For reducing fire, it is necessary to differentiate between deficiency and excess; bitter-cold herbs are used for excess, while sweet-cold is applied for deficiency.

As for Qi-moving herbs, one must avoid random selection without principle. The cold and wind pathogens invade from the outside and envelop the phlegm and fluids; using Xiao Qing Long Tang can disperse the evil externally while expelling phlegm and fluids downward. The turbid Yang Qi enters from below and entraps the phlegm and fluids; employing Fu Ling Hou Po Tang will allow the turbid Qi to descend and the phlegm and fluids to rise.[68p]

多怒则肝气上逆而血亦随之，气血痰饮，互结成癖，用柴胡鳖甲散以除之。多忧则脾气内郁，而食亦不化，气食痰饮，亦互结成癖，用清痰丸以除之。多欲则肾气上逆，直透膜原，结垒万千，(月真)胀重坠，不可以仰，用桂苓丸引气下趋，痰饮始豁也。　　虚寒痰饮，少壮十中间见一二，老人小儿十中常见四五。若果脾胃虚寒，饮食不思，阴气痞塞，呕吐涎沫者，宜温其中。真阳虚者，更补其下，清上诸药不可用也。　　小儿慢脾风，痰饮阻塞窍隧，星附六君汤以醒之。　　老人肾虚水泛，痰饮上涌，崔氏八味丸以摄之。　　痰在膈上，大满大实，非吐不除，然非定法也。[69p]

Excessive anger causes liver qi to rise, and the blood follows suit; qi and blood, along with phlegm and fluids, intertwine and form obstructions. Use Chai Hu Bie Jia San to expel them. Excessive worry causes spleen qi to become stagnant, leading to poor digestion; qi, food, and phlegm also intermingle and create obstructions. Use Qing Tan Wan to eliminate them. Excessive desire causes kidney qi to rise, penetrating the membranes and creating numerous blockages, resulting in a feeling of heaviness and a tendency to sag; one cannot bear to look up. Use Gui Ling Wan to guide the qi downward, clearing phlegm and fluids.

Cold phlegm and fluids in the body are seen in a few cases among the young but are common in the elderly and children. If there is coldness in the spleen and stomach, loss of appetite, and blockage of yin qi causing vomiting of saliva, warming the interior is advisable. If there is true yang deficiency, one must further nourish the lower body, avoiding clearing medications.

For children with chronic spleen phlegm, phlegm obstructs the passages; use Xing Fu Liu Jun Tang to awaken them.

For the elderly with kidney deficiency leading to water rising and phlegm surging upward, use Cui Shi Ba Wei Wan to stabilize.

If phlegm is lodged in the diaphragm causing fullness and heaviness, it can only be resolved through vomiting; however, it is not a fixed prescription.[69p]

使为定法，人人能用之矣，何必独推子和哉。子和必相其人可吐后，乃吐之。一吐不彻，俟再俟三，缓以开之。据云涌痰之法，自有擒纵卷舒，其非浪用可知。再论《金匮》不言之意以明之。《伤寒论》用汗吐下和温之法矣，至痰饮首当言吐者，仲景反不言之，何耶？其以吐发二字为言者，因喘满而痰饮上溢，从内而自发也。其曰：医吐下之，不愈。亦非以吐下为咎也。其曰：呕家本渴，渴者为欲解。又属望于从吐得解也。胡竟不出可吐一语耶？仲景意中谓痰饮证内多夹冲气眩冒等证，吐之则殆，故不烦辞说，直不以吐立法，开后世之过端，所以为立法之祖也。自子和以吐法擅名，无识者争趋捷径，贻误　　不可胜道，必会仲景意以言吐，然后吐罔不当也。[70p]

To establish a definitive method that everyone can utilize, why insist solely on promoting Zihe? Zihe necessarily considers the individual's condition before inducing vomiting. If one attempt does not suffice, one waits and tries again, easing into it gradually. The method of expelling phlegm through vomiting indeed has its own control and release, so it is clear that it is not used recklessly. Further discussion reveals that the "Shang Han Lun" employs methods of sweating, inducing vomiting, purging, and harmonizing with warming techniques. When it comes to phlegm and fluids, it is essential to address vomiting first; however, Zhang Zhongjing does not mention it. Why is this? The term "vomit" is used because phlegm and fluids rise as a result of internal pressure and overflow from within. If one states that inducing vomiting does not lead to recovery, it does not blame the act of vomiting itself. Moreover, it is said that those prone to vomiting are fundamentally thirsty, and thirst prompts the desire to relieve it, suggesting reliance on vomiting for relief. Why is there no clear mention that one should vomit? Zhang Zhongjing implies that within the evidence of phlegm and fluid syndrome, there are many mixed symptoms of counterflow, dizziness, etc.; inducing vomiting might be risky, hence he does not elaborate on it, refraining from making it a fundamental method to avoid leading future generations astray, thereby establishing himself as the founding father of this methodology. Since Zihe has gained fame by advocating for vomiting, the unknowledgeable rush to take shortcuts, which can lead to errors beyond description; one must truly understand Zhang Zhongjing’s intentions regarding vomiting to avoid inappropriate uses.[70p]

　　　　　痰饮留伏论

　　眩冒昏运不可吐，气高气浅不可吐，积劳未息不可吐，病后新虚不可吐，脉道微弱不可吐，病势险急不可吐，阳虚多汗不可吐，素惯失血不可吐，风雨晦瞑不可吐，冬气闭藏不可吐，多疑少决不可吐，吐后犯戒不可吐。
　　　　　药禁十则

　　阴虚枯燥，妄用二陈。阳虚多汗，妄用青龙。心虚神怯，妄用辛散。肺虚无气，妄用苦泻。肝虚气刺，妄用龙荟。脾虚浮肿，妄用滚痰。胃虚津竭，妄用香燥。脏腑易动，妄行涌泄。本非坚积，妄行峻攻。血气虚羸，妄行针灸。　　律三条
　　凡热痰乘风火上入，目暗耳鸣，多似虚证，误行温补，转锢其痰，永无出路，医之罪也。　　凡痰饮随食并出，不开幽门，徒温其胃，束手无策，迁延误人，医之罪也。　　凡遇肾虚水泛，痰涌气高，喘急之证，不补其下，反清其上，必致气脱而死，医之罪也。[71p]

Discussion on the Retention of Phlegm and Fluid

Dizziness and fainting cannot be treated with vomiting; high and shallow breathing cannot be treated with vomiting; fatigue that has not rested cannot be treated with vomiting; post-illness new frailty cannot be treated with vomiting; weak pulse cannot be treated with vomiting; critical illness cannot be treated with vomiting; excessive sweating due to yang deficiency cannot be treated with vomiting; history of blood loss cannot be treated with vomiting; misty weather and dimness cannot be treated with vomiting; winter's closed and hidden energy cannot be treated with vomiting; excessive doubt and little decisiveness cannot be treated with vomiting; and breaking prohibitions after vomiting cannot be treated with vomiting.

Ten Drug Prohibitions

For yin deficiency and dryness, do not recklessly use Er Chen. For yang deficiency and excessive sweating, do not recklessly use Qing Long. For heart deficiency and timid spirit, do not recklessly use pungent dispersants. For lung deficiency and lack of qi, do not recklessly use bitter purgatives. For liver deficiency with qi stagnation, do not recklessly use Long Huo. For spleen deficiency and swelling, do not recklessly use rolling phlegm. For stomach deficiency and depletion of fluids, do not recklessly use aromatic drying agents. For easily activated organs, do not recklessly use purging. If not a solid accumulation, do not recklessly use harsh attacks. For blood-qi deficiency and weakness, do not recklessly use acupuncture.

Three Regulations

Whenever phlegm heat rises with wind and fire, leading to dim vision and tinnitus, resembling a deficiency pattern, mistakenly applying warming tonics will trap the phlegm, leaving no way out—it is the doctor's fault.

Whenever phlegm and fluids exit along with food, not opening the pylorus but merely warming the stomach, leaving one helpless and delaying treatment, it is the doctor's fault.

Whenever facing symptoms of kidney deficiency with water overabundance, phlegm surging, high qi, and urgent breathing, not reinforcing the lower part but instead clearing the upper part will inevitably lead to qi collapse and death—this is the doctor's fault.[71p]

　　　　　论苓桂朮甘汤

　　痰饮阴象，阻抑其阳，用此阳药，化气以伸其阳，此正法也。兹所主，乃在胸胁支满目眩者，何耶？《灵枢》谓心包之脉，是动则病胸胁支满。然则痰饮积于心包，其病自必若是。目眩者，痰饮阻其胸中之阳，不能布水精于上也。茯苓治痰饮，伐肾邪，渗水道；桂枝通阳气，和荣卫，开经络；白朮治风眩，燥痰水，除胀满；甘草得茯苓，则不资满而反泄满。《本草》亦曰：甘草能下气除烦满，故用之也。
　　　　　论苓桂朮甘汤肾气丸二方

　　《金匮》云：夫短气有微饮，当从小便去之，苓桂朮甘汤主之，肾气丸亦主之。并出二方，其妙义愈益彰着。仲景于短气分呼吸，各出一方，呼气之短，用苓桂朮甘汤以通其阳，阳化气则小便能出矣。吸气之短，用肾气丸以通其阴，肾气通则小便之关门利矣。一言半句，莫非精蕴，其斯以为圣人乎。[72p]

Discussion on Ling Gui Zhu Gan Decoction

Phlegm and fluid, being of a yin nature, obstruct and suppress the yang. Using this yang medicine to transform energy and promote the yang is the correct method. The focus here is on cases of fullness and oppression in the chest and ribs, with accompanying dizziness. The "Lingshu" states that the pulse of the pericardium can cause disease related to fullness in the chest and ribs. Therefore, when phlegm and fluid accumulate in the pericardium, the resulting illness must manifest as such. Dizziness occurs when phlegm and fluid obstruct the yang in the chest, preventing the distribution of water essence upwards. Poria helps to treat phlegm and fluid, eliminate kidney evil, and promote the water pathways; cinnamon twig moves the yang qi, harmonizes the nutritive and defensive energies, and opens the meridians; white atractylodes addresses wind-related dizziness, dries phlegm and fluid, and relieves fullness; licorice, when used with poria, prevents excess fullness and promotes functional alleviation. The "Ben Cao" also states that licorice can descend qi and relieve fullness, which is why it is included.

Discussion on Ling Gui Zhu Gan Decoction and Kidney Qi Pill

The "Jin Kui" states that for shortness of breath with mild fluid accumulation, it should be resolved through urination. Ling Gui Zhu Gan Decoction and Kidney Qi Pill both address this condition. Presenting these two formulas, their profound meanings become all the more evident. In cases of shortness of breath, one formula is used for each aspect: for exhalation that is short, Ling Gui Zhu Gan Decoction is employed to open the yang, allowing qi transformation so urination can occur. For inhalation that is short, Kidney Qi Pill is used to open the yin; with the kidney qi unblocked, the gateway for urination is thereby facilitated. Each word and phrase carries deep essence, revealing the wisdom of the sages.[72p]

　　　　　论大小青龙汤

　　溢饮之证，水饮溢出于表，荣卫尽为之不利，必仿伤寒病荣卫两伤之法，发汗以散其水，而荣卫通，经脉行，则四肢之水亦散矣。究竟大青龙升天而行云雨，小青龙鼓浪而奔沧海，治饮证必以小青龙为第一义也。
　　　　　论十枣汤甘遂半夏汤二方

　　伤寒病，两胁痞满而痛，用十枣汤下。其痰饮杂病，虽非伤寒之比，而悬饮内痛在胁则同。况脉见沉弦，非亟夺其邪，邪必不去，脉必不返，所以用十枣汤不嫌其过峻也。凡病之在胁而当用下者，必仿此为例也。至甘遂甘草汤之治留饮，微妙元通，非深入圣域，莫能制之。《内经》但曰留者攻之耳，仲景于是析义以尽其变。无形之气，热结于胃则用调胃承气攻之，热结于肠则用大小承气攻之。有形之饮，痞结于胸，则用陷胸汤攻之；痞结于胁，则用十枣汤攻之；留结于肠胃之间，则用甘遂半夏汤攻之。[73p]

On Big and Small Qinglong Decoction

In the case of excessive drinking, when water overflows to the surface, the ying and wei are both adversely affected. One must follow the methods used for cold damage that harm both the ying and wei, inducing sweating to disperse the water. When the ying and wei are harmonious and the meridians flow smoothly, the water in the limbs will also dissipate. Ultimately, the Big Qinglong ascends to the heavens, producing clouds and rain, while the Small Qinglong stirs the waves and rushes into the vast sea. Therefore, for the treatment of water retention, the Small Qinglong must be regarded as the foremost principle.

On the Ten Jujube Decoction and Gansui and Banxia Decoction

For cold damage, with fullness and pain in both flanks, Ten Jujube Decoction should be administered. For phlegm and fluid retention illnesses, although they are not directly comparable to cold damage, if the retained water causes pain in the flanks, it is similar. Moreover, if the pulse is deep and tight, the pathogenic factor will not leave unless it is urgently expelled, hence using Ten Jujube Decoction is not considered excessive. Any illness located in the flanks that requires purging should follow this example. As for the Gansui and Gancao Decoction for treating retained fluids, it is subtle and profound; only those deep in the sacred domain can master it. The Neijing only states to attack the retained fluid, and thus Zhong Jing elaborated on its implications to encompass its variations. For intangible pathogenic energy, if heat is concentrated in the stomach, one should use the Adjust Stomach and Purge Decoction to attack it; if heat is concentrated in the intestines, one should use the Big and Small Purge Decoction to attack it. For tangible fluids, if they are collected in the chest, use the Chest Trap Decoction to attack; if they are collected in the flanks, use the Ten Jujube Decoction to attack; if they are retained between the intestines and stomach, use the Gansui and Banxia Decoction to attack.[73p]

法曰，病者脉伏，其人欲自利，利反快，虽利心下续坚满，此为留饮欲去故也，甘遂半夏汤主之。脉道为留饮所隔，伏而不行，其证欲下利，利反快，似乎留饮欲去，然虽欲去不能去也。心下续坚满，可见留饮之末，已及于肠，留饮之根，仍着于胃，不刬其根，饮必不去，故立是方。甘遂甘草大相反者，合而用之，俾其向留着之根，尽力一刬，得留者去而药性已不存矣，正《内经》有故无殒之义也。又加白蜜同煎，留恋其药，不致迸入无过之地。其用半夏、芍药者，由木入土中，成其坚满，半夏益土，芍药伐木，抑何神耶？后世方书，并甘草删去，神奇化为腐朽，制方立论，皆中人以下之事矣，竟何益哉！[74p]

The text states that when a patient has a concealed pulse, they desire self-benefit, but such benefit leads to more discomfort. Even though there is a stubborn fullness in the heart area, this is due to the presence of retained fluids that need to be expelled. The formula "Gansui Banxia Decoction" is indicated for this condition. The pulse is obstructed by the retained fluids, which remain stagnant; thus, even though there is a desire for relief, it cannot be achieved. The persistent fullness in the heart area indicates that the fluids have reached the intestines, while their source is still in the stomach. Unless the root cause is addressed, the retained fluids cannot be eliminated, hence the creation of this formula.

Gansui and licorice are opposites and should be combined to effectively target the root of retention, allowing for their complete expulsion without preserving any medicinal properties. This aligns with the principle from the "Inner Canon" that emphasizes the importance of not discarding necessary elements. Additionally, white honey is added to avoid any adverse reactions. The inclusion of Banxia and Shaoyao is due to their relation to the transformation of wood into earth, solidifying the fullness. Banxia enhances the earth, and Shaoyao counters the wood—what is the underlying principle here? Later texts have often omitted licorice, leading to a decline in their efficacy and turning formulas into mere trivialities. This raises the question of what benefit such changes truly deliver.[74p]

　　　　　论木防己汤葶苈大枣泻肺汤防己椒目葶苈大黄丸三方
　　三方皆治支饮上入膈中，而有浅深次第之分。首一方先治其肺，中一方颛治其肺，后一方兼治肺气所传之腑。盖支饮上入于膈，逼近心肺，粤援肾邪。本文云：其人喘满，心下痞坚，面色黧黑，其脉沉紧，得之数十日，医吐下之，不愈，木防己汤主之。虚者即愈，实者三日复发，复与不愈者，去石膏加茯苓、芒硝。盖以支饮上入，阻其气则逆于肺间而为喘满，阻其血则杂揉心下而为痞坚。肾气上应，其色黑，血凝之色亦黑，故黧黑见于面部。然且姑缓心肾之治，先治其肺，肺之气行，则饮不逆而俱解耳。[75p]

On the Three Formulas: Mufangji Decoction, Denglizhidaozhao Decoction, and Fangji Jiao Mu Denglizhihuang Pill

All three formulas treat fluid accumulation entering the diaphragm, differing in depth and order of treatment. The first formula primarily treats the lung, the second firmly addresses the lung, and the third simultaneously treats the lung qi transmitted to the organs. Fluid accumulation enters the diaphragm, pressing against the heart and lungs, and may cause kidney problems. The text states that the person experiences wheezing and fullness, has a firm sensation below the heart, a dark complexion, and a tight, deep pulse. After several days, if the physician administers vomiting or purging and the patient does not improve, the Mufangji Decoction is indicated. If the condition is due to deficiency, it will improve; if due to excess, it may relapse after three days. For those unhealed, remove gypsum and add Poria and Glauber's salt. This is because fluid accumulation obstructs the qi, leading to wheezing and fullness in the lungs, while obstructing the blood causes a firm sensation below the heart. The kidney qi responds upwards, resulting in a dark complexion; thus, the blood's dark color appears on the face. However, it is important to ease the treatment of the heart and kidneys and prioritize the treatment of the lung. If lung qi is flowing, the fluid does not reverse, and they will both be resolved.[75p]

木防己味辛温，能散留饮结气，又主肺气喘满；石膏辛甘微寒，主心下逆气，清肺定喘；人参甘温，治喘消膈饮，补心肺不足；桂枝辛热，通血脉，开结气，宣导诸药，在气分服之即愈。若饮在血分，深连下焦，必愈而复发，故去石膏气分之药，加芒硝入阴分、开痰结、消血癖，合之茯苓，去心下坚，且伐肾邪也。葶苈大枣汤，大泻其肺气，亦以气停故液聚耳。防己椒目亭苈大黄丸，治腹满口舌干燥，肠间有水气之证，乃肺气膹郁于上，以致水饮不行于下，而燥热之甚，用此丸急通水道，以救金气之膹郁，不治上而治其下，故用丸剂也。[76p]

Mutual infiltration of flavors and temperatures, such as morus wood and toxic herbs, can dissipate residual fluid and resolve qi stagnation, primarily addressing lung-related wheezing and fullness. Gypsum, with its slightly cold, sweet, and pungent properties, governs counterflow of qi in the chest, clears the lungs, and settles wheezing. Ginseng, warming and sweet, is effective for alleviating wheezing, dissolving phlegm, and replenishing the heart and lungs' deficiencies. Cinnamon twig is spicy and warm, promoting blood flow, unblocking qi, and harmonizing various medicines for immediate effect when taken in the qi level.

However, if the fluid is within the blood aspect and deeply connected to the lower energies, recurrence is inevitable. Therefore, it is necessary to remove gypsum, which addresses the qi aspect, and incorporate Glauber's salt to resolve phlegm accumulation and eliminate blood stagnation, combining it with poria to soften hardness below the heart and also tackle kidney evil.

The Da Zao Tang, by forcefully draining lung qi, also treats cases where fluids accumulate due to stagnation. The Fang Ji Jiao Mu Ting Li Da Huang Wan is indicated for abdominal fullness with dry mouth and tongue, as well as the presence of watery qi in the intestines, attributed to lung qi congestion leading to fluid retention below. To urgently open the waterways and relieve the trapped lung qi, this pill is used to approach the lower aspect of treatment, making it a pill form for effectiveness.[76p]

　　　　　论小半夏汤小半夏加茯苓汤外台茯苓饮三方
　　前一方治支饮呕而不渴者，支饮上入膈中，而至于呕，从高而越，其势最便。但呕家本当渴，渴则可征支饮之全去。若不渴，其饮尚留，去之未尽也。不必加治，但用半夏之辛温，生姜之辛散，再引其欲出之势，则所留之邪自尽矣。中一方，亦治卒呕吐者，但多心下痞，膈间有水眩悸，故加茯苓以去水伐肾而安心也。后一方加人参、枳实、橘皮，尤为紧要。治积饮既去，而虚气塞满其中，不能进食，此证最多，《金匮》早附《外台》一方，启诱后人，非天民之先觉而谁？
　　　　　论泽泻汤厚朴大黄汤二方[77p]

On Xiaobanjia Decoction, Xiaobanjia Decocted with Poria, and the Poria Drink from the External Source

The first formula treats phlegm-dampness with vomiting but no thirst. The phlegm dampness rises to the diaphragm, leading to vomiting; its force is most prominent when it ascends. However, if one vomits, thirst is normally expected, and if there is thirst, one can expect the phlegm-dampness to completely disperse. If there is no thirst, then some fluid remains, indicating that it hasn’t been entirely expelled. There is no need for additional treatment; simply using the acrid warmth of Banxia and the acrid dispersing qualities of fresh ginger will help urge out what remains, thus allowing any retained evils to dissipate.

The middle formula also treats sudden vomiting, but with more pronounced heaviness in the abdomen and water retention in the diaphragm causing dizziness and palpitations. Therefore, Poria is added to remove water and tranquilize the heart.

The final formula includes ginseng, bitter orange, and tangerine peel, which is particularly crucial. It treats accumulated fluid that has been dispersed, yet the qi remains trapped and full, preventing the intake of food. This condition is most commonly encountered. The "Jinkui" earlier included the formula from the "External Source" to enlighten later generations. Who, if not the wise awareness of the celestial people, could have foreseen this?

On ZeXie Decoction and Huopo Dahuang Decoction[77p]

　　二方之治支饮，俱从下夺，而有气血之分，前后之辨。首一方为支饮之在心下者，阻其阳气之升降，心气郁极，火动风生而作冒眩。惟是不治其冒眩，但利小便以泄其支饮，则阳自升而风火自息。仲景制方每多若此。后一方治支饮之胸满者。夫支饮而至胸满，在仲景自用大小陷胸汤治之。此方乃承气之法，止可施于伤寒无形气分热结，乃以之治有质之痰饮，非仲景丝丝毕贯之法矣，其为编书者误入何疑。
　　　　　论五苓散方

　　本文云：假令瘦人脐下有悸，吐涎沫而癫眩，此水也，五苓散主之。此寻常一方耳。深维其义，譬如以手指月，当下了然。盖瘦人木火之气本盛，今以水饮之故，下郁于阴中，挟其阴邪，鼓动于脐则为悸，上入于胃则吐涎沫，及其郁极乃发，直上头目为癫为眩。巢氏《病源》云：邪入之阴则癫。夫阳郁于阴，其时不为癫眩，出归阳位，反为癫眩者，夹带阴气而上也。故不治其癫眩，但散其在上夹带之阴邪，则立愈矣。[78p]

The text discusses the treatment of fluid retention (支饮) and associated symptoms as described in classical Chinese medicine. It details two different approaches to address the condition:

The first approach addresses the retention of fluids affecting the heart, which obstructs the upward and downward movements of Yang Qi, leading to symptoms such as dizziness and a feeling of heaviness. If one does not treat the dizziness directly but instead facilitates urination to expel the retained fluids, the Yang Qi can rise properly, and the associated wind and fire symptoms will subside. This is a common method practiced by Zhang Zhongjing.

The second approach pertains to the treatment of chest fullness caused by fluid retention. In this case, Zhang Zhongjing would use a specific formula to address the condition, which involves purging trapped heat and fluid from the body.

The text also references the Wuling San formula, indicating that if a thin person experiences palpitations and produces frothy saliva with dizziness, this is due to water retention and the Wuling San formula is indicated. The underlying principle is that a build-up of fluids in the body due to their inherent Yin qualities can lead to these symptoms, and it is not enough to treat the dizziness directly; one must disperse the accompanying Yin pathogenic factors for a cure. Thus, proper treatment will alleviate the condition.[78p]

散阴邪之法，固当从表，然不如五苓散之表法为良，以五苓散兼利其水耳。今世之用五苓散者，但知其为分利前后水谷之方，不知其为分利表里阴阳之方，方下所云多饮暖水，汗出愈之文，总置不录，何其浅耶！不但此也，即如小青龙一方，世但知为发表之轻剂，全不知为利小水而设。夫山泽小龙，养成头角，乘雷雨而直奔沧海，其不能奋髯而升天，岂待问哉。所以《金匮》治支饮五方，总不出小青龙一方为加减，取其开通水道，千里不留行耳。[79p]

The method for dispersing the Yin pathogen should indeed start from the exterior; however, it is better to follow the method of Wu Ling San, which also benefits the water. Those in the modern world who use Wu Ling San only understand it as a formula to regulate the distribution of food and water, not realizing its significance in balancing the interior and exterior, Yin and Yang. The text mentions drinking warm water and sweating as beneficial but fails to note these essential points, showing a profound lack of understanding! Moreover, regarding Xiao Qing Long Tang, people only recognize it as a light remedy for releasing the exterior and do not realize it is designed to facilitate the small water. The Xiao Long from the mountains and marshes grows its horns and rushes towards the dark sea amidst thunder and rain; it cannot simply ascend to the heavens. Thus, the treatment for cough and thirst in the "Jin Kui" largely draws from Xiao Qing Long Tang for modification, aiming to unblock the waterways, without leaving any path unfollowed.[79p]

　　　　　痰证问答

　　告门人曰：治痰之规则，不见于方书。如在上者，用瓜蒂散、栀豉汤等方；在左者，用龙荟丸；在右者，用滚痰丸；以及虚人用竹沥达痰丸，沉寒锢冷用三建汤之类，全无奥义，岂得心应手之妙，未可传之纸上耶？吾今为子辈传之。盖五味入口而藏于胃，胃为水谷之海，五脏六腑之总司，人之食饮太过，而结为痰涎者，每随脾之健运而渗灌于经隧，其间往返之机，如海潮然，脾气行则潮去，脾气止则潮回，所以治沉锢之法，但取辛热，微动寒凝，已后止而不用，恐痰得热而妄行，为害不浅也。不但痰得热而妄行，即脾得热而亦过动不息，如潮之有去无回，其痰病之决裂，可胜道哉。[80p]

Questions and Answers on Phlegm Disorders

The person was told: The rules for treating phlegm do not appear in the prescription books. For a condition above, one would use formulas like Guati Powder or Zhihua Decoction; for the left side, Longhui Pill; for the right side, Gunphlegm Pill; and for those of weak constitution, Zhu Li Datan Pill. In cases of cold and stagnant conditions, Sanjian Decoction can be used. All these methods lack profound principles; how can one expect to master them readily, and can they be passed down on paper? I will now transmit this knowledge to the younger generation.

The essence is that when the five flavors enter the mouth, they are stored in the stomach, which serves as the sea of food and drink, and the central controller of the five organs and six bowels. When a person consumes too much food and drink, phlegm and saliva are produced. This occurs as phlegm saturates the meridians, following the healthy functioning of the spleen and its ability to circulate. The dynamics of this back and forth resemble the ebb and flow of ocean tides: when the energy of the spleen flows, the tide goes out; when it stops, the tide returns. Therefore, the method for treating stagnation involves taking warming, spicy substances to slightly invigorate and relieve the cold that has condensed. After this, one must stop further intervention, as allowing phlegm to become hot and move recklessly can lead to significant harm.

Not only can phlegm behave erratically when heated, but excessive heat in the spleen can also cause it to become overly active without rest, reminiscent of tides that flow out without returning. The consequences of such phlegm disorders can be grave indeed.[80p]

从来服峻补之药者，深夜亦欲得食，人皆不知其故，反以能食为庆，曾不思爱惜脾气，令其昼运夜息，乃可有常。况人身之痰，既由胃以流于经隧，则经隧之痰，亦必返之于胃，然后可从口而上越，从肠而下达，此惟脾气静息之时，其痰可返。故凡有痰证者，早食午食而外，但宜休养脾气不动，使经隧之痰，得以返之于胃，而从胃之气上下，不从脾之气四迄，乃为善也。试观人痰病轻者，夜间安卧，次早即能呕出泄出，痰病重者，昏迷复醒，不能呕出泄出者，岂非未曾得食，脾气静息，而予痰以出路耶。世之喜用热药峻攻者，能知此乎？噫！天下之服辛热而转能夜食者多矣，肯因俚言而三思否？[81p]

Those who have long consumed harsh and strong medicines also yearn for food in the dead of night. People do not understand the reason for this; instead, they celebrate the ability to eat without realizing the importance of preserving the spleen's function, allowing it to operate during the day and rest at night, which is necessary for balance. Furthermore, the phlegm in the human body flows from the stomach through the meridians; thus, the phlegm from the meridians must return to the stomach to rise up through the mouth and descend through the intestines. This can only happen when the spleen’s function is tranquil. Therefore, anyone with phlegm-related issues should not only eat early and at noon but should also rest and preserve the spleen's function to allow the phlegm in the meridians to return to the stomach, where it can properly ascend and descend, rather than dispersing from the spleen. Observe those with mild phlegm conditions who can comfortably sleep at night and the next morning can expel phlegm; contrast this with those with severe phlegm conditions who are dazed, unable to expel it due to lack of food and the spleen not being at rest, thus blocking the phlegm’s exit. Do those who love to use strong medicines realize this? Alas! Many in the world who enjoy spicy and heated treatments manage to eat at night; will they reconsider their words and reflect three times?[81p]

　　　　景岳全书 【明　张介宾】

　　　　　论证

　　痰饮一证，在《内经》止有积饮之说，本无痰证之名，此《内经》之不重痰证，概可知矣。及考痰之为名，虽起自仲景，后世相传，无论是痰非痰，开口便言痰火，有云怪病之为痰者，有云痰为百病母者，似乎痰之关系不为不重，而何《内经》之忽之也？不知痰之为病，必有所以致之者，如因风因火而生痰者，但治其风火，风火息而痰自清也。因虚因实而生痰者，但治其虚实，虚实愈而痰自平也。未闻治其痰而风火可自散，虚实可自调者。[82p]

On Evidence

The condition of phlegm and fluid is only mentioned in the "Inner Canon" as a case of accumulated fluid, and it never explicitly refers to phlegm as a disease. This indicates that the "Inner Canon" does not place significant emphasis on the phlegm condition. Upon examining the term "phlegm," though it originated from Zhongjing, it has been passed down through generations, and regardless of whether one discusses phlegm or not, people often mention "phlegm-fire." Some say strange diseases are due to phlegm, while others claim phlegm is the source of numerous ailments, suggesting that the relationship with phlegm is not taken lightly. So why then does the "Inner Canon" overlook it?

One must understand that the occurrence of phlegm as a disease must have its causes. For example, if phlegm arises from wind or fire, treating the wind or fire will clear the phlegm on its own. If phlegm arises from deficiency or excess, addressing the deficiency or excess will also resolve the phlegm. I have never heard of treating phlegm alone to disperse wind and fire or to adjust deficiency and excess.[82p]

此所以痰必因病而生，非病之因痰而致也。故《内经》之不言痰者，正以痰非病之本，乃病之标耳。今举世医流，但知百计攻痰，便是治病，竟不知所以为痰，及因何而起，是何异引指以使臂，灌叶以救根者乎？标本误认，主见失真，欲求愈病，难矣。　　痰之与饮，虽曰同类，而实有不同也。盖饮为水液之属，凡呕吐清水及胸腹膨满，吞酸嗳腐，渥渥有声等证，此皆水谷之余，停积不行，是即所谓饮也。若痰有不同于饮者，饮清彻而痰稠浊，饮惟停积肠胃，而痰则无处不到。[83p]

This is why phlegm must arise due to illness, and not the other way around—illness does not cause phlegm. Therefore, the "Inner Canon" does not mention phlegm, specifically because phlegm is not the root of the disease; it is merely a symptom. Today, practitioners worldwide focus solely on attacking phlegm, believing that this treats the disease, yet they do not understand what phlegm is or how it arises. This is akin to pointing at an arm to understand the shoulder or watering leaves to save the roots. Misrecognition of symptoms and underlying causes leads to losing the true perspective; seeking to cure the disease becomes difficult.

Although phlegm and liquid are said to belong to the same category, they are indeed different. Liquid pertains to water and fluids; any vomiting of clear water, abdominal distension, sour belching, or sounds of wetness are all symptoms of stagnant food and fluids that do not circulate—this is referred to as liquid. Phlegm, however, differs from liquid; liquid is clear, while phlegm is thick and turbid. Liquid merely stagnates in the intestines and stomach, while phlegm can appear in any part of the body.[83p]

水谷不化而停为饮者，其病全由脾胃；无处不到而化为痰者，凡五脏之伤皆能致之。故治此者，当知所辨，而不可不察其本也。　　痰即人之津液，无非水谷之所化，此痰亦既化之物，而非不化之属也。但化得其正，则形体强，荣卫充，而痰涎本皆血气。若化失其正，则脏腑病，津液败，而血气即成痰涎。此亦犹乱世之盗贼，何孰非治世之良民。但盗贼之兴，必由国运之病；而痰涎之作，必由元气之病。尝闻之立斋先生曰：使血气俱盛，何痰之有？余于初年颇疑此言，而谓岂无实痰乎？及今见定识多，始信其然也。[84p]

When food and drink do not transform and instead become phlegm, this illness is entirely due to the spleen and stomach. Phlegm arises from various organs' injuries, and thus, in treating this, one must understand how to discern the problem, paying close attention to its root.

Phlegm is essentially the body's fluids, transformed from food and drink. This phlegm is a transformed substance, not something that does not transform. When transformation occurs properly, the body is strong, and nourishment flows abundantly, with phlegm and mucus originating from blood and qi. However, when transformation goes awry, the organs suffer, fluids become disrupted, and blood and qi turn into phlegm and mucus. This is akin to thieves arising in a chaotic world; who among them does not wish for peace? Yet, the rise of thieves is surely due to the decline of the state, and the emergence of phlegm and mucus must occur due to the decay of vital energy.

I once heard Mr. Li Zhai say: if blood and qi are both flourishing, how could there be phlegm? In my early years, I somewhat doubted this statement, thinking, is there truly no real phlegm? But now, having gained deeper understanding, I begin to believe it.[84p]

何以见之？盖痰涎之化，本因水谷，使果脾强胃健如少壮者流，则随食随化，皆成血气，焉得留而为痰。惟其不能尽化，而十留一二，则一二为痰矣；十留三四，则三四为痰矣；甚至留其七八，则但见血气日消，而痰涎日多矣。此其故，正以元气不能运化，愈虚则痰愈盛也。然则立斋之言，岂非出常之见乎。今见治痰者，必曰痰之为患，不攻如何得去。不知正气不行，而虚痰结聚，则虽竭力攻之，非惟痰不可去，而且益增其虚。故或有因攻而遽绝者，或偶尔暂苏而更甚于他日者，皆误攻也。孰知痰之可攻者少，而不可攻者多，治痰者不可不先察虚实。[85p]

How can one see this? The transformation of phlegm and saliva fundamentally arises from food and water. If the spleen is strong and the stomach healthy, just like in youth, then it transforms food into blood and qi as it is consumed, leaving no room for phlegm to remain. However, if transformation is not complete, and one or two parts are left over, then those become phlegm; if three or four parts linger, then those are phlegm too; and if seven or eight remain, one will see the daily decline of blood and qi, while phlegm increases daily. The reason for this is that the original qi cannot function effectively, and as deficiency increases, phlegm becomes more abundant. Thus, the words of Li Zhai suggest a perspective beyond the ordinary. Currently, those who treat phlegm always say it is the cause of suffering and that one must attack it to eliminate it. They do not realize that when the righteous qi is stagnant and phlegm accumulates due to deficiency, even with vigorous efforts to attack it, not only can phlegm not be expelled, but the deficiency may worsen. Some may experience sudden cessation of phlegm due to aggressive treatment, only to find that it becomes more severe later on—this is a miscalculation in treatment. Few know that the phlegm that can be attacked is rarer, while the phlegm that cannot be attacked is more common; hence, those treating phlegm must first assess the underlying deficiency or excess.[85p]

　　痰有虚实，不可不辨。夫痰若有余，又何有虚实之异？盖虚实二字，全以元气为言。凡可攻者，便是实痰；不可攻者，便是虚痰。何为可攻？以其年力犹盛，血气未伤，或以肥甘过度，或以湿热盛行，或风寒外闭皮毛，或逆气内连肝膈，皆能骤致痰饮。但察其形气病气，但属有余者，则实痰也。实痰者何？谓其元气犹实也。此则宜行消伐，但去其痰无不可也。何为不可攻？则或以形羸气弱，年及中衰者，即虚痰也。[86p]

Phlegm has qualities of deficiency and excess, and it is important to distinguish between them. If phlegm were always in excess, then what difference would there be between deficiency and excess? The terms deficiency and excess are entirely related to the original qi. Anything that can be addressed or treated is considered excess phlegm; anything that cannot be addressed is considered deficient phlegm. What does it mean to be treatable? It refers to cases where the body’s strength is still robust, the blood and qi are not harmed, or when there is an overabundance of rich and sweet foods, or when dampness and heat are prevalent, or when wind and cold block the skin, or when rebellious qi obstructs the liver and diaphragm; all these can suddenly lead to phlegm retention. By observing the manifestations and the signs of disease, anything that is characterized by excess is excess phlegm. What is excess phlegm? It means that the original qi is still strong. In this case, it is appropriate to disperse and eliminate it, as it is permissible to remove the phlegm. What does it mean to be untreatable? This refers to cases where the body is slender and weak, or where one has reached middle age and is declining; such conditions indicate deficient phlegm.[86p]

或以多病，或以劳倦，或以忧思酒色，致成劳损非风卒厥者，亦虚痰也。或脉见细数，脏无阳邪，时为呕恶泄泻气短声哑等证，但察其形气病气，本无有余者，皆虚痰也。虚痰者何？谓其元气已虚也。此则但宜调补，若或攻之，无不危矣。且凡实痰本不多，其来也骤，其去亦速，其病亦易治。何也？以病本不深也。虚痰反多，其来则渐，其去则迟，其病亦难治。何也？以病非一日也。是以实痰无足虑，而最可畏者虚痰耳。总之，治痰之法无他，但能使元气日强，则痰必日少，即有微痰，亦不能为害，而且以充助胃气。若元气日衰，则水谷津液，无非痰耳。[87p]

Some are plagued by various illnesses, some by exhaustion, and some by worries, drink, and indulgence, leading to fatigue and ailments that are not due to wind or sudden seizures but rather to phlegm due to deficiency. Others may present with thin and rapid pulses, and without any pathogenic factors in the organs, exhibiting symptoms of nausea, vomiting, diarrhea, shortness of breath, and hoarseness. However, upon observing their physical condition and the nature of their symptoms, if there is no excess, it is all phlegm due to deficiency. What is phlegm due to deficiency? It refers to the depletion of one's vital energy. In this case, one should only proceed with nourishment and reinforcement; any attempt to attack it will lead to danger. Moreover, in the case of phlegm due to excess, it is originally not abundant, it arises suddenly, disperses quickly, and the illness is easy to treat. Why is that? Because the illness is not deep-rooted. In contrast, phlegm due to deficiency is often abundant; it accumulates gradually, disperses slowly, and is difficult to treat. Why is that? Because the illness has persisted for a long time. Therefore, phlegm due to excess is not a great concern, while phlegm due to deficiency is the most fearsome. In summary, the method to treat phlegm is straightforward: the key is to strengthen the vital energy daily, and then the phlegm will gradually decrease. Even if there is a slight phlegm, it will not cause harm, and it will also support the stomach’s energy. Conversely, if the vital energy declines daily, then all fluids from food and drink will essentially turn into phlegm.[87p]

随去随生，有能攻之使尽，而且保元气无恙者，吾不信也。故善治痰者，惟能使之不生，方是补天之手。然则治此者，可不辨其虚实，而欲一概攻之，如王隐君所论内外百病皆生于痰，悉用滚痰丸之类，其亦但知目前而不知日后之害也。五脏之病，虽俱能生痰，然无不由乎脾肾。盖肾主湿，湿动则为痰；肾主水，水泛亦为痰。故痰之化无不在脾，而痰之本无不在肾。所以凡是痰证，非此则彼，必与二脏有涉。但脾家之痰，则有虚有实。如湿滞太过者，脾之实也；土衰不能制水者，脾之虚也。若肾家之痰，则无非虚耳。[88p]

As one goes, one lives; if there are those who can attack it to the end, while also protecting the original vital energy unharmed, I do not believe it is possible. Therefore, those skilled in treating phlegm are only able to prevent its generation, which is the true art of mending heaven. Hence, regarding treatment of this condition, one cannot discern its reality or falsehood, and wishes to attack it indiscriminately, as Wang Yinjun discussed, claiming that all internal and external ailments arise from phlegm, applying remedies like the rolling phlegm pill without knowing the future harm that may ensue.

While diseases of the five organs can indeed produce phlegm, they all derive from the spleen and kidneys. The kidneys govern dampness; when dampness moves, it becomes phlegm. The kidneys also govern water; when water overflows, it too becomes phlegm. Hence, the transformation of phlegm does not occur without the spleen, and the essence of phlegm always lies in the kidneys. Therefore, every phlegm condition, whether one aspect or the other, must involve these two organs. However, phlegm from the spleen can be either deficient or excessive. If there is excessive stagnation of dampness, it is due to the spleen being full; if the earth is weak and cannot control water, it results from the spleen being deficient. Conversely, phlegm arising from the kidneys is always a matter of deficiency.[88p]

盖火不能生土者，即火不制水，阳不胜阴者，必水反侵脾，是皆阴中之火虚也。若火盛烁金，则精不守舍，津枯液涸，则金水相残，是皆阴中之水虚也。此脾肾虚实之有不同者，所当辨也。又若古人所云湿痰、郁痰、寒痰、热痰之类，虽其在上在下，或寒或热，各有不同，然其化生之原，又安能外此二脏？如寒痰湿痰本脾家之病，而寒湿之生，果无干于肾乎？木郁生风，本肝家之痰，而木强制土，能无涉于脾乎？火盛克金，其痰在肺，而火邪炎上，有不从中下二焦者乎？故凡欲治痰而不知所源者，总惟猜摸而已耳。[89p]

The essence of fire cannot generate earth; that is, fire does not control water, and yang cannot overcome yin, which results in water invading the spleen; this indicates a deficiency of fire within yin. Conversely, if fire is strong and scorches metal, essence cannot reside properly, and fluids dry up, leading to mutual destruction between metal and water; this indicates a deficiency of water within yin. This distinction between the deficiency and surplus of the spleen and kidneys must be clarified.

Furthermore, regarding what ancient people referred to as damp phlegm, stagnant phlegm, cold phlegm, and heat phlegm, despite their differing locations—whether up or down, cold or hot—each has its own characteristics; however, their origins of transformation must also involve these two organs. For instance, cold phlegm and damp phlegm fundamentally stem from spleen issues, yet does the generation of cold dampness not also involve the kidneys? Wind from wood stagnation originates from the liver's phlegm, but when wood overpowers earth, can it not also relate to the spleen? When fire is strong and attacks metal, phlegm resides in the lungs, and when fire pathogenic heat rises, can it not impact both the upper and lower jiao? Therefore, anyone wishing to treat phlegm without understanding its source is merely guessing.[89p]

　　　　　论治

　　脾胃之痰，有虚有实。凡脾土湿胜，或食饮过度，别无虚证而生痰者，此乃脾家本病，但去其湿滞，而痰自清，宜二陈汤为主治，或六安煎、橘皮半夏汤、平胃散、润下丸、滚痰丸之类，皆可择而用之。若胃寒生痰而兼胀满者，宜和胃二陈煎；或兼呕吐而痛者，宜神香散；或为饮食所致，宜加麦芽、神曲、山楂、枳实之类。然脾胃不虚，则虽生痰饮，不过微有留滞，亦必不多，且无大害。惟脾虚饮食不能消化而作痰者，其变最多，但当调理脾胃，使其气强，则自无食积之患，而痰饮即皆血气矣。[90p]

On Treatment

The phlegm of the spleen and stomach can be either due to deficiency or excess. When the dampness of the spleen soil is excessive, or when there is overindulgence in food and drink, and there are no deficiency symptoms that lead to phlegm, this is a primary condition of the spleen. Simply removing the dampness will clear the phlegm, and the primary treatment should be Er Chen Decoction, or alternatives such as Liu An Decoction, Tangerine Peel and Pinellia Decoction, Ping Wei San, Run Xia Wan, and Gun Tan Wan, among others. If phlegm arises from cold in the stomach along with bloating, He Wei Er Chen Decoction should be used; if accompanied by vomiting and pain, Shen Xiang San is appropriate; if caused by food, one should add malt, spirit-activated barley, hawthorn, and bitter orange. However, if the spleen and stomach are not deficient, then even if phlegm and fluid arise, it is likely only slight retention, thus not very harmful. Only in cases where the spleen is deficient and food cannot be digested, leading to phlegm, can the variations be many. The solution lies in regulating the spleen and stomach to strengthen their qi, which will eliminate the problems of food stagnation, making the phlegm and fluids part of the blood and qi.[90p]

若脾气微虚，不能制湿，或不能运化而为痰者，其证必食减神倦，或兼痞闷等证，宜六君子汤或五味异功散之类主之，金水六君煎亦妙。若微虚兼寒者，宜苓朮二陈煎主之。若脾气大虚，或兼胃寒呕恶而多痰者，宜六味异功煎、温胃饮、理中汤、圣朮煎之类主之。又有劳倦本以伤脾，而疲极又伤肝肾，脾气伤则饮食减少，或见恶心，肝肾伤则水液妄行，或痰饮起自脐下，直冲而上，此脾肾俱伤，命门土母之病也。虽八味地黄丸乃其正治，然无如理阴煎，其效更如神也。或加白朮、陈皮亦可。　　肾经之痰，水泛为痰者也，无非虚证。有以肿胀而生痰者，此水入脾经，谓之反克。脏平者，宜六味地黄丸、左归饮之类主之。[91p]

If the spleen qi is slightly deficient and unable to control dampness, or unable to transform and thus produces phlegm, the symptoms will be reduced appetite and fatigue, possibly accompanied by feelings of fullness or oppression. The appropriate treatments are six gentlemen decoction or five-flavored pilose antler powder, with Jinshui Liu Jun decoction also being excellent. If there is slight deficiency combined with cold, use Ling Zhu Er Chen decoction for treatment. If the spleen qi is greatly deficient, or if there is accompanying stomach cold leading to nausea and excessive phlegm, one should use six flavors of medicinal herbs decoction, warming the stomach drink, or regulating middle decoction as treatments.

Furthermore, overexertion can damage the spleen, and extreme fatigue can harm the liver and kidneys. With spleen qi damage, intake may decrease or nausea may be experienced; with liver and kidney damage, there may be misdirection of fluids or phlegm rising from below the navel. This indicates injury to both the spleen and kidney, a condition related to the root of life and mother of the earth. While the Eight Flavor Rehmannia Pill is the standard treatment, the Yin regulating decoction is even more effective. White atractylodes and dried tangerine peel may also be added.

Phlegm originating from the kidney channel occurs when fluid becomes phlegm, which is mostly a deficiency syndrome. There are instances where swelling leads to phlegm due to water entering the spleen channel, termed counteracting. For a balanced condition, one should use the Eight Flavor Rehmannia Pill or Zuo Gui Decoction as treatments.[91p]

脏寒者，宜理阴煎、加减金匮肾气丸、八味地黄丸之类主之。其或但宜温燥者，则单助脾经亦能化湿，惟六味异功煎及理中汤、圣朮煎俱可酌用。有虚损而生痰者，此水亏金涸，精不化气，气不化精而然。使不养阴以济阳，则水气不充，痰终不化，水不归源，痰终不宁，宜以左归、右归、六味、八味等丸，酌其寒热而用之。若阴火乘肺，津液干枯，或喉痛，或烦热，或喜冷，或便实，必察其真有火邪，而痰嗽不已者，宜四阴煎、一阴煎之类加减主之。若火本非真，则但宜纯补，庶保万全也。[92p]

For those with cold and dampness, it is advisable to treat with warming decoctions such as Yin Jian and modified versions of Ren Shen Qi Wan and Ba Wei Di Huang Wan. If one merely requires warmth and dryness, then solely assisting the spleen channel can also resolve dampness; in this case, Liu Wei Di Huang Jian, Li Zhong Tang, and Sheng Zhu Jian can be appropriately used. In cases of deficiency leading to phlegm, where water is depleted and metal is drained, essence cannot transform into qi, and qi cannot transform into essence. If one does not nourish yin to support yang, then water and qi will not be sufficient, leading to unresolved phlegm and stagnant water. It is advisable to use formulations such as Zuo Gui Wan, You Gui Wan, Liu Wei Wan, and Ba Wei Wan, adjusting for cold and heat as necessary. If yin fire attacks the lungs, causing dry fluids, sore throat, restlessness, preference for cold, or firm stools, one must check for genuine fire evil and persistent phlegm cough. In such cases, modified versions of Si Yin Jian and Yi Yin Jian should be prescribed. If the fire is not genuine, then pure tonification is sufficient to ensure safety and health.[92p]

　　风寒之痰，以邪自皮毛，内袭于肺，肺气不清，乃致生痰，是即伤寒之类，但从辛散，其痰自愈，宜六安煎、二陈汤，甚者小青龙汤之类主之。其有风寒外袭，内兼火邪者，亦可兼用黄芩。若血气兼虚者，不得单用消耗，宜金水六君煎主之。若伤寒见风而兼发热嗽痰者，宜柴陈煎主之，或金水六君煎加柴胡亦可。　　中风之痰本非外感，悉由脾肾虚败所致，治痰之法，详载非风门，当与此互察之。　　治痰当分缓急。凡非风等证，其有痰涎壅盛，闭塞上焦，而药食不能进者，此不得不先治其痰，以开清道。若痰之甚者，惟用吐法为最妙。若痰气不甚，食饮可进，便当从缓求其本而治之，不宜妄行攻击，或但以六安煎、二陈汤、润下丸、橘皮半夏汤之类调之为宜。若火盛生痰者，宜清膈煎、抽薪饮之类主之。[93p]

Phlegm caused by wind-cold arises from external pathogens affecting the skin and hair, invading the lungs, leading to unclear lung qi and subsequently the production of phlegm. This is a type of cold damage; if treated with pungent and dispersing methods, the phlegm can resolve on its own. It is advisable to use formulas like Liu'an Decoction or Erchen Decoction, and for more severe cases, Xiao Qinglong Decoction or similar remedies. If there is an external invasion of wind-cold combined with internal fire, one may also use Huangqin. In cases where blood and qi are both deficient, one should not solely rely on depleting treatments but should use Jinshui Liujun Decoction as the main remedy.
