Elder Liang Houzhai had shortness of breath with phlegm, red and painful urination, heel pain, and a floating and large pulse that felt weak upon palpation. This was a case of kidney deficiency with phlegm accumulation. I administered Si Wu Decoction combined with Liu Wei Wan, and he recovered in less than a month. As taught by Master Zhang Zhongjing, when there is qi deficiency with phlegm, one should use Kidney Qi Pills to tonify and eliminate it. Truly, it enlightens the ignorant and rescues the constrained. The Kidney Qi Pill is indeed the Liu Wei Wan.[195p]

　　都宪孟有涯气短痰运，服辛香之剂，痰盛遗尿，两尺浮大，按之如无。余以为肾家不能纳气归源，香燥致甚耳。用八味丸料三剂而愈。
　　上舍顾桐石会饮于周上舍第，问余曰：向孟有涯、陈东谷俱为无嗣纳宠，已而得疾，皆头运吐痰，并用苏合香丸，惟有涯得生，何也？余曰：二证因肾虚不能纳气而为头运，不能制水而为痰涎。东谷专主攻痰行气，有涯专于益火补气故耳。后余应杭人之请，桐石房劳过度，亦患前证，或用清气化痰，愈甚。顾曰：我病是肾虚不能纳气归源。治者不悟而殁，惜哉！
　　一男子素厚味，胸满痰盛。余曰：膏粱之人，内多积热。与法制清气化痰丸而愈。彼为有验，修合馈送，脾胃虚者，无不受害。
　　先兄体貌丰伟，唾痰甚多，脉洪有力，殊不耐劳，通风头运欲仆，口舌破裂，或至赤烂，误食姜蒜少许，口疮益甚，服八味丸及补中益气加附子钱许，即愈。停药月余，诸证仍作。此命门虚火不归源也，仍服前药而愈。[196p]

Du Xian Meng had a shortness of breath with a lot of phlegm, leading to urinary issues, with a significant swelling that felt like there was nothing there when pressed. I believed that the kidney function was incapable of properly taking in breath, and the strong aromatic herbs exacerbated the issue. Using the Ba Wei pill in three doses cured him.

Gao Tong Shi was drinking at the ZHOU Shang She residence and asked me: "Meng Youya and Chen Donggu both had no offspring and then fell ill, resulting in vomiting phlegm; both used Suhe Xiang pills, yet only Youya survived. Why is that?" I replied: "Both cases stem from kidney deficiency that cannot take in breath, leading to head wind and the inability to control water, resulting in phlegm. Donggu emphasized treating phlegm to move qi, while Youya focused on supporting fire and tonifying qi." Later, at the request of a Hangzhou person, after Gao Tong Shi overworked himself, he experienced similar symptoms. Using methods to clear qi and transform phlegm made him worse. He remarked: "My illness is due to kidney deficiency that cannot return breath to its source." Unfortunately, the physician did not realize it and he passed away, what a pity!

One man had a preference for rich food and suffered from chest fullness and excessive phlegm. I said: "A person with rich diet tends to accumulate heat." I prescribed the Qing Qi Hua Tan pill and he was cured. This was effective and showed that those with weak spleen and stomach would inevitably suffer.

My older brother had a robust appearance but produced much phlegm. His pulse was strong and full, yet he could not endure exertion, often experiencing a head wind that made him faint, and had oral sores that would sometimes become red and ulcerated. After mistakenly eating a little ginger and garlic, his mouth sores worsened. He took the Ba Wei pill and added a tonifying midsection and qi with Fu Zi, and he recovered. After stopping the medication for over a month, the symptoms recurred. This indicated a deficiency of the life gate fire that did not return to its source, so he continued taking the previous medicine and was cured again.[196p]

　　一儒者每劳役则食少胸痞，发热头痛，吐痰作渴，脉浮大，余谓此脾胃气虚而血病也。不信，服二陈、四物、黄蘗、知母之类，腹痛作呕，脉洪数而无伦次。先以六君子汤加炮姜，痛呕渐愈；又用补中益气汤而痊。
　　学士徐崦西口干有痰，欲服琼玉膏。予曰：此沉阴降火之剂，君面白口干而有痰，属脾肺气虚也，当用温补之剂。不信仍服。两月余大便不实，饮食少思，且兼阴痿，始信予言。先用补中益气，加茯苓、半夏二味以温补脾胃，饮食渐加，大便渐实；乃去二味服月余而痊；更服六味丸，三月余阴道如常。矧琼玉膏、固本丸、坎离丸，此辈俱是沉寒泻火之剂，非肠胃有燥热者不宜服。若足三阴经阴虚发热者，久而服之，令人无子。盖谓损其阳气，则阴血无所生故也，屡验。[197p]

A scholar experienced labor and then had little appetite, felt a tightness in the chest, developed a fever and headache, coughed up phlegm, and felt thirsty, with a pulse that was floating and large. I believed this was due to a deficiency of spleen and stomach qi and related to a blood condition. When I was not believed, he took herbs like Erchen and Siwu, Huangbo, and Zhimu, resulting in abdominal pain and vomiting, with a pulse that was surging, rapid, and disordered. Initially, I prescribed Liu Junzi Decoction with roasted ginger, and his pain and vomiting gradually improved. I followed up with Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction, and he fully recovered.

Scholar Xu Yan had a dry mouth and phlegm, wanting to take Qiongyu Paste. I advised him that this was a remedy to subdue yin and lower fire. He had a pale face, dry mouth, and phlegm, suggesting a deficiency of spleen and lung qi; thus, he should use warming and tonifying remedies. He did not believe me and insisted on taking it. After more than two months, he had loose stools, little appetite, and also developed impotence; only then did he start to believe my words. I first used Bu Zhong Yi Qi, adding Poria and Banxia to warm and tonify the spleen and stomach. Gradually, his appetite increased, and his stools became firmer. After stopping those two herbs and taking the formula for over a month, he fully recovered; moreover, after taking Liuwei Dihuang Wan for more than three months, his condition returned to normal.

Furthermore, Qiongyu Paste, Guben Wan, and Kanli Wan are all remedies for reducing cold and lowering fire; they should not be taken by those whose intestines and stomach are not dry and hot. If someone with yin deficiency in the three yin channels takes them for a long time, it may render them childless. This is because it depletes their yang qi, resulting in insufficient yin blood for generation, as has been repeatedly observed.[197p]

　　阳山之内素善怒，胸膈不利，吐痰甚多，吞酸嗳腐，饮食少思，手足发热。所服非芩连枳实，必槟苏厚朴。左关弦洪，右关弦数。余以为肝火血燥，木乘土位也。朝用六味地黄丸以滋养肝木，夕用六君子加当归、芍药以调补脾土，不月而愈。后因恚怒，前疾复作。或用二陈加石膏服之，吐涎如涌，外热如灼，脉洪大，按之如无。余曰：脾主涎，乃脾损发热而涎泛溢也。用六君子加姜桂，一服即睡，觉而诸证顿失，又数剂而康。若服理气化痰等药，必变腹胀喘促腿浮膝肿淋沥等证，急用济生加减肾气丸救之，多有得生者。[198p]

Within Yangshan, the individual is prone to anger, experiences discomfort in the chest, produces excessive phlegm, swallows sour and putrid substances, has diminished appetite, and feels heat in the hands and feet. The medications taken are not likely to be for clearing heat such as Chuanqionghua and Zhi Shi, but should instead include ingredients like Bingsu and Houpo. The left pulse is strong and full, while the right is weak and rapid. I believe this indicates liver fire and blood dryness, with wood overpowering earth.

In the morning, use Liuwei Dihuang Wan to nourish the liver wood; in the evening, employ Liu Junzi Decoction with added Donggui and Shaoyao to tonify the spleen earth. Recovery should occur in less than a month. However, if anger arises again, the previous ailment may reoccur. One might take Er Chen Tang with Gypsum, leading to a surge of saliva, external heat resembling burning, and a strong, large pulse that feels empty upon pressure. I argue that the spleen governs saliva, and its deficiency leads to heat and excessive salivation.

Using Liu Junzi with Ginger and Cinnamon will allow for immediate sleep, resulting in the sudden disappearance of all symptoms, with a few doses leading to recovery. However, if one takes medications for regulating qi or transforming phlegm, symptoms such as abdominal distension, shortness of breath, leg swelling, knee edema, and dripping may develop. In emergencies, use Jisheng Jiajian Shenqi Wan for rescue, which often saves many lives.[198p]

　　一男子食少胸满，手足逆冷，饮食畏寒，发热吐痰，时欲作呕。自用清气化痰之剂，胸腹愈胀，呼吸不利，吐痰呕食，小便淋漓；又用五苓散之类，小便不利，诸病益甚。余曰：此脾土虚寒，无火之证，故食入不消而反出，非气膈所致。遂用八味丸、补中益气加半夏茯苓姜桂，旬日乃愈。
　　一男子体肥善饮，舌本强，语濇痰壅，口眼喎斜，肢体不遂。余谓脾虚湿热痰涎所致，用六君子加煨干姜、山栀、神曲而愈。
　　少司马黎仰之因怒耳鸣，吐痰作呕不食，寒热胁痛，用小柴胡合四物，加山栀、茯神，陈皮而瘥。[199p]

A man experienced reduced appetite, a feeling of fullness in his chest, coldness in his hands and feet, aversion to cold foods, fever, sputum, and occasional nausea. He self-administered a remedy to clear phlegm but found his chest and abdomen more distended, breathing hindered, and continued to spit up phlegm and vomit food, with urine being scant and dribbling. He then tried a formula like Wuling San, but urination was still difficult and all his ailments worsened. I said: This is due to a deficiency and coldness in the spleen's earth element, with no fire present; therefore, food cannot be digested and instead is regurgitated, not caused by qi obstruction. I prescribed Bawei Wan, supplemented with Zhongyiqi and added Banxia, Fuling, Ginger, and Cinnamon. He recovered in ten days.

Another man, robust and fond of drinking, had a strong root of the tongue, spoke with difficulty due to phlegm obstruction, and had a crooked mouth and eyes, with limbs not functioning properly. I diagnosed this as due to spleen deficiency with damp heat and phlegm accumulation. I treated him with Liujunzi Decoction, adding dry ginger, Shan Zhi, and Shen Qu, and he recovered.

A young official named Li had tinnitus from anger, experienced phlegm and nausea, could not eat, and suffered cold and hot pain in his side. I prescribed Xiao Chai Hu Decoction combined with Si Wu, adding Shan Zhi, Fuling, and Chen Pi, and he was cured.[199p]

　　一男子素不善调摄，唾痰口干，饮食不美，服化痰行气之剂，胸满腹膨，痰涎愈盛；服导痰理脾之剂，肚腹膨胀，二便不利；服分气利水之剂，腹大胁痛，睡卧不得；服破血消导之剂，两足背肿，两关脉浮大，不及于寸口。余以脾土虚而生痰，朝用金匮加减肾气丸，夕用补中益气汤煎送前丸，月余诸证渐退，饮食渐进；再用八味丸、补中益气汤，月余乃能转侧，又两月而能步履；却服十全大补汤、还少丹，又半载而康。后稍失调理，其腹仍胀，随服前药即愈。
　　旧僚钱可久素善饮，面赤痰盛，大便不实。余以为肠胃湿痰壅滞，用二陈、芩、连、山栀、枳实、干葛、泽泻、升麻一剂，吐痰甚多，大便始实，此后日以黄连三钱泡汤饮之而安。
　　横金陈子复面带赤色，吐痰口干，或时作泻。或用二陈、黄连、枳实之类，不应。予脉之，左关弦急，右关弦大，此乃肾水挟肝木之势，而克胜脾土也。不信，后交夏果患痢而亡。[200p]

A man, not skilled at moderation, experienced dry mouth and excessive phlegm, with unappetizing meals. He took medicine to resolve phlegm and promote qi, but felt full in the chest and his abdomen swelled, with phlegm increasing. He then took medicine to guide phlegm and regulate the spleen, but his belly expanded, and he had difficulty with urination and defecation. After that, he took medicine to disperse qi and relieve water retention; his abdomen became large, and he had pain in the sides, preventing him from sleeping. Upon taking medicine to break blood and guide out, he had swelling in both legs and his pulses were large at the joints, but weak at the inch pulse. I diagnosed his condition as phlegm caused by spleen deficiency and prescribed modified Kidney Qi Pills in the morning and tonic decoction in the evening. After a month, his symptoms gradually improved, and he could eat more. Then, I prescribed Eight Flavor Pills and the tonic decoction again. After another month, he could turn over, and in two months, he was able to walk. Eventually, he took Complete Qi Tonic Decoction and a rejuvenating pill, and after half a year, he fully recovered. Later, if he lost regulation slightly, his abdomen would swell again, but taking the previous medicine would cure him.

My old colleague Qian Kejiu, who enjoyed drinking, had a red face and excessive phlegm, with unformed stools. I considered his condition as damp phlegm stagnating in the intestines and stomach, so I prescribed a formula including Erchen, Qinjiao, Lian, Shan Zhi, Zhishi, Gande, Zexie, and Shengma. He coughed up a lot of phlegm, and his stool became firm. After that, he drank a decoction of Huanglian three qian daily and felt at ease.

Heng Jincheng also had a red face, coughed up phlegm, and occasionally experienced diarrhea. I prescribed something similar to Erchen, Huanglian, and Zhishi, but it did not work for him. I felt his pulse; the left guan was tense, and the right guan was large, indicating that kidney water was carrying liver wood, overpowering spleen earth. If he did not believe this, later he succumbed to dysentery from summer fruits and passed away.[200p]

　　府庠沈文姬母食湿面，吞酸呕吐绝食。服芩连等剂，加寒热口干流涎；又食冬瓜一星，而呕吐愈甚。予谓：此脾气虚寒也。急用盐艾附子炒热熨脐腹，又以其子口气接其母气，神气少苏；以参、朮、附子、陈皮为末，丸如粟米大，津咽五七粒，次日加至十余粒；渐服煎剂一二匙，乃思粥饮；又以参朮等药五十余剂而愈。
　　一儒者咳嗽痰盛，胸腹不利，饮食少思，肢体倦怠，脉浮大，按之微弱，服二陈、枳壳等药愈盛。余曰：脾肺肾虚也。用补中益气汤、六味地黄丸而愈。
　　一妇人脾胃虚弱，饮食素少，忽痰壅气喘，头摇目札，手扬足掷，难以候脉。视其面色，黄中兼青，此肝木乘脾胃也。用六君子加柴胡、升麻治之而苏；更以补中益气加半夏调理而痊。
　　一男子素吐痰，遇怒，其痰益甚，胸膈痞满，此肝木制脾土也，用六君加木香治之而痊。
　　一妇人素郁结，胸膈不宽，吐痰如胶，用加味归脾汤乃瘥。[201p]

In the official residence, Shen Wenji’s mother ate damp noodles, suffered from sourness and vomiting, and refused to eat. After taking herbal formulas such as Qinjian, she experienced cold and heat, dry mouth, and drooling; she then ate a piece of winter melon, which intensified her vomiting. I assessed that her spleen was weak and cold. I urgently applied a warm poultice of salt, mugwort, and aconite to her navel and abdomen. Additionally, her son inhaled her breath to connect with her spirit, which slightly revived her. I ground ginseng, poria, aconite, and dried tangerine peel into powder and formed pills the size of millet, instructing her to swallow five to seven pills, increasing to more than ten the next day. Gradually, she took one or two spoonfuls of decoction and craved porridge to drink. After over fifty doses of ginseng and poria, she recovered.

A scholar suffered from a persistent cough with excessive phlegm, discomfort in the chest and abdomen, little appetite, fatigue in his limbs, and a pulse that was floating and large yet weak upon pressure. After taking Erchen decoction and bitter orange, the phlegm became worse. I suggested that he had deficiencies in the spleen, lungs, and kidneys. By administering the Bu Zhong Yi Qi decoction and Liu Wei Di Huang Wan, he recovered.

A woman with weak spleen and stomach, who had little appetite, suddenly experienced phlegm obstructing her breath, shaking her head and eyes, and throwing her hands and feet, making it hard to take her pulse. Observing her complexion, which was yellow with a hint of blue, showed that the liver's wood element was overwhelming her spleen and stomach. After treating her with the Six Gentlemen decoction, adding Bupleurum and Cimicifuga, she revived and further used Bu Zhong Yi Qi plus Pinellia for recovery.

A man commonly had phlegm and worsened it with anger, feeling fullness and obstruction in his chest. This indicated that the liver's wood was constraining the spleen's earth. After using the Six Gentlemen with cardamom for treatment, he was cured.

A woman, generally feeling oppressed, found her chest tight and vomited thick phlegm like glue. She was cured by taking the modified Gui Pi decoction.[201p]

　　一妇人吐痰头运，带下青黄，用四七汤送白丸子、小柴胡加白朮、茯苓治之而安。
　　一妇人元气素弱，痰气时作，或咽间不利，或胸痞等证。予以为郁结伤脾，用加味归脾汤治之而愈。后遇恚怒，前证仍作，惑于众言，以为痰饮，妄用祛痰之剂，吐泻数次，变诸异证，口噤不醒。余以为脾胃复伤，日用六君子一剂米饮浓煎，常服匙许；至四日渐进粥食，乃服前药，间以归脾汤。喜其善调养，两月余诸证悉愈。
　　锦衣杨永兴筋骨软痛，气粗痰盛，作渴喜水。或用愈风汤、天麻丸，更加痰甚体麻。余以为脾肾俱虚，用补中益气汤、加减八味丸，三月余而痊。
　　州判蒋大用年五十，形体魁梧，中满吐痰，劳则头运，所服皆清痰理气。余曰：中满者，脾气亏损也；痰盛者，脾气不能运也；头运者，脾气不能升也；指麻者，脾气虚而不能周也。遂以补中益气加茯苓、半夏以补脾土，八味丸以补脾母而愈。[202p]

A woman coughed up phlegm accompanied by a greenish-yellow discharge. I treated her with a concoction of Si Qi Tang to send down white pills, supplementing with Xiao Chai Hu Tang and Bai Zhu, which brought her comfort.

Another woman, whose vital energy was naturally weak, experienced phlegm and qi disruptions, with symptoms like discomfort in the throat and chest fullness. Confused by various opinions, she thought it was due to phlegm and hastily used phlegm-dispelling medications, resulting in vomiting and diarrhea, altering her symptoms to a state of silence and unconsciousness. I believed this to be a further injury to her spleen and stomach, so for daily use, I prescribed Liu Jun Zi Tang with a strong decoction of rice, which she took in teaspoon amounts. After four days, she gradually advanced to porridge, and then took her previous medicine, alternating with Gui Pi Tang. I was pleased with her good care, and after more than two months, all her symptoms completely resolved.

Jin Yi Yang Yongxing suffered from soft, painful muscles and bones, with coarse qi and abundant phlegm, leading to thirst and a desire for water. Treatments such as Yu Feng Tang and Tian Ma Wan exacerbated the phlegm and caused numbness. Zhou Pan Jiang Dayong, fifty years old, was robust but felt fullness and phlegm, with headaches upon exertion. He had only taken medications to clear phlegm and regulate qi. I remarked that fullness indicated a deficiency of spleen qi; excessive phlegm meant the spleen could not move it; headaches indicated the spleen's qi could not rise; and numbness suggested deficiency in the spleen's ability to circulate. 　　一儒者脾肾素虚而有痰，或用导痰之法，痰甚作渴，头运烦热。余谓中气虚弱而变证，用补中益气汤而愈。后劳役发热头运，此气虚不能上升也，用前汤加蔓荆子而愈。后又劳神，畏见风寒，四肢逆冷，口沃痰涎，予以为脾虚寒之真病，以六君子加炮姜、肉桂而愈。
　　一男子素肾虚而咳痰，亦用导痰之法，虚证悉具，痰涎上涌，小便频数。余谓足三阴虚而复损也，朝用补养脾气汤培养脾肺之气，夕用六味丸加五味子收敛耗散之精而愈。
　　进士张禹功饮食停滞，胸满唾痰。或用药导之，痰涎上涌，眩运热渴，大便秘结，喜冷饮食，手足发热，余谓：肾水虚弱，津液难降，败液为痰，用六味丸而愈。
　　太宜人年七十五，遍身作痛，筋骨尤甚，不能伸屈，口干目赤，头眩痰涌，胸膈不利，小便赤濇而短少，夜间痰热殊甚，遍身作痒如虫行，此肝经气燥而风动也。用六味地黄丸料，加山栀、柴胡治之而愈。[203p]

A scholar had a deficiency in the spleen and kidneys, accompanied by phlegm. He attempted to resolve the phlegm, which led to great thirst and a feeling of heat and discomfort in the head. A man with a chronic kidney deficiency and phlegm cough also employed methods to resolve phlegm, which led to all the signs of deficiency. A 75-year-old man experienced widespread pain, particularly in the muscles and bones, with an inability to bend or stretch. 　　儒者王录之素痰甚，导吐之后，大便燥结，头运眼花等证，尺脉浮大，按之则濇，此肾气虚而兼血虚也，四物送六味丸四剂，诸证悉退，仍用前丸，月余而康。
　　佥宪高如斋素唾痰，服下痰药，痰去甚多，大便秘结，小便频数，头运眼花，尺脉浮大，按之如无。余谓：肾家不能纳气归源，前药复耗金水而甚，用加减八味丸料煎服而愈。
　　仪制贺朝卿吞酸胸满，痰盛作泻，饮食少思。用清气化痰等药，前证益甚，两膝渐肿，寒热往来。余谓：脾胃虚，湿热下注，用补中益气汤倍参、朮加茯苓、半夏、炮姜而愈。
　　余甥范允迪咳嗽痰盛，胸腹不利，饮食少思，肢体倦怠，脉浮大，按之微弱，服二陈枳壳等药愈盛。余曰：脾肺肾虚也，用补中益气、六味丸而愈。[204p]

The Confucian scholar Wang had a chronic cough with phlegm; after being induced to expel it, he experienced dry and hard stools, dizziness, and blurred vision. The official Qian Xian had a sour feeling in his chest and fullness, accompanied by excessive phlegm and diarrhea, with little appetite. My nephew Fan Yundike experienced a cough with abundant phlegm, discomfort in his chest and abdomen, poor appetite, fatigue, and a floating and large pulse that felt weak upon pressure. 　　侍御谭希曾喘咳吐痰，或手足时冷，此中气虚寒，用补中益气、炮姜而愈。
　　考功杨朴庵呕吐痰涎，胸腹膨胀，饮食少思，左关脉弦长，按之无力，右关脉弦长，按之微弱，此木克土，用六君子加柴胡、山栀、木香而愈。
　　一儒者体肥，仲夏患痰喘，用二陈、芩、连、桔梗，痰喘益甚；加桑皮、杏仁、(艹舌)蒌，盗汗气促；加贝母、枳谷，不时发热，饮食渐减，脉大而无力。予以为脾肺虚寒，用八味地黄丸以补土母，用补中益气汤以接中气而愈。
　　二守陈子忠饮食少思，吐痰口干，常服二陈、枳实、黄连之类，脾胃受伤，乃问于余。余述东垣先生云：脾胃之证，实则枳实、黄连泻之，虚则白朮、陈皮补之。彼遂以二味等分为丸，常服。由是多食而不伤，过时而不饥。
　　一儒者脾气虚弱，呕吐痰涎，因怒胸腹膨胀，饮食少思，左关脉弦长按之无力，右关脉弦长按之微弱，此木克土也。用六君子加柴胡、山栀、木香治之而愈。[205p]

The Royal Attendant Tan Xi once experienced coughing and sputum, and occasionally his hands and feet were cold. This was due to a deficiency of qi and cold; he was cured using the formula to tonify the middle and benefit qi, with the addition of roasted ginger.

Kao Gong Yang Pu'an had vomiting of sputum and saliva, a bloated chest and abdomen, little appetite, and a mind that was troubled. His left pulse was long and wiry with no strength upon pressing, while his right pulse was also long and wiry but weak. This indicated wood overcoming earth; he was treated with the Six Gentleman’s Decoction supplemented with Chai Hu, Shan Zhi, and Mu Xiang, resulting in recovery.

A certain Confucian scholar was corpulent and suffered from phlegm and wheezing in mid-summer, using Er Chen, Qin, Lian, and Jie Geng which aggravated his phlegm and wheezing. After adding Sang Pi, Xing Ren, and (Cao She) Lou, he experienced night sweats and shortness of breath. Adding Bei Mu and Zhi Gu, he suffered from intermittent fever, a gradual decrease in appetite, and a large but weak pulse. I diagnosed it as a deficiency of the spleen and lungs, hence I administered the Eight-Flavor Rehmannia Pill to tonify the earth mother, along with the Decoction to Tonify the Middle and Benefit Qi to restore the central qi, resulting in recovery.

Another official, Chen Zi Zhong, had little appetite and a dry mouth with sputum. He frequently took Er Chen, Zhi Shi, and Huang Lian, which damaged his spleen and stomach, so he consulted me. I referred to Master Dong Yuan's words: in cases of the spleen and stomach, if there is excess, then Zhi Shi and Huang Lian should be purged; if there is deficiency, then Bai Zhu and Chen Pi should be used to tonify. He subsequently mixed the two flavors equal in parts into pills for regular consumption. As a result, he could eat plenty without harm and was not hungry at mealtime.

A certain Confucian scholar had a weak spleen qi and suffered from vomiting and sputum due to anger, which caused a bloated chest and abdomen, little appetite, and a long and wiry left pulse that was weak upon pressing, with a long and wiry right pulse that was slightly weak. This indicated wood overcoming earth. He was treated with the Six Gentleman’s Decoction supplemented with Chai Hu, Shan Zhi, and Mu Xiang, leading to recovery.[205p]

　　冢宰刘紫岩因劳下体软痛，发热痰盛。用清燥汤入竹沥、姜汁服之，热痛减半；再剂而全愈。
　　一妇人咳嗽吐痰，胸膈作痛，右寸关浮滑，项下牵强，此脾胃积热成痰，非肺痈也。以二陈汤加山栀、白朮、桔梗治之而痊。
　　《古今医统》曰：一妇人年二十，身颇肥，性急，因气恼后，得痰咳呕逆，用二陈加顺气降火开郁利痰之剂，如水投石，渐次咳逆，怪声哈哈，日夜不绝。昔人所谓咳逆，连连五七十声方已，或三五十声而已者，此之谓咳逆也。兹日夜连声不息，无乃死证欤？脉浮而微洪，沉按小滑，复以滚痰丸下之，亦如故。予意痰郁滞胃脘胸膈之间，而气不得宣通，咳逆而后能出，非吐之不可。遂以瓜蒂散酸浆水调，鹅翎探吐，得痰碗许而咳逆遂止，寂然无声，而其效若神也。逾二日，因食面及肉汁，又复咳逆。与清痰顺气药，不效。予意前日吐痰不多，尚有未尽，再吐之，又得痰半碗许，即愈。[206p]

Minister Liu Ziyan suffered from pain and weakness in his lower body due to overwork, accompanied by fever and excessive phlegm. He was given a clear drying decoction mixed with bamboo juice and ginger juice, which reduced the heat and pain by half; another dose cured him completely.

A woman experienced coughing with phlegm and pain in her chest, with a floating and slippery pulse at the right wrist, and tightness in the neck. This was due to heat accumulation in the spleen and stomach producing phlegm, not a lung abscess. She was treated with the Erchen Decoction, adding gardenia, white attractor, and platycodon, and she recovered.

The "Ancient and Modern Medical Guidelines" states: A woman aged twenty, somewhat overweight and quick-tempered, after being angry, developed a cough with phlegm and nausea. She was given the Erchen Decoction with additional ingredients to soothe the qi, reduce fire, and resolve phlegm. It was as if throwing water against a stone; gradually she coughed violently, making strange noises day and night without pause. The ancients referred to “coughing reversely” as a series of fifty or seventy sounds in quick succession, or sometimes thirty or fifty. This case involved continuous sound without end, which seemed indicative of severe illness. Her pulse was floating and slightly surging, with a sinking, slightly slippery touch. I decided to give her a rolling phlegm pill, but it had no effect. I believed phlegm was stagnant between the stomach and chest, preventing the qi from flowing. Only through coughing could it be expelled, so I used a preparation of melon stem powder mixed with sour jujube water, using a goose feather to help induce vomiting, resulting in a bowlful of phlegm being expelled, and her cough ceased, silent and effective.

After two days, due to eating noodles and meat sauce, she again developed coughing and regurgitation. I gave her clear phlegm and qi-soothing medicine, but it did not work. I reasoned that the phlegm she had expelled the previous day was not fully eliminated, so she needed to vomit again. After another effort, she expelled about half a bowl of phlegm and was then cured.[206p]

　　一丈夫年四十余，身肥，素躭劳神，有痰火。一日，先恶寒后发热，头微痛，眩多，如不胜其重，躁热不退。自用参苏饮发汗，不愈，请予治。诊其脉沉洪而滑。予谓：痰火郁积无疑矣。以二陈加芩、连、天麻、神曲之粪，复以滚痰丸下之三，逾日反躁热不退，咳唾痰涎不止。此正丹溪云：痰在膈上，非吐不可，泻之亦不去。复用瓜蒂散采吐之，得痰半碗许，彼畏苦而止。予意痰少不能效，躁热如旧，但以人参白虎汤、五苓散合服，亦不愈。予谓：郁滞重，吐难得出，分利亦不去，宜以散郁之剂。仍用二陈加前胡、柴胡、葛根、桔梗、苍朮、川芎、姜汁炒芩栀，三剂遂愈。[207p]

A man over forty years old, stout in build, often burdened by fatigue and phlegm heat. One day, he first felt cold, then developed a fever, experiencing slight head pain, frequent dizziness, as if he could not bear the weight, and restless heat that did not subside. He tried to sweat it out with a ginseng and perilla drink, but it did not help and sought treatment. Upon examining his pulse, it was deep, surging, and slippery. I concluded there was definitely phlegm-heat stagnation. I prescribed a modified Er Chen decoction with Scutellaria, Phragmites, Gastrodia, and the excrement of ferment, along with pill to expel phlegm. However, the next day, he still had restless heat and persistent coughing with phlegm. This is precisely what Danxi said: when phlegm is in the diaphragm, it must be vomited; it cannot be expelled by purging. I used Gua Ti San to induce vomiting and gathered about half a bowl of phlegm, but he stopped out of fear of bitterness. I felt that the small amount of phlegm was insufficient to be effective; the restless heat remained the same. However, with a combination of Ginseng Bai Hu Decoction and Wuling San, he still did not improve. I said: the stagnation is heavy, making it hard to vomit it out, and purging does not relieve it, so a remedy to disperse the stagnation is needed. I then used a modified Er Chen with Qian Hu, Chai Hu, Ge Gen, Jie Geng, Cang Zhu, Chuan Xiong, and ginger juice-fried Scutellaria and Gardenia. After three doses, he was cured.[207p]

　　《寓意草》曰：钱叔翁太老先生，形体清瘦，平素多火少痰，迩年内蕴之热，蒸湿为痰。辛巳秋夏间，湿热交胜，时忽患右足麻木，冷如冰石。盖热极似寒，如暑月反雨冰雹之类。医者以其足跗之冷也，不细察其为热极似寒，误以牛膝、木瓜、防己、加皮、羌、独之属温之；甚且认为下元虚惫，误用桂、附、河车之属补之。以火济火，以热益热，繇是肿溃出脓水，浸淫数月，踝骨已下，足背指肿，废而不用，总为误治而至此极耳。其理甚明，无难于辨。若果寒痰下坠，不过坚凝不散止耳，甚者不过痿痹不仁止耳，何至肿而且溃，黄水淋漓，腐肉穿筋耶？太翁不知为医药所误，乃委咎于方隅神杀所致，岂其然哉。此与伤寒坏证，热邪深入经络而生流注，无少异也。所用参膏，但专理元气，而无清解湿热之药以佐之，是以未显决效。[208p]

The "Yuyi Cao" states: Mr. Qian Shuweng, an elderly gentleman, has a thin physique and usually has a lot of heat and little phlegm. In recent years, the heat within him has combined with humidity to produce phlegm. In the autumn of the Xin Si year, with a mixture of dampness and heat, he suddenly suffered from numbness in his right foot, feeling as cold as ice or stone. This was due to extreme heat manifesting as cold, similar to the summer months when rain and hail occur. The doctors, observing the coldness of his foot, did not discern that it was extreme heat resembling cold, mistakenly prescribed warming herbs such as cowherb, papaya, and others; they furthermore believed that his lower energy was depleted, wrongly using warming tonics like cinnamon and aconite.

By adding fire to fire and heat to heat, his condition worsened, leading to swelling and discharge of pus. Over several months, it spread down to the ankle bones, causing swelling in the back of the foot and toes, rendering them unusable. This was entirely due to mismanagement of treatment. The reasoning is quite clear and not difficult to differentiate. If it were just cold phlegm sinking down, it would merely cause hardening and not dispersing; at worst, it would lead to weakness and numbness. How could it result in swelling and pus, with yellow water oozing and decaying flesh penetrating tendons? Mr. Taiweng, unaware of the medical errors, blamed it on the deities in the corners, but could it truly be so? This is not much different from the complications of typhoid where heat invades the meridians and causes flux.

The ginseng paste used only focused on replenishing the vital energy, without any medications to clear and resolve the damp heat, which is why there was no evident resolution of the symptoms.[208p]

以元老之官，不可以理烦剧，设与竹沥同事，人参固其经，竹沥通其络，则甘寒气味，相得益彰矣。徐太掖先生服人参以治虚风，误佐以附子之热，迄今筋脉短缩，不便行持，亦繇不识甘寒可通经络也。且太翁用参膏后，脾气亦既大旺，健运有加矣。此时傥能撙节饮食，俾脾中所生之阳气，得端力以驱痰驱热，则痰热运行，而足患并可结局。[209p]

As a senior official, one should not be involved in trivial matters. If ginseng works in harmony with bamboo leaf, ginseng strengthens the meridians, and bamboo leaf opens the collaterals, then their sweet and cold properties would complement each other wonderfully. Master Xu Taiye took ginseng to treat his deficiency wind, but mistakenly combined it with the heat of aconite. To this day, his sinews are shortened and he cannot move freely, which is due to his lack of understanding of how sweet and cold can open the meridians. Moreover, after the old gentleman used ginseng paste, his spleen qi became robust and his digestive function improved. At this time, if he could moderate his diet, allowing the yang qi generated within the spleen to actively dispel phlegm and heat, then the phlegm heat would circulate, and the affliction in his legs could be resolved.[209p]

乃日食而外，加以夜食，虽脾气之旺不为食所伤，然以参力所生之脾气，不用之运痰运热，止用之以运食，诚可惜也。今者食入亦不易运，以助长而反得衰，乃至痰饮胶结于胸中，为饱为闷，为频咳而痰不行。总为脾失其健，不为胃行津液，而饮食反以生痰，渐渍充满肺窍，咳不易出。虽以治痰为急，然治痰之药，大率耗气动虚，恐痰未出而风先入也。唯是确以甘寒之药，杜风消热，润躁补虚，豁痰，乃为合法。至于辛热之药，断断不可再误矣。医者明明见此，辄用桂附无算，想必因脓水易干，认为辛热之功，而极力以催之结局耳，可胜诛哉！[210p]

On the day of an eclipse, along with night eating, although the spleen's energy is robust and not harmed by food, it is indeed regrettable that the spleen's energy, generated by ginseng, is solely used to process food and not to move phlegm or heat. Nowadays, food intake is also difficult to process, which, instead of promoting health, leads to decline, causing phlegm and fluids to accumulate in the chest, resulting in fullness and discomfort, as well as frequent coughing with phlegm not being expelled. This is fundamentally due to the spleen losing its strength, and not because the stomach is able to move fluids; rather, food intake generates phlegm, gradually saturating the lung pathways, making coughing difficult.

Although treating phlegm is urgent, the medicines for phlegm generally exhaust energy and induce deficiency, thus risking that phlegm may not be expelled before pathogenic wind enters. The only proper way is to use sweet and cold medicines to quell wind, dispel heat, moisten dryness, and replenish deficiency, thereby opening phlegm. As for spicy and warming medicines, they must not be mistakenly used again. Physicians clearly see this, yet they continue to use large amounts of cinnamon and other warming agents, presumably thinking them effective because purulent fluid easily dries up, and thus they push vigorously for a resolution. Is this not deserving of condemnation?[210p]

　　卣翁老先生脉盛体坚，神采百倍，从无病邪敢犯。但每早浴面，必呕痰水几口，胸前惯自摩揉，乳下宗气，其动应衣，若夜睡宁，水道清，则胸中爽然。其候似病非病，遍考方书，广询明医，不得其解。昌谓是痰饮结于胸膈，小有窠囊，缘其气之壮盛，随聚随呕，是以痰饮不致为害，而膻中之气，则因呕而伤矣。夫膻中者，与上焦同位胸膈。经云上焦如雾，言其气之氤氲如雾也。又曰膻中者臣使之官，言其能分布胸中之气而下传也。今以呕之故而数动其气，则氤氲变为急迫上奔，然稍定则仍下布，亦不为害也。大率痰为标，气为本，治标易而治本则难。非治本之难，以往哲从未言其治法，而后人不知所治耳。昌试论之：治气之源有三：一曰肺气。肺气清则周身之气，肃然下行，先生之肺气则素清也。一曰胃气。胃气和则胸中之气亦易下行，先生之胃气则素和也。一曰膀胱之气。[211p]

The old man You is robust and shows vitality, never suffering from illness or invasion of pathogens. However, every morning, he must expel a few mouthfuls of phlegm after bathing his face, habitually rubbing his chest and stimulating the energy beneath his ribs. If he sleeps soundly at night and has clear pathways for water, he feels refreshed in his chest. His symptoms resemble illness but are not truly so. After extensive examination of medical texts and inquiring with knowledgeable doctors, no clear answer could be found. Chang posited that this is phlegm and fluid accumulating in the chest cavity, with a minor stagnation formed due to his vigorous energy, leading to simultaneous gathering and expulsion. Thus, the phlegm and fluid do not cause harm; however, the energy in the chest can be injured by the act of expulsion. The chest region, or “Dan Zhong,” is at the same level as the upper burner. The classics state that the upper burner is like mist, indicating that its energy is diffused like fog. It also states that Dan Zhong is the official in charge of distributing energy within the chest and transmitting it downward. Now, due to frequent expulsions, the diffused energy turns into urgency and ascends, but when settled, it resumes its downward distribution, thus not causing harm. Generally, phlegm is the symptom while energy is the root; treating the symptom is easy, but treating the root is difficult. The difficulty in treating the root lies in the fact that previous sages have never discussed methods for it, leaving later generations unaware of how to treat it. Chang attempted to theorize on this: there are three sources of energy to address: First is lung energy. When lung energy is clear, the body's energy flows smoothly downward, and the old man’s lung energy is typically clear. Second is stomach energy. When stomach energy is harmonious, the energy within the chest also flows more easily downward, and the old man’s stomach energy is usually harmonious. Third is bladder energy.[211p]

膀胱之气旺，则能吸引胸中之气下行，先生青年善养，膀胱之气则素旺也。其膻中之气乱而即治，扰而即恬者，赖此三气暗为输运，是以不觉其累，即谓之无病也可。若三气反干胸膈之人，其为紧为胀，可胜道哉！故未形之病可以不言，而屡动之气不可不亟反于氤氲。先生但觉为痰饮所苦，昼日尝鼓呼吸之气，触出胸膈之痰，而未知痰不可出，徒伤气也。盖夜卧则痰聚于胃，晨起自能呕出，日间胃之津液四达脏腑，即激之亦不出耳。[212p]

When the energy of the bladder is strong, it can attract the energy within the chest to descend. Therefore, young students should cultivate this energy, which is inherently vigorous. If the energy in the heart region is chaotic, it can be treated immediately; if it is disturbed, it can be calmed right away. This depends on the subtle transport of these three energies, so one does not perceive their burdens, and this is called being free from illness. However, when these three energies oppose the chest diaphragm, the resulting tightness and distension can hardly be tolerated! Thus, undiagnosed illnesses may remain unspoken, but the occurring energies must urgently return to their balance. The patient may feel tormented by phlegm and fluids, attempting to expel the energy through breathing, thereby dislodging phlegm from the chest diaphragm, yet unaware that this phlegm cannot be expelled and only damages the energy. Indeed, at night, phlegm accumulates in the stomach, and upon waking, it can be naturally vomited out; during the day, the stomach's fluids circulate through the organs, and even if stimulated, they will not be expelled.[212p]

然则痰消则气自顺，是必以治痰为急。而体盛痰不易除，又必以健脾为先，脾健则新痰不生。其宿痰之在窠囊者，渐渍于胃，而上下分消，于是无痰则不呕，不呕则气不乱，气不乱则日返于氤氲矣。虽然，尚有一吃紧关头，当并讲也。人身胸中空旷如太虚，地气上则为云，必天气降而为雨，地气始收藏不动。诚会上焦如雾、中焦如沤、下焦如渎之意，则知云行雨施，而后沟渎皆盈，水道通决，乾坤有一番新景象矣。此义首重膀胱一经。[213p]

Thus, when phlegm is resolved, the qi will naturally be smooth; therefore, treating phlegm should be a priority. However, when the body is full of phlegm, it is not easily eliminated, and one must first strengthen the spleen; when the spleen is strong, new phlegm does not form. As for the old phlegm that is lodged in the body's cavities, it gradually penetrates the stomach and is dispersed both above and below; thus, without phlegm there is no vomiting, without vomiting the qi remains undisturbed, and when the qi is undisturbed, it will gradually return to its harmonious state. Nevertheless, there is still a critical point that must be addressed. The human chest is vast and empty like the great void; when the earth's qi rises, it becomes clouds. The heavenly qi must descend to become rain, and the earth's qi then begins to collect and remain still. Indeed, if the upper Jiao is like mist, the middle Jiao like fermentation, and the lower Jiao like a channel, one will understand how clouds move and rain falls, and as a result, all waterways will be filled, and the paths will be cleared, bringing a new scene to the universe. This principle places vital importance on the bladder meridian.[213p]

经云：膀胱者州都之官，津液藏焉，气化则能出矣。如人之饮酒无算而不醉者，皆从膀胱之气化而出也。膻中位于膈内，膀胱位于腹内，膀胱之气化，则空洞善容，而膻中之气得以下运；若膀胱不化，则腹已先胀，膻中之气，安能下达耶？然欲膀胱之气化，其权尤在于葆肾，肾以膀胱为腑者也。肾气动，必先注于膀胱。屡动不已，膀胱满胀，势必逆奔于胸膈，其窒塞之状，不可名言。肾气不动，则收藏愈固，膀胱得以清净无为，而膻中之气注之不盈矣。膻中之气，下走既捷，则不为牵引所乱，而胸中旷若太空。昌更曰：顺气则痰不留，即不治痰而痰自运矣。卣臣先生问曰：痰在膈中，去喉不远，每早必痛呕始出者，何耶？曰：道不同也。胸膈之间，重重脂膜遮蔽，浑无空隙，痰从何出？所出者，胃中之痰耳。曰：然则膈中之痰不出耶？曰：安得不出，但出之艰耳。[214p]

The classics say: The bladder is the official of the capital region; it stores the fluids, and when Qi is transformed, it can be expelled. Just as a person can drink without limit and not become drunk, this is all due to the Qi transformation of the bladder. The Zang Zhong (the area of the heart) is located within the diaphragm, while the bladder is situated in the abdomen. When the Qi of the bladder transforms, it creates a hollow space that is good for storage, allowing the Qi of the Zang Zhong to descend; if the bladder does not transform, the abdomen will already be distended, making it impossible for the Qi of the Zang Zhong to descend.

However, in order for the bladder's Qi to transform, its authority lies in preserving the kidneys, as the kidneys regard the bladder as a cavity. When kidney Qi moves, it must first flow into the bladder. If the movement is excessive and persistent, the bladder becomes full and distended, inevitably causing a reverse flow into the chest and diaphragm, resulting in a blockage that cannot be easily described. If the kidney Qi is not active, then its storage becomes firmer, allowing the bladder to remain clear and unaffected, thus the Qi of the Zang Zhong cannot be overfilled.

When the Qi of the Zang Zhong flows downward swiftly, it is not disturbed by the pulls of excess, and the chest feels open as if in the vastness of space. Chang Geng further states: When Qi is flowing smoothly, phlegm does not linger; thus, without treating the phlegm, it eliminates itself. The servant asked: Phlegm in the diaphragm is not far from the throat, and it must cause pain and vomiting each morning; why is this? The answer: It is a difference in pathways. Between the chest and diaphragm lies a thick layer of fatty membranes, completely blocking any gaps; from where can the phlegm escape? What comes out is just the phlegm from the stomach. The servant asked: Then does the phlegm in the diaphragm not come out? The answer: How could it not come out? It is just that expulsion is challenging.[214p]

盖膻中之气，四布于十二经，布于手足六阳经，则其气从喉物而上出；布于手足六阴经，则其气从前后二阴而下出。然从下出者无碍，从上出者亦必先下注阳明，始得上越，是以难也。曰：若是则所论膀胱气化一段，渊乎微矣。但吸引之机权，从不见于经典，岂有所自乎？曰：《内经》有巨阳引精之义，缘无注解，人不能会。巨阳者，太阳膀胱也。谓膀胱能吸引胸中之气下行，而胸中之胀自消，此足证也。[215p]

The Qi of the diaphragm spreads throughout the twelve meridians. When it spreads to the six Yang meridians of the hands and feet, the Qi rises and exits from the throat; when it spreads to the six Yin meridians of the hands and feet, the Qi descends and exits from the front and back Yin. However, the Qi that exits from below is unobstructed, while the Qi that exits from above must first descend to the Yangming before it can rise, which makes it more difficult. It is said that this discussion of the transformation of the bladder Qi is profoundly subtle. Yet, the mechanism of suction is not seen in the classics; could it possibly have a source? It is stated that the "Inner Canon" contains the principle of the Greater Yang drawing the essence, but due to the lack of annotations, people cannot comprehend it. The Greater Yang refers to the bladder of the Sun. This means that the bladder can draw down the Qi from the chest, resulting in the dissipation of the distension in the chest, which serves as sufficient proof.[215p]

曰：胸中窠囊之说，确然无疑，但不知始于何因，结于何处，消于何时也？曰：人身之气，经盛则注于络，络盛则注于经。窠囊之来，始于痰聚胃口，呕时数动胃气，胃气动则半从上出于喉，半从内入于络。胃之络，贯膈者也。其气奔入之急，则冲透膈膜，而痰得以居之。痰入既久，则阻碍气道，而气之奔入者，复结一囊，如蜂子之营穴，日增一日，故治之甚难。必先去胃中之痰而不呕不触，俾胃经之气，不急奔于络，转虚其胃以听络中之气返还于胃，逐渐以药开导其囊而涤去其痰，则自愈矣。此昌独得之见，屡试之法也。[216p]

It is said: The theory of the "cavity in the chest" is indeed certain and without doubt, but one does not know what caused it, where it ends, or when it dissipates. It is said: The Qi of the human body, when abundant, flows into the meridians; when the meridians are abundant, Qi flows into the collaterals. The origin of the cavity begins with phlegm accumulating at the stomach, and during vomiting, the stomach Qi moves several times, with half emerging from the throat and half entering the collaterals. The collaterals of the stomach pass through the diaphragm. When the Qi rushes in urgently, it penetrates the diaphragm, allowing the phlegm to settle there. Once the phlegm has been there for a long time, it obstructs the airway, and the rushing Qi forms another cavity, like a bee's nest, growing day by day, hence making treatment very difficult. One must first eliminate the phlegm in the stomach without causing vomiting or irritation, so that the Qi of the stomach does not rush into the collaterals, allowing the stomach to become more receptive to the Qi returning from the collaterals. Gradually, using medicine to guide the cavity and clear away the phlegm, healing will occur spontaneously. This understanding is unique to me and has been tested multiple times.[216p]

　　黄我兼世兄尊夫人惊痰堵塞窍隧，肝肺心包络间无处不有，三部脉虚软无力，邪盛正衰，不易开散。有欲用涌剂稍吐十分之三，诚为快事。但细筹之，此法殆不可行。盖涌法政如兵家劫营之法，安危反掌，原属险道。况痰迷不过片晌耳，设以涌药投之，痰才一动人即运去，探之指不得入，咽之气不能下，药势与病势相扼，转致连日不苏，将若之何？无已，如丹溪所云：惧吐者，宜消息下之乎？不知窍隧之痰，即导之下行，万不能导，徒伤脾气，痰愈窒塞，此法亦不可用也。为今之计，确以理脾为先。脾气者，人身健运之阳气，如天之有日也。阴凝四塞者，日失其所；痰迷不省者，脾失其权耳。理脾则如烈日当空，片云纤翳能掩之乎？其次莫如清肺。[217p]

Huang, my esteemed brother, the lady is suffering from phlegm obstructing the passages. There is stagnation between the liver, lungs, and pericardium; there is weakness in all three pulse sections, with excess evil and deficient righteousness, making it difficult to disperse. If one wishes to use an expelling method to slightly induce a吐 (vomit) of about thirty percent, it would indeed be a relief. However, upon careful consideration, this method is hardly feasible. The expelling technique is like a military tactic, where security and danger are easily reversed; it is inherently perilous. Moreover, phlegm is merely a fleeting disturbance; if we apply expelling medicine, the phlegm may stir and be expelled just as someone is about to address it. However, the point of entry is blocked, and the qi cannot descend. The medicinal effect conflicts with the pathological condition, possibly leading to days of unconsciousness. What can be done? Ultimately, as Danxi stated: if expulsion is feared, should it not be better to nourish and guide it downward? The phlegm in the passages cannot be led downward; it merely consumes the spleen qi, causing further obstruction. This method is not advisable either. For the current plan, it is necessary to focus on nourishing the spleen first. The spleen qi is the yang energy that supports health and movement in the body, much like the sun in the sky. When the yin condenses and blocks, it is as if the sun has lost its position; when phlegm obscures perception, it signifies that the spleen has lost its authority. Nourishing the spleen is akin to the blazing sun at its zenith; can a wisp of cloud obscure it? Next, nothing is better than clearing the lungs.[217p]

肺为将帅之官，气清则严肃下行，气下行则痰之藉为坚城固垒者，方示以瑕，而可用其攻击之力，所谓攻坚则瑕者亦坚，攻瑕则坚者亦瑕是也。今四末肿麻，气壅已甚，尤不可不亟亟矣。其理脾之法，须药饵与饮食相参，白饭香蔬苦茗便为佳珍。不但滑腻当禁，即粥亦不宜食，以粥饮之结为痰饮易易耳。不但杂食当禁，即饭食亦宜少减，以脾气不用以消谷，转用之消痰，较药力万万耳。其辛辣酒脯，及煎煿日曝之物，俱能伤肺，并不宜食。至于用药，自有节次矩矱，俟日渐轻安，来春方奏全绩也。缘此病人不识治，前贤亦未见高出手眼。但思之累日，窃以为要领在是。所以必欲持久者，与金城方略同意，且先除胁从，后歼巨魁，是势所不易捷得之事。盖以惊痰之来，始于肝胆，冬月木气归根，不敢攻治，故但以理脾药平调，必至春月木旺，才用四君子汤加龙胆草、芦荟、代赭石、黄连、青黛等药，为丸服之，痰迷之证，果获全瘳，此后不发。
[218p]

The lungs are the organ of the general and commander. When the qi is clear, it will be solemn and descend; when the qi descends, phlegm will serve as a stronghold, illustrating flaws that can be targeted for attack. The saying goes, “To attack the strong, even flaws are strong; to attack flaws, the strong also have flaws.” Now, with the limbs swollen and numb, the qi is extremely stagnant, and it cannot be neglected.

To address this condition, the method concerning the spleen must combine medicine with diet. White rice, fragrant vegetables, and bitter tea are preferable. It is essential to avoid smooth and greasy foods; even porridge should not be consumed, as it tends to form phlegm easily. Not only should mixed foods be avoided, but rice should also be reduced to prevent spleen qi from being used to digest grains; instead, it should be used to eliminate phlegm, which is much more effective than medication.

Spicy, alcoholic, and sun-dried foods all harm the lungs and should be avoided. As for medication, there is a particular order to follow, waiting for gradual improvement and full recovery in the coming spring. Due to this illness, patients do not understand treatment, and the sages of old also did not have superior methods. However, after much thought, I believe the key lies here.

Therefore, those who want to sustain this must agree with the strategies of a fortified city, first eliminating the smaller issues and then eliminating the major ones, as this is not something easily achieved. It is said that the onset of phlegm originates from the liver and gallbladder; in winter, the wood qi returns to its root, preventing aggressive treatment. Thus, we only use spleen-regulating medicines. Only when spring arrives, with the wood qi flourishing, should we employ the Four Gentlemen Decoction, adding gentian, aloe, realgar, coptis, and indigo among other herbs in pill form. This will resolve the symptoms of phlegm obstruction, leading to complete recovery and preventing future occurrences.[218p]
